PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 26 of 200
Question ID: 613337
As a project manager, you are in the process of obtaining team members. You lobbied for a
particular developer that has worked on similar projects; however, that developer is now
committed to a different project.
What should you do?
- **A Update the project charter to list the developer as pre-assigned to your project**
- **B Set up the project team as a virtual team to allow the developer to work on your project**
part-time
- **C Add a recommendation in the lessons learned register to use pre-assignment as needed for**
future projects
- **D Include the developer's role and responsibilities in the project team assignments for your**
project
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which project document may be updated as part of the Acquire Resources process?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that you, as the project manager, are performing the Acquire Resources
process by obtaining the project team members. The lessons learned register is one of the project
documents that may be updated as a result of this process. The lessons learned register should be
updated with information on challenges encountered and how they could have been avoided as
well as approaches that worked well for acquiring resources. The incorrect answer choices
represent actions that are not relevant since the developer is already committed to a different
project. At this point, the best course of action is to record the information in the lessons learned

---

register so the knowledge gained can improve future performance. Therefore, of the available
choices, adding a recommendation in the lessons learned register to use pre-assignment for future
projects is your best course of action.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Update the project charter to list the developer as pre-assigned to your project**
Incorrect. Using pre-assignment during the Develop Project Charter process may have
prevented the problem described by the question. However, with the developer already
committed to a different project, it is too late to pre-assign the developer to your project.
- **B Set up the project team as a virtual team to allow the developer to work on your project**
part-time
Incorrect. A virtual team setup can create new possibilities when acquiring project team
members, such as enabling the geographically diverse individuals to serve on the same
project team. However, in this scenario, the developer is already committed to a different
project. Therefore, setting up the team in a virtual configuration would not 'reserve' the
developer for your project. Additionally, there is not enough information in the question to
determine if the needs of another project would allow the developer to work on your project
part-time.
- **C Add a recommendation in the lessons learned register to use pre-assignment as needed for**
future projects
Correct. The lessons learned register can be updated with information on challenges
encountered and how they could have been avoided. With the developer already committed
to another project, the best course of action is to record the information in the lessons
learned register so the knowledge gained can improve future performance.
- **D Include the developer's role and responsibilities in the project team assignments for your**
project
Incorrect. Project team assignments is a project document that provides information on the
team members and their roles and responsibilities for the project. This document is an
output of the Acquire Resources process described in the scenario and should include only
those team members who have been acquired as part of this process. The developer has not
been acquired.

Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 335

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 27 of 200
Question ID: 613249
During video conferences, a project manager notices that a project team member frequently
stands up and paces around the room while speaking. This behavior causes the team member to
disappear from view and creates a distraction for the other meeting participants.
What should the project manager do?
- **A Discreetly mention the behavior to the meeting participants and tell them to accept the**
behavior
- **B Nothing, since all people are different**
- **C Discuss the issue in private with the team member**
- **D Make a rule that all people should stay seated during meetings**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

There is an opportunity to improve the team member's communication skills.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The project team member's pacing is an example of non-verbal communication. Non-verbal
communication can enhance communication; however, in this case, it is causing a distraction for
the video conference participants. Additionally, when the project team member cannot be seen in
the video conference, any positive non-verbal communication is lost. While this behavior would
not be an issue for an audio conference call, it is a problem for the video conference. It is
possible that the project team member's behavior is subconscious, and he is unaware of the
negative impact on communication. It could also be a situation where there is some other
underlying reason for the behavior like a fear of public speaking, which should be understood in
order to determine how best to address the issue. Regardless of the reason, the project manager

---

should take the opportunity to further develop the team member's non-verbal communication and
overall communication skills. Therefore, of the available options, discussing the issue in private
with the team member is the best course of action.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Discreetly mention the behavior to the meeting participants and tell them to accept the**
behavior
Incorrect. It is not appropriate to discuss the team member's performance issue with the
larger group. Additionally, telling meeting participants to accept the behavior does not
prevent it from being a distraction.
- **B Nothing, since all people are different**
Incorrect. Although it is true that all people are different, doing nothing is not the best
option. Although the behavior is not offensive or even a serious issue, it is detrimental to
the video conferences as it is distracting to the meeting participants. It is best to address the
issue, and, at the very least, gain an understanding of the team member's behavior.
- **C Discuss the issue in private with the team member**
Correct. Since the behavior is distracting to other meeting participants, it represents an
opportunity to improve communication skills. The project manager should address the issue
in private to develop the project team member into a better communicator.
- **D Make a rule that all people should stay seated during meetings**
Incorrect. This action might be effective in addressing the issue, but it is not the best
approach. The question indicates that the issue only applies to one team member, so
establishing a rule for everyone is not necessary. Additionally, there may be some unknown
reason for the team member's behavior that should be understood so that it can be
addressed in the most effective manner.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 384
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 6
Question 28 of 200
Question ID: 613083
During project closure, there is a dispute with the customer regarding whether or not a
deliverable was formally accepted.
Which of the following project documents is the least likely to help resolve this issue?
- **A Lessons learned register**
- **B Project communications**
- **C Requirements documentation**
- **D Change log**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

This option may contribute to closing the project but is least likely to help resolve the issue.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The lessons learned register is used to record knowledge gained during a project so that it can be
used in the current project and entered into the lessons learned repository. Although the lessons
learned register is an input to closing a project, it is unlikely to be helpful in resolving this issue.
The issues may be identified by looking at project communications, requirements
documentation, and the change log along with other project documents and artifacts. Keep in
mind that the question is asking for the project document that is the 'least' likely to help resolve
this issue. Therefore, of options presented, the lessons learned register is the best response.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Lessons learned register**
Correct. The lessons learned register is a project document used to record knowledge
gained during a project. Although the lessons learned register is an input to the Close
Project or Phase process, it is unlikely to identify whether or not a deliverable was formally
accepted.
- **B Project communications**
Incorrect. Project communications include communications that have been created
throughout the project. Project communications may answer questions about the
understanding of what the customer requested or what they were alerted to during the
project.
- **C Requirements documentation**
Incorrect. The requirements documentation describes how individual requirements meet the
business need for the project. The requirements documentation can be used in project
closure to demonstrate compliance with the project scope.
- **D Change log**
Incorrect. The change log contains the status of all change requests throughout the project.
The change log might highlight which changes to the deliverable were approved, rejected,
or deferred. This document may provide insight into why there might be a disagreement
about the approved project scope.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 124

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 29 of 200
Question ID: 612905
- **A project manager has just taken over during the first phase of a project, which is running ahead**
of schedule. Each phase of the project will require different competencies, and the project
manager needs to understand what training should be provided to the team in preparation for the
upcoming phases and when this training will be needed.
What is the best course of action?
- **A Consult the project schedule**
- **B Talk to the human resources department**
- **C Review the resource calendars**
- **D Examine the training management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which project document presents linked activities with planned dates, durations, milestones, and
resources?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the project manager is performing the Develop Team process and
needs to gain an understanding of how and when to provide training to the team which will be
required for the upcoming phases. The project schedule serves as an input to the Develop Team
process and presents linked activities with planned dates, durations, milestones, and resources.
Note, the project schedule alone does not define 'what' training is needed for a particular team
member and 'how' this training should be conducted. However, by analyzing the project schedule
and identifying what activities are scheduled, when they are scheduled, and who is assigned to
these activities, the project manager can determine in advance what training is required for each

---

project team member, and how this training should be conducted to develop the competencies
required at different phases. In other words, the project schedule helps identify the need for team
development strategies during project execution. Therefore, of the available choices, checking
the project schedule is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Consult the project schedule**
Correct. The project schedule is an output of a schedule model that presents linked
activities with planned dates, durations, milestones, and resources. The project schedule
defines how and when to provide training to the project team and develop the competencies
required at different phases.
- **B Talk to the human resources department**
Incorrect. While the human resources department may have a general idea about training,
it is unlikely that they would have information on specific training required for the team
members of every project undertaken by the performing organization.
- **C Review the resource calendars**
Incorrect. A resource calendar is a calendar that identifies the working days and shifts
upon which each specific resource is available. While the resource calendars may help
determine team and resource availability for scheduling team development activities, the
resource calendar does not provide guidance on how and when to provide training, nor
does it help to understand 'what' training is needed since the information about the
assigned tasks is not included in the resource calendar.
- **D Examine the training management plan**
Incorrect. 'Training management plan' is a made-up term.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 339, 217

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 30 of 200
Question ID: 613098
You have just taken over an infrastructure development project, and you have developed the
earned value analysis chart below.
If the current forecast holds true, what action might you need to take before the end of the
project?
- **A The submission of a change request to access the contingency reserves**
- **B A recommendation that the project be terminated if project costs can't be brought into**
alignment with the BAC

---

- **C The submission of a change request to update the cost baseline**
- **D No action will be required as the project is trending to meet the project budget**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Management reserves are not included in the cost baseline.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The estimate at completion (EAC) is the expected total cost of completing all work expressed as
the sum of the actual cost to date and the estimate to complete. In this case, the current EAC
exceeds the budget at completion (BAC) and, if the trend continues, will require the use of the
management reserves to complete the project. The management reserves are part of the overall
project budget but are not included in the cost baseline. Therefore, an approved change request
will be required to transfer the management reserves into the cost baseline which will have to be
updated to reflect the added funds. Hence, of the available choices, the submission of a change
request to update the cost baseline is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The submission of a change request to access the contingency reserves**
Incorrect. Contingency reserves are part of the cost baseline, and a project manager has
direct control over these funds. Therefore, there is no reason to submit a change request to
access the contingency reserve.
- **B A recommendation that the project be terminated if project costs can't be brought into**
alignment with the BAC
Incorrect. There is no reason to terminate a project if it exceeds the budget at completion
(BAC). In this case, although the project is trending to exceed the BAC, the forecast is still
within the overall project budget. Therefore, there is no reason to recommend the
termination of the project based on the information provided in this scenario.
- **C The submission of a change request to update the cost baseline**

---

Correct. The chart indicates that if the current forecast holds, the management reserves will
be required to complete the project. The management reserves are part of the overall
project budget but are not included in the cost baseline. Therefore, an approved change
request will be required to transfer the management reserves into the cost baseline.
- **D No action will be required as the project is trending to meet the project budget**
Incorrect. The chart indicates that at the current forecast, the costs are trending in a way
that will require management reserves to complete the project. Therefore, saying that no
action will be required is unlikely to be the correct answer.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 254-255, 264

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 31 of 200
Question ID: 613402
During a project closure meeting, a stakeholder makes a suggestion that would improve the
functionality of a vendor's deliverable. The suggestion does not get the attention of the
participants and is quickly dropped without further action.
What is the most likely reason for the suggestion being dropped?
- **A Suggestions are not allowed during project closure.**
- **B The project team has already been released.**
- **C Stakeholder influence during project closure is low.**
- **D The deliverable still needs to be accepted.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The ability of stakeholders to influence the outcome of the project is greatest at the start of the
project.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the Close Project or Phase process is being performed. With project
closure underway, the deliverable produced by the vendor would have already been formally
accepted. During project closure, stakeholders have little, if any, influence over project
deliverables. Stakeholders' ability to control the outcome of the project is lowest towards the end
of the project because most of the work has already been completed. Therefore, of the available
options, low stakeholder influence is the best response.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Suggestions are not allowed during project closure.**
Incorrect. Suggestions are allowed at any point in the project life cycle. The point is not
about whether or not the suggestions are allowed, but about the low probability of the
suggestion to be implemented during project closure where the deliverables have likely
already been accepted.
- **B The project team has already been released.**
Incorrect. Releasing the project team is one of the actions associated with project closure
described by the scenario. However, this action is typically taken as one of the last steps of
project closure since the team members may be needed to perform some of the closing
tasks. Additionally, there is not enough information in the question to determine if the
project team has already been released.
- **C Stakeholder influence during project closure is low.**
Correct. Stakeholder influence declines as the project nears completion. During project
closure, stakeholders have little, if any, influence over project deliverables.
- **D The deliverable still needs to be accepted.**
Incorrect. Deliverables are formally accepted during the Validate Scope process, which
should have already been completed at the time of project closure. During the Close
Project or Phase process, the project team may 'confirm' formal acceptance of the
deliverable.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 127

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 32 of 200
Question ID: 612002
- **A project manager has recently been given a promotion and became the sponsor of a new**
initiative within her company. Given her past success in managing similar projects, the
organization’s project steering committee asks her to submit a project estimate that will be
reviewed next week.
What is the best course of action for the new sponsor?
- **A Use her own expert judgment and some historical information**
- **B Get a professional estimate from external subject matter experts**
- **C Use the WBS to create an accurate bottom-up estimate**
- **D Work with the project team to create the requested estimate**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Project managers that get promoted tend to be skilled in knowing what to estimate and how to
make good decisions.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

It is important to note that the project manager was promoted to sponsor after successfully
managing past similar projects. One can make the reasonable assumption that she has the
necessary expertise in project management principles and practices to carry out an analogous or
top-down project estimate. By using this technique, the project sponsor should be able to provide
the steering committee with enough information for a review of the project. Later, once the
project enters the planning stage, any rough order of magnitude (ROM) estimates created in

---

initiation (-25% to +75%) should be revisited by the project manager and updated with new
information to create definitive estimates (-5% to +10%).

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Use her own expert judgment and some historical information**
Correct. This answer choice describes analogous or top-down estimating. Analogous
estimating is a technique to estimate the duration or cost of an activity or project using
historical information. Analogous estimating is appropriate when the items being estimated
are similar in nature, and those preparing the estimates have the needed expertise. Since
the project sponsor is described as being successful in managing her past projects, it is
reasonable to assume that she has the skills necessary to provide the steering committee
with a preliminary project estimate using this technique.
- **B Get a professional estimate from external subject matter experts**
Incorrect. While this option presents a good idea, it is not the best choice since it involves
the use of ‘external’ subject matter experts (SMEs). No project budget or funds have been
committed to the project yet, nor is it clear from the question if any SMEs are available at
such short notice. Moreover, the sponsor should first check the organization’s process
assets library to find any relevant information that could be used in their project before
seeking outside (likely paid) advice from experts.
- **C Use the WBS to create an accurate bottom-up estimate**
Incorrect. Bottom-up estimating uses the greatest level of specific detail available. Detailed
estimates are then “rolled up” to higher levels for subsequent reporting and tracking
purposes. Since the project is in the initiation, the work breakdown structure (WBS) is not
yet available; therefore, creating a bottom-up estimate is unlikely to be a plausible option.
- **D Work with the project team to create the requested estimate**
Incorrect. The scenario implies that the project is still in the initiation. Therefore, it is
unlikely that any of the team members are available to assist in the estimating process
(unless some are already pre-assigned, but this cannot be determined from the information
given). While a better answer choice would have been to task the assigned project manager
with providing a rough order of magnitude (ROM) estimate, that option is not provided.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 200, 241, 79
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Prev Next

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 33 of 200
Question ID: 613054
Weather-related issues threaten the project objectives of a building construction project. In order
to determine if it is necessary to request a change in the project objectives, the project manager
needs to perform an earned value analysis.
With the actual schedule and cost performance data in hand, what should the project manager
do?
- **A Compare the actual results to the cost baseline**
- **B Compare the schedule baseline to the actual performance**
- **C Compare the actual results to the performance measurement baseline (PMB)**
- **D Create the baselines for scope, cost, and schedule.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project manager needs to compare actual results to all of the baselines.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The performance measurement baseline (PMB) is the integrated scope, schedule, and cost
baselines used for comparison to manage, measure, and control project execution. When using
earned value analysis, the PMB is compared to actual schedule and cost performance to
determine if a change, corrective action, or preventive action is necessary. Meeting the project
objectives means completing the entire scope of the project on time and budget. Only comparing
the actual project performance against the PMB will provide insight in determining whether or
not the project objectives (scope, cost, and schedule) can be met or if a change request is

---

necessary to adjust some or all of the project objectives. Therefore, of the available options,
comparing the actual results to the PMB is what the project manager should do.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Compare the actual results to the cost baseline**
Incorrect. The question states that the project objectives are threatened. The project
objectives include completing the entire scope of the project on time and on budget. Using
just the cost baseline will not help in determining if a change request is needed to adjust the
scope or schedule baselines for the project.
- **B Compare the schedule baseline to the actual performance**
Incorrect. With the project objectives at risk, the project manager will need to decide
whether or not to submit a change request to adjust the project scope, cost, and/or
schedule. Just using the schedule baseline will not provide the needed information related
to cost and scope.
- **C Compare the actual results to the performance measurement baseline (PMB)**
Correct. When using earned value analysis, the performance measurement baseline (PMB)
is compared to actual results to determine if a change, corrective action, or preventive
action is necessary.
- **D Create the baselines for scope, cost, and schedule.**
Incorrect. The question suggests that project execution has already begun; otherwise,
project performance data would not exist. The project baselines are created during various
processes of the Planning Process Group. Project execution cannot begin until the project
has been baselined. Therefore, the baselines must already exist at this point in the project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 259, 261
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Prev Next

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 34 of 200
Question ID: 612704
To reduce inventory costs, senior management has directed a project manager to establish a
just-in-time manufacturing process for a project.
What is the project manager’s best course of action?
- **A Implement total quality management (TQM)**
- **B Apply the theory of constraints methodology**
- **C Introduce a Kaizen approach**
- **D Adopt a Kanban process**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How might a system for scheduling inventory control and replenishment be established?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Kanban in lean manufacturing is a system for scheduling inventory control and replenishment.
This process of "just-in-time" inventory replenishment was originally seen in grocery stores
when shelves were restocked based on the gaps in the shelves and not supplier inventory.
Inspired by these just-in-time inventory systems, Taiichi Ohno developed Kanban, and it was
applied at the main Toyota manufacturing facility in 1953. Adopting a Kanban approach would
establish a pull system, where new inventory is ordered only when it is required. Therefore, of
the available choices, the best course of action is to adopt a Kanban process.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Implement total quality management (TQM)**
Incorrect. Total quality management (TQM) strives to create a culture of continuous
improvement to deliver high-quality products and services. TQM is established to improve
quality and not reduce inventory levels.
- **B Apply the theory of constraints methodology**
Incorrect. The theory of constraints is a method of identifying the most important limiting
factor, or constraint, and then improving that constraint until it is no longer a limiting
factor. Therefore, the theory of constraints can be effective in removing bottlenecks from a
manufacturing process, but it does not address inventory levels.
- **C Introduce a Kaizen approach**
Incorrect. Kaizen is the Japanese word for improvement. A Kaizen approach strives to
make incremental change through small steps and establishes a process of continuous
improvement. Introducing a Kaizen approach may be helpful in optimizing efficiency and
quality, and it might even be applied to inventory control. However, Kaizen is not directly
related to reducing inventory levels in a manufacturing process.
- **D Adopt a Kanban process**
Correct. Kanban in lean manufacturing is a system for scheduling inventory control and
replenishment. Adopting a Kanban approach would establish a pull system, where new
inventory is ordered only when it is required.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 310, 177; see also Agile Practice Guide - First
Edition, Project Management Institute Inc, 2018, Pages(s) 103
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 35 of 200
Question ID: 610092
According to the construction plan for a custom home, a standard type of concrete will be used
for the patio since the patio is required to support significantly less weight than a foundation on
which the patio is built. During an inspection, it was found that the concrete used for the patio is
of a stronger type, the same type that was used for the foundation.
Which of the following statements is true?
- **A The stronger concrete supports more weight and, therefore, is of higher quality.**
- **B The standard concrete was of lower quality and should not have been used anyway.**
- **C The patio of the house will be of a higher grade than originally planned.**
- **D By using the stronger concrete, the patio will exceed its defined quality metrics.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Quality and grade are not the same concepts.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Quality and grade are not the same concepts. Quality is defined as the degree to which the
product fulfills the requirements. Grade refers to the classification of products that have a
common function but offer different technical specifications. In the scenario described, concrete
is used as the foundation of the home and as a patio. However, the stronger concrete supports a
higher weight and is, therefore, a higher-grade concrete. The quality of either concrete will be
determined by whether it meets the established quality requirements that are defined in the
quality management plan, not by its grade. The scenario does not give us any information on the
quality of the patio, only that the higher-grade concrete was used. Since higher grade does not

---

mean higher quality, the only correct answer of all the options given is that the patio will be of a
higher grade than planned.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The stronger concrete supports more weight and, therefore, is of higher quality.**
Incorrect. In the scenario described, the stronger concrete is a higher grade, but not
necessarily higher quality. Quality and grade are not the same concepts. Different grades
are used to describe deliverables that have the same function but different technical
characteristics. Quality is defined as the degree to which the established requirements are
met. The stronger concrete is a higher grade because it supports a higher weight. However,
just because the concrete is a higher grade, does not necessarily mean the patio has met the
established quality requirements. The higher-grade concrete could be of low quality if the
mixing or pouring resulted in a patio that fails to meet the quality metrics.
- **B The standard concrete was of lower quality and should not have been used anyway.**
Incorrect. The standard concrete is of lower 'grade', not lower quality. Grade describes a
product's technical specifications, for example, the standard concrete supports less weight
than the stronger, 'high-grade' concrete. Quality is defined by how well the product meets
the established requirements. A low-grade product can be of high quality if it meets the
established quality metrics for the product, for example, zero defects. Therefore, the lower
grade concrete is not necessarily of lower quality, making this answer incorrect.
- **C The patio of the house will be of a higher grade than originally planned.**
Correct. Grade describes a product's technical specifications, for example, a product with a
higher grade may have more functions. In the scenario described, the stronger concrete
supports more weight than the standard concrete and is; therefore, a higher-grade concrete
making the patio a higher grade than initially planned.
- **D By using the stronger concrete, the patio will exceed its defined quality metrics.**
Incorrect. The quality metrics describe which attributes in a project will be measured and
what requirements must be met to determine if the attributes achieve the desired quality. In
the scenario described, the stronger concrete supports a higher weight and is, therefore, a
higher grade than the concrete that was planned for the patio. Grade describes a product's
specifications or technical characteristics whereas quality is defined by the degree to which
the established requirements are met. The use of high-grade concrete does not guarantee
the patio will meet or exceed the established specifications, or quality metrics, only that the

---

concrete will support more weight. Therefore, this is not the best answer to the question
asked.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 274

Question 36 of 200
Question ID: 612847
- **A project manager is leading a project, which is running behind schedule. A review of the team**
performance assessments indicates that one developer's productivity is lacking compared with
the others due to repetitive attendance issues.
What should the project manager do to determine the appropriate disciplinary actions specific to
this project?
- **A Check the resource management plan**
- **B Research the organizational process assets**
- **C Look at the project team directory**
- **D Consult with the developer's functional manager**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Guidance for disciplinary actions should have been developed during project planning.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The resource management plan is a component of the project management plan that describes
how project resources are acquired, allocated, monitored, and controlled. The resource
management plan specifies guidance on providing team member rewards, feedback, additional
training, and disciplinary actions as a result of team performance assessments and other forms of
project team management. Therefore, of the available options, checking the resource
management plan is the best answer to the question asked.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Check the resource management plan**
Correct. The resource management plan provides guidance on various aspects of team
development including disciplinary actions as a result of team performance assessments.
- **B Research the organizational process assets**
Incorrect. The organizational process assets may or may not have corporate policy and
procedures regarding disciplinary action. However, the question is asking for appropriate
disciplinary actions specific to the current project. The corporate policies and procedures
would apply to the organization as a whole and would not be customized for a particular
project. Note that the disciplinary actions outlined in the project management plan should
be consistent with company policies.
- **C Look at the project team directory**
Incorrect. The project team directory is a documented list of project team members, their
project roles, and communication information. This document does not specify the
disciplinary actions for the project.
- **D Consult with the developer's functional manager**
Incorrect. There is not enough information in the question to determine what type of the
organization is described in the scenario to assume if the developer comes from a
functional department. Even if yes, the project manager should seek sources of information
which are readily available before consulting with or escalating the issue to the functional
manager.

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 339

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 37 of 200
Question ID: 612935
Some of the changes requested on the project you are leading may result in the modification to
the original project requirements. To ensure these changes do not represent scope creep, you are
looking for a document that describes how requirements are analyzed, documented, and
managed.
Where would you find this information?
- **A Business analysis plan**
- **B Change management plan**
- **C Configuration management plan**
- **D Requirements traceability matrix**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the alternative name for the requirements management plan?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question implies that you, as the project manager, are performing the Control Scope process
in order to ensure that the suggested changes do not represent scope creep. The requirements
management plan, also known as the business analysis plan, describes how requirements are
analyzed, documented, and managed. The change management plan, configuration management
plan, and requirements management plan are all inputs into the Control Scope process. However,
the requirements management plan, or business analysis plan, is the only element of the project
management plan that would provide the requested information. Therefore, of the available
choices, the business analysis plan is the best response.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Business analysis plan**
Correct. The requirements management plan, sometimes referred to as the business
analysis plan, describes how requirements are analyzed, documented, and managed.
- **B Change management plan**
Incorrect. The change management plan is a component of the project management plan
that establishes the change control board, documents the extent of its authority, and
describes how the change control system will be implemented. This plan does not describe
how requirements are analyzed, documented, and managed.
- **C Configuration management plan**
Incorrect. The configuration management plan is a component of the project management
plan that describes how to identify and account for project artifacts under configuration
control, and how to record and report changes to them. This document may need to be
referenced in this scenario, but the configuration management plan does not provide
information on how requirements are to be managed.
- **D Requirements traceability matrix**
Incorrect: The requirements traceability matrix is a grid that links product requirements
from their origin to the deliverables that satisfy them. This document does not provide
information on how requirements are analyzed, documented, and managed.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 137, 169

PMP Exam 6
Question 38 of 200
Question ID: 612258
- **A project sponsor tells the project manager that stakeholder expectations and risk thresholds**
have not been addressed by a particular document. Project planning cannot begin until the
sponsor approves this document.
What might the project manager have neglected?
- **A Review of organizational process assets**
- **B Consideration of enterprise environmental factors**
- **C Development of a risk management plan**
- **D Creation of the risk register**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project manager is in the process of developing the project charter.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the project manager has developed a draft of the project charter,
which must be reviewed and approved by the project sponsor before project planning can begin.
High-level risks may be captured in the project charter and may be of particular importance if
key stakeholders have low-risk tolerances. Stakeholder expectations and risk thresholds are part
of the enterprise environmental factors, which may serve as an input into the development of the
project charter. Therefore, of the available answer choices, the project manager most likely did
not adequately consider the enterprise environmental factors.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Review of organizational process assets**
Incorrect. Although organizational process assets are inputs into the development of the
project charter, which is the document described in the question, stakeholder expectations
and risk thresholds are not an element of the organizational process assets.
- **B Consideration of enterprise environmental factors**
Correct. Stakeholder expectations and risk thresholds are part of the enterprise
environmental factors and serve as an input into the development of the project charter.
- **C Development of a risk management plan**
Incorrect. The risk management plan is a subsidiary of the project management plan. The
question implies that the project is still in the initiation stage, and the risk management
plan has not been developed.
- **D Creation of the risk register**
Incorrect. The question indicates that the project is still in the initiation stage. The risk
register is an output of the Identify Risks process, which occurs later during project
planning.

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 78

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 39 of 200
Question ID: 613273
- **A new executive, who has just joined the company emails the project manager who is leading**
one of the company's projects and requests to be included in all communications about the
project.
What should the project manager do next?
- **A Decline the request**
- **B Submit a change request**
- **C Consult with the sponsor**
- **D Meet with the executive**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How can the project manager best understand the needs of this stakeholder?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

This scenario involves several project management processes. Identify Stakeholders is one of
them. Meetings are used as part of this process to develop an understanding of significant project
stakeholders and their needs. Monitor Communications is another process that applies to this
scenario. Meetings, as they pertain to the Monitor Communications process, are held to respond
to stakeholder requests.
In this scenario, a new executive is asking to be included in all of the project's communications,
which are likely to be quite voluminous. It does not seem likely that an executive would need to
be informed on every aspect of a project, and an executive summary may be more appropriate.
The project manager should discuss what the executive's goals are for being included in the

---

project communications and what stake they have in the project. The project manager should
understand the needs and involvement of stakeholders before updating any documents. After
discussing the situation with the executive, the project manager will be in a better position to
determine how best to engage this stakeholder; then it will be appropriate to make arrangements,
including any necessary change requests, to update the relevant components of the project
management plan and project documents. Therefore, of the available options, talking to the
executive and understanding their needs is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Decline the request**
Incorrect. Declining a reasonable request without having a sound justification does not
sound like a plausible option.
- **B Submit a change request**
Incorrect. Submitting a change request is a premature action. Not only this answer choice
is vague as to what this change request is supposed to achieve, but also even if this change
is requested to update a component of the project management plan, the needs of the
executive should first be determined.
- **C Consult with the sponsor**
Incorrect. There is nothing unusual with the executive's request. It is a reasonable situation
when a new executive requests to be included in project communications. Instead of
consulting with the sponsor, the project manager should first meet with the executive to
understand their needs.
- **D Meet with the executive**
Correct. The project manager should first meet with the executive to understand their needs
and ask what the executive's goals are for being included in the project's communications.
After discussing the situation with the executive, the project manager will be in a better
position to determine how best to engage this stakeholder.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 514

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 40 of 200
Question ID: 612864
As part of monitoring and controlling costs for your project, you need to calculate a cost variance
(CV). You have already determined that $22,000 has been spent thus far on the project.
In order to calculate the CV, what should you do next?
- **A Check the project cost management plan**
- **B Examine the quality control measurements**
- **C Look up the budget at completion for the project**
- **D Review the cost baseline and project schedule**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The formula for cost variance is CV = EV - AC.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The cost variance (CV) is the earned value (EV) less the actual cost (AC). The actual cost is
provided as $22,000. Therefore, to calculate the CV, one should obtain the EV. The EV is the
budget associated with the authorized work that has been completed. The project manager has to
know what work packages have been completed so far and the planned values of these packages.
The values of the work packages are represented by the budget allocated for those packages. The
cost baseline is the approved version of the time-phased project budget and serves as one of the
inputs to the Control Costs process described in the scenario. The cost baseline should specify
the cost estimates broken down to the work package level (and even the activity level, if needed).
The project schedule, on the other hand, will show what work packages or activities have been
completed. Knowing these two elements, the packages/activities that have been completed and

---

their planned values (PVs), the project manager can calculate the EV, and, eventually, the CV as
requested by the question.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Check the project cost management plan**
Incorrect. To calculate the CV, the value of the work completed thus far is needed. The cost
management plan is the component of a project management plan that describes how costs
will be planned, structured, and controlled. While the cost management plan will provide
guidance for the Control Costs process, it does not have the values associated with
activities and work packages.
- **B Examine the quality control measurements**
Incorrect. Quality control measurements are the documented results of the activities
performed during the Control Quality process. These measurements do not provide
information related to the earned value analysis that is required for the calculation of the
cost variance as requested by the question.
- **C Look up the budget at completion for the project**
Incorrect. The budget at completion (BAC) is the sum of all budgets established for the
work to be performed. To calculate the CV, the value of the work completed thus far is
needed. The BAC does not provide work package level detail.
- **D Review the cost baseline and project schedule**
Correct. The cost variance (CV) is the earned value (EV) less the actual cost (AC). EV is
the budget associated with the authorized work that has been completed. The cost baseline
should have the cost estimates broken down to the work package level, and the project
schedule can indicate the activities that have already been completed. Together, these two
project artifacts will help determine the EV.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 254-255, 259, 261-262
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 41 of 200
Question ID: 651324
- **A major project deliverable has been completed and transitioned to operations. The project team**
is ready to move on to the next deliverable scheduled. One team member speaks up and asks if
the team should conduct a retrospective.
What is the project manager's best response?
- **A Yes, whenever any part of the project closes, the team can conduct a retrospective.**
- **B No, the retrospectives are held only after the project is closed.**
- **C Yes, but at the end of the project phase when we review the other deliverables.**
- **D No, retrospectives are only for agile chartered projects.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the objective of a retrospective?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

- **A retrospective is a scheduled review to record lessons that have been learned during the process**
of producing the project deliverables. Retrospectives are a valuable tool and technique of closing
any key time in the project - an iteration, phase, deliverable, milestone, or even the project as a
whole. These sessions are conducted as needed to help the project team learn from their work,
processes, and the project management practices. These lessons learned can be applied to the
future work of this project, as well as other projects. Therefore, of the choices provided,
responding to the team member that a retrospective should be conducted and it can be held
whenever any part of the project closes is the best answer to the question asked.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Yes, whenever any part of the project closes, the team can conduct a retrospective.**
Correct. Retrospectives can be held at any time during the project where there is an
opportunity for the project to document and discuss lessons learned, improvements, and
evaluate practices.
- **B No, the retrospectives are held only after the project is closed.**
Incorrect. Retrospectives are part of the Monitoring and Controlling Process Group and the
Closing Process Group. These sessions are held at any key time during the project.
- **C Yes, but at the end of the project phase when we review the other deliverables.**
Incorrect. A retrospective can occur at any point in the project. There is no requirement to
hold them at the end of an iteration or project phase.
- **D No, retrospectives are only for agile chartered projects.**
Incorrect. Whether a project is chartered and expected to be managed in a traditional
approach or an agile approach, the methodologies, tools, and techniques can be used in
any project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 127, 224, 305; see also the Agile Practice
Guide, Project Management Institute Inc, 2017, Page(s) 50-51

Question 42 of 200
Question ID: 612240
- **A project manager has taken over a project early in its execution. The company has a policy that**
specifies the minimum frequency for conducting risk audits on all projects.
What should the project manager do to determine the timing of the risk audits for this particular
project?
- **A Look in the project management plan**
- **B Check the applicable policy in the organizational process assets**
- **C Review the risk register for risk audit information**
- **D Use discretion to determine when and if a risk audit is needed**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Risk audits for a particular project might be performed more frequently than is required by the
company's policy.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Risk audits are a type of audit that may be used to consider the effectiveness of the risk
management process. The project manager is responsible for ensuring that risk audits are
performed at an appropriate frequency, as defined in the project's risk management plan.
Therefore, the best answer to the question asked is to check the risk management plan for the
information. However, the risk management plan was not offered as an answer choice. The risk
management plan is a subsidiary of the project management plan. Since the risk management
plan is not an option in this case, among the available choices, looking in the project
management plan is the best way to determine the timing of the risk audits for the project.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Look in the project management plan**
Correct. The risk management plan is a subsidiary of the project management plan. The
required frequency of risk audits is defined in the risk management plan.
- **B Check the applicable policy in the organizational process assets**
Incorrect. The company policy is part of the organizational process assets. Although the
policy may state a minimum frequency of risk audits, the risk management plan may require
more frequent risk audits based on what is appropriate for the project.
- **C Review the risk register for risk audit information**
Incorrect. The risk register is a repository in which the outputs of risk management
processes are recorded. The risk register does not specify the frequency of risk audits for
projects.
- **D Use discretion to determine when and if a risk audit is needed**
Incorrect. The project manager is responsible for ensuring that risk audits are performed at
an appropriate frequency, as defined in the project's risk management plan. Therefore, the
project manager does not have discretion over when and if a risk audit is needed.

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**

PMP Exam 6
Question 43 of 200
Question ID: 613374
- **A project manager is in the process of obtaining the necessary equipment for a high-rise building**
construction project. A review of the resource calendar reveals a conflict with the only tower
crane that has the required capabilities. The project manager wants to address the conflict with a
minor revision to the planned work.
What should the project manager do?
- **A Adjust the project schedule to accommodate the availability of the crane**
- **B Capture the information in the lessons learned register to improve project performance**
- **C Update the resource calendar to remove any potential conflicts**
- **D Adjust the resource requirements as necessary to eliminate any potential conflict**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The resource calendar is a calendar that identifies the working days and shifts upon which each
specific resource is available.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the project manager is carrying out the Acquire Resources process with
the acquisition of the tower crane. The resource calendar is a calendar that identifies the working
days and shifts upon which each specific resource is available. Therefore, the conflict that is
described by the question is a scheduling conflict. In this case, the scheduling conflict might be
resolved by making adjustments to the project schedule, so that the activities which require the
use of the tower crane are scheduled when the crane is available. None of the incorrect answer
choices will make the tower crane available, so the only other option is to adjust the schedule.

---

Therefore, of the available options, adjusting the project schedule to accommodate the crane
availability is what the project manager should do to minimize the conflict.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Adjust the project schedule to accommodate the availability of the crane**
Correct. The question suggests that a scheduling conflict exists with the required tower
crane. A scheduling conflict might be resolved by making adjustments to the project
schedule so that the activities which require the use of the required resource are scheduled
when the resource is available. Note, a change request is not required to update the project
schedule as long as the schedule baseline is not affected. There is not enough information
in the question to determine if the schedule baseline is affected.
- **B Capture the information in the lessons learned register to improve project performance**
Incorrect. Knowledge gained during project execution should be captured in the lessons
learned register to improve future performance. In this scenario, the capturing of any
lessons learned may or may not prevent future conflicts with the availability of required
resources but will not resolve the existing conflict with the tower crane.
- **C Update the resource calendar to remove any potential conflicts**
Incorrect. The resource calendar is a calendar that identifies the working days and shifts
upon which each specific resource is available. Therefore, the conflict that is described by
the question is a scheduling conflict. The resource calendar merely reflects resource
availability, and just changing the calendar does not change the fact that the tower crane is
not available during some portion of the project schedule.
- **D Adjust the resource requirements as necessary to eliminate any potential conflict**
Incorrect. The resource requirements reflect the types and quantities of resources required
for each activity in a work package. There is not enough information in the question to
determine if adjusting the resource requirements by, for example, substituting the tower
crane with a different resource would minimize the conflict. The question states that it is the
only tower crane that has the required capabilities. Since the resource is required, adjusting
the resource requirements is unlikely to be the best answer to the question asked.

Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 335

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 44 of 200
Question ID: 613638
You are working with the team to create a schedule network diagram. As you sequence the
activities to create your network diagram, your team begins to see which activities are most
important and how they depend on one another.
In addition to creating a network diagram, all of the following are potential outcomes of this
sequencing process except:
- **A Activity attributes are updated based on the discovery of new predecessors or successors.**
- **B The risk register is updated based on the discovery of path divergences and convergences,**
which indicate activities that are at greater risk.
- **C The activity list is updated based on the discovery of a new activity.**
- **D The amount of time each activity will take to complete is determined.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Duration estimates are an output of which schedule management process?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

In this scenario, the team is performing the Sequence Activities process, which involves
identifying and documenting relationships among the project activities. The key output of this
sequencing process is a project schedule network diagram, but various project documents are
also likely to be updated as a result of carrying out this process as new activities and/or
dependencies are discovered. Those documents include but are not limited to the activity
attributes and activity list. If new risks are discovered during the sequencing process, a logical
step would be to update the risk register. Since duration estimates are an output of a subsequent
schedule management process, Estimate Activity Durations, determining the amount of time

---

each activity will take to complete would not be an outcome of this sequencing process and is,
therefore, the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Activity attributes are updated based on the discovery of new predecessors or successors.**
Incorrect. As you sequence activities, it sometimes becomes apparent that two tasks rely on
each other. If you find new predecessors or successors, their attributes will need to be
updated.
- **B The risk register is updated based on the discovery of path divergences and convergences,**
which indicate activities that are at greater risk.
Incorrect. When you sequence your project activities, you may find activities that carry a
lot of risk to the project. For example, activities with divergence and convergence are at
greater risk as they are affected by multiple activities or can affect multiple activities. Any
risks you find in the process should be added to the risk register. While risk register updates
are not specifically listed in the PMBOK® Guide among the outputs of the Sequence
Activities process, it is reasonable to assume the risk register will need to be updated as
explained above. Note the language of the PMBOK® Guide, “Project documents that may
be updated as a result of carrying out this process include but are not limited to:”
- **C The activity list is updated based on the discovery of a new activity.**
Incorrect. During the sequencing process, you may find new activities that need to be
added. If you find a new activity while sequencing, updates need to be made to the activity
list.
- **D The amount of time each activity will take to complete is determined.**
Correct. In this scenario, the team is creating a schedule network diagram, which means
they are performing the Sequence Activities process. However, estimating the amount of
time each activity will take to complete takes place during the Estimate Activity Durations
process, which occurs after the team has finished sequencing activities.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 194-195

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 45 of 200
Question ID: 613184
As a project manager, you recently completed a project team performance appraisal, and a
previously unknown competency gap in technical skills was uncovered, which needs to be
addressed.
What should you do next?
- **A Implement the appropriate risk response**
- **B Conduct unplanned training to address the competency gap**
- **C Consult the training management plan**
- **D Let go of the staff who have technical skill gaps**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Unplanned training takes place as a result of observation, conversation, and project performance
appraisals conducted during management of the project team.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question states that a competency gap was uncovered as a result of a project team appraisal
which was previously unknown. As a result, the newly discovered training need is not likely to
be addressed in the resource management plan. If project team members lack the necessary
management or technical skills, such skills can be developed as part of the project work.
Scheduled training takes place as stated in the resource management plan. Unplanned training
takes place as a result of observation, conversation, and project performance appraisals
conducted during management of the project team. The incorrect answer choices represent
actions which do not directly address the newly discovered training need. Therefore, of the

---

available options, conducting unplanned training to address the competency gap is the best
response.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Implement the appropriate risk response**
Incorrect. Risk responses are developed to address risks that have been identified during
project planning or later as the project progresses. The competency gap is a risk. However,
according to the scenario, the gap was previously unknown, implying no response exists for
this risk.
- **B Conduct unplanned training to address the competency gap**
Correct. When project team members lack the necessary technical skills, these skills can be
developed as part of the project work. Unplanned training takes place as a result of
observation, conversation, and project performance appraisals conducted during
management of the project team.
- **C Consult the training management plan**
Incorrect. 'Training management plan' is a made-up term not specified in the PMBOK®
Guide.
- **D Let go of the staff who have technical skill gaps**
Incorrect. There is not enough information provided in the question to suggest that
termination of employment is appropriate in this situation. Termination is a serious action
that when initiated is generally the culmination of a series of progressive actions. Typically,
a plan should be created and followed to fill the technical deficiencies.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 342

Question 46 of 200
Question ID: 612680
You are developing your project’s resource management plan. You are looking for a project
document that would help you determine the specific types and quantities of resources needed
for the project.
What is your best course of action?
- **A Review the organizational process assets**
- **B Consult the requirements documentation**
- **C Check the project management plan**
- **D Look into the project charter**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What drives resource allocation, and in what project document can this information be found?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The scenario implies you are carrying out the Plan Resource Management process. The project
charter, several components of the project management plan, various project documents, as well
as enterprise environmental factors, and organizational process assets serve as inputs to this
process. However, the key sources used to determine resource specifics are the scope baseline,
the project schedule, and the requirements documentation. Together these will contain all the
activities, schedule detail, and requirements. Of the choices offered, only the requirements
documentation is a project document which contains the information that dictates the specific
types and quantities of resources needed, thus making the requirements documentation the best
answer to the question asked. The scope baseline (and the project management plan that contains

---

it) is not a project document. Organizational process assets are useful but provide only historical
details, while the project charter will contain high-level information only.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Review the organizational process assets**
Incorrect. While organizational process assets can provide guidance and historical
information, they do not contain the specifics of this project.
- **B Consult the requirements documentation**
Correct. Requirements will dictate the specific types and amounts of resources needed for
the project, and the requirements documentation contains all project requirements.
- **C Check the project management plan**
Incorrect. Although the project management plan does contain essential information, it is
not a project document.
- **D Look into the project charter**
Incorrect. The project charter does contain essential information that may help determine
the resources needed for the project. However, the information is all at a high level and
does not contain the details needed to determine specific resource types and quantities.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 314

PMP Exam 6
Question 47 of 200
Question ID: 613651
- **A project manager is searching for more information on the work being performed on the project**
he has recently taken over. He has been provided the WBS and the WBS dictionary. He hopes to
learn more details such as where some of the work is being performed and the effort involved in
completing that work.
Which of the following would best provide the information sought?
- **A Project team assignments**
- **B Performance measurement baseline**
- **C WBS detail report**
- **D Activity attributes**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Consider which answer would extend beyond the WBS to display more characteristics of the
activities.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Activity attributes provide information that extends the WBS and WBS dictionary descriptions
by identifying multiple components of each activity. In the initial stages, information such as
unique activity identifiers, labels and names may be included. As activities and their components
continue to evolve during the project, activity descriptions, resource requirements, constraints,
and leads and lags are examples of information that can be included. The activity attributes can
be useful in learning where work is being performed and the type of effort involved in
completing the work as described in this question.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project team assignments**
Incorrect. The project team assignments are the record of which resources are assigned to
each activity. However, it does not provide the detail described in this question.
- **B Performance measurement baseline**
Incorrect. The performance measurement baseline integrates the scope, schedule and cost
baselines; that integration is measured against project performance and execution. It does
not contain the detail sought in this question.
- **C WBS detail report**
Incorrect. 'WBS detail report" is a fake term made up for this question.
- **D Activity attributes**
Correct. Activity attributes extend the information of an activity by providing detail on
multiple components of project activities in the initial stages. More details can be provided
as the project progresses, such as where work is to be performed and the type of effort
involved.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 186

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 48 of 200
Question ID: 625023
- **A project manager is starting a new project for a client with whom the project manager has**
worked with before. Although this project is very different, it has many of the same stakeholders
as the prior project.
Is it ethical to use a stakeholder register from a previous project as a reference when identifying
project stakeholders for this project?
- **A Yes, because project management best practices recommend using information from past**
projects as an input to the Identify Stakeholders process
- **B No, because every project is unique and historic information does not apply for**
stakeholder identification
- **C No, the PMI Code of Ethics and Professional Conduct does not allow project managers to**
use old documents for new projects
- **D No, the PMBOK® Guide does not list the use of past project documents as a best practice**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Organizational process assets are inputs to the Identify Stakeholders process.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Organizational process assets are inputs to the Identify Stakeholders process. Lessons learned
and the stakeholder register from previous projects can be used as references for identifying
project stakeholders for any project. A stakeholder register from a past similar project can be
used as a starting point, where the project team can add, remove, or modify specific
names/positions.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Yes, because project management best practices recommend using information from past**
projects as an input to the Identify Stakeholders process
Correct. Prior stakeholder registers from previous projects can be very valuable and save
time. However, the lessons learned register should also be referenced to address how
accurate the stakeholder register was.
- **B No, because every project is unique and historic information does not apply for**
stakeholder identification
Incorrect. Although the projects are unique, people do not change frequently, and the
information from prior stakeholder registers might save some time and effort.
- **C No, the PMI Code of Ethics and Professional Conduct does not allow project managers to**
use old documents for new projects
Incorrect. The PMI Code of Ethics and Professional Conduct does not contain any text that
disallows or discourages project managers from using old documents for new projects.
- **D No, the PMBOK® Guide does not list the use of past project documents as a best practice**
Incorrect. The PMBOK® Guide does recommend using documents from prior projects in
the proper manner. In this situation, the PMBOK® Guide lists stakeholder registers from
previous projects as an organizational process asset, which can be used as an input to the
Identify Stakeholders process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 510

Question 49 of 200
Question ID: 612892
To schedule team building activities, the project manager wants to find details on the availability
of the team members so that the meetings would have a minimal impact on the project team
assignments.
What should the project manager do?
- **A Look at the resource calendar**
- **B Review the project team assignments**
- **C Check with the team members**
- **D Consult the project schedule**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where might the project manager find the working days and shifts upon which each specific
resource is available?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The resource calendar is a calendar that identifies the working days and shifts upon which each
specific resource is available helping identify times when the project team members can
participate in team development activities. The resource calendars may provide information on
the availability of other needed resources such as a meeting room, audio/visual equipment, etc.
The incorrect answer choices may or may not provide some information, but they do not specify
resource availability. Therefore, of the available options, looking at the resource calendar is the
best answer to the question asked.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Look at the resource calendar**
Correct. The resource calendar is a calendar that identifies the working days and shifts
upon which each specific resource is available. Thus, resource calendars may help identify
times when the project team members can participate in team building activities.
- **B Review the project team assignments**
Incorrect. The project team assignments identify the team and member roles and
responsibilities. However, the project team assignments do not provide insight into the team
members' availability to participate in team building activities.
- **C Check with the team members**
Incorrect. While checking with the team members may address the needs of the project
manager, this action is unlikely to be the best use of time of the project manager and the
team members when the requested information is readily available in project documents.
- **D Consult the project schedule**
Incorrect. The project schedule may provide some useful information including when the
project team members have existing commitments for completing project activities.
However, the project schedule does not have the team members availability for scheduling
activities as well as other resources that might be used such as a meeting room.

Question 50 of 200
Question ID: 651331
Three prospective vendors were selected and underwent high-level technical evaluations. Vendor
X scored slightly higher than vendors Y and Z. Nevertheless, the top procurement manager in the
company requests the project manager to select vendor Y over vendor X due to past experience,
reliability scores, and contract dealings. These criteria were not included in the evaluations but
described in the procurement management plan.
What is the project manager's best response?
- **A Follow the expert judgment of the procurement manager**
- **B Select vendor Z to avoid conflict of interest**
- **C Hold a bidder conference with vendors X and Y**
- **D Select vendor X based on technical criteria**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is in the best interest of the project?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Conducting procurements for the project requires information and consultation from different
sources. A high-level technical evaluation was conducted for this procurement need, but on its
own, it does not provide a complete picture of a potential sellers' ability to fulfill the procurement
needs. Additional evaluation is needed to assess a vendor's non-technical capabilities. The
procurement manager informally conducted such an evaluation. Given the choices presented,
moving forward with the procurement manager's expert judgment is the best option for the
project manager in this situation.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Follow the expert judgment of the procurement manager**
Correct. Technically - solely based on the high-level technical evaluation conducted -
vendor X rated higher, but the project manager must consider the additional information
and the advice of the procurement manager.
- **B Select vendor Z to avoid conflict of interest**
Incorrect. Vendor Z was determined not to be the best vendor choice from a technical
aspect and procurement aspect. There is nothing in the question that suggests a conflict of
interest with vendor Z.
- **C Hold a bidder conference with vendors X and Y**
Incorrect. A bidder conference is held prior to the bids to communicate the needs of a bid to
potential sellers. Such a meeting does not help in this situation.
- **D Select vendor X based on technical criteria**
Incorrect. Technical evaluations are important, but they do not provide the complete picture
of a vendor's ability to deliver and be a reliable supplier. It is important for the project
manager to assess the technical criteria along with other evaluation criteria is also
important.

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
