PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 51 of 200
Question ID: 612978
- **A project manager is in the process of defining and documenting stakeholders' needs for a**
software development project. The project manager feels that creating user stories might be
particularly helpful in this process.
What should the project manager do first?
- **A Schedule a requirements workshop**
- **B Hold an iteration retrospective**
- **C Conduct a sprint review meeting**
- **D Develop a requirements traceability matrix**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

User stories are short, textual descriptions of required functionality.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the Collect Requirements process is being carried out with the defining
and documenting stakeholders' needs. User stories, which are short, textual descriptions of
required functionality, are often developed during a requirements workshop. User stories
describe the stakeholder role, who benefits from the feature (role), what the stakeholder needs to
accomplish (goal), and the benefit to the stakeholder (motivation). The incorrect answer choices
represent activities that can only be performed after the requirements have been determined.
Therefore, of the available options, scheduling a requirements workshop is the best response.
Note, although the scenario suggests the project is managed using agile methodology where
traditional project management processes may or may not be conducted as specified in the

---

PMBOK® Guide, some of the answer choices and the explanations refer to the traditional
approach. Regardless of this, scheduling a requirements workshop is still the best answer to the
question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Schedule a requirements workshop**
Correct. User stories, which are short, textual descriptions of required functionality, are
often developed during a requirements workshop.
- **B Hold an iteration retrospective**
Incorrect. An iteration retrospective is a scheduled review to record lessons learned from
the iteration. The question suggests that the Collect Requirements process is being
conducted and a retrospective would not be conducted as part of the Collect Requirements
process.
- **C Conduct a sprint review meeting**
Incorrect. A sprint review is a meeting where the project team demonstrates the product
increment that has been built during the iteration in order to get feedback from
stakeholders and gain the approval of the product owner. The question implies that the
Collect Requirements process is underway. Requirements must be determined before an
increment of the product can be developed. Note, the exam may use the terms "sprint" and
"iteration" interchangeably.
- **D Develop a requirements traceability matrix**
Incorrect. The requirements traceability matrix is a grid that links product requirements
from their origin to the deliverables that satisfy them. The question suggests that the
Collect Requirements process is underway, and the requirements traceability matrix is an
output of this process. Customer requirements must first be gathered before the information
can be recorded in the requirements traceability matrix.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 145

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 52 of 200
Question ID: 613013
Which of the following integrates scope, cost, and schedule and should be updated to reflect
changes to a project?
- **A Benefits management plan**
- **B Performance measurement baseline**
- **C Risk register**
- **D Requirements traceability matrix**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Only one of the choices integrates cost, schedule, and scope.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The performance measurement baseline (PMB) is a component of the project management plan
that integrates scope, schedule, and cost baselines and is used for comparison to manage,
measure, and control project execution. In order for the project manager and the team to be able
to use the PMB as a measure of the project's performance, the PMB must be updated to reflect
the current state of the project, which includes all the approved changes. If the PMB is not
updated, it will give an inaccurate representation of the performance and will not be useful when
compared to the results of the earned value analysis.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Benefits management plan**
Incorrect. The benefits management plan defines the processes for creating, maximizing,
and sustaining the benefits provided by a project. The benefits management plan does not
integrate scope, cost, and schedule. The plan is neither a project document nor a
component of the project management plan and should, therefore, not be updated to reflect
changes to a project.
- **B Performance measurement baseline**
Correct. The performance measurement baseline (PMB) is a plan that integrates the scope,
schedule, and cost baselines. When changes are implemented, the PMB must be updated to
reflect these changes. The actual results of the project's execution are compared to the PMB
to measure and manage performance.
- **C Risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register is a repository in which the outputs of the risk management
processes are recorded. While the risk register can be updated with the new risks that may
arise as the result of the changes, the risk register is not an integrated scope, cost, and
schedule baseline implied by the question.
- **D Requirements traceability matrix**
Incorrect. The requirements traceability matrix is a grid that links product requirements
from their origin to the deliverables that satisfy them. This document can be updated as a
result of changes to the project. However, the requirements traceability matrix does not
integrate scope, cost, and schedule, making this choice an incorrect answer.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 88, 169

PMP Exam 6
Question 53 of 200
Question ID: 612509
To better use existing knowledge and to create new knowledge for a project, the project manager
is looking for ways to identify any knowledge gaps.
Which of the following would help the project manager the most to complete this process?
- **A Bid documents**
- **B Resource breakdown structure**
- **C Quality metrics**
- **D To-complete performance index**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which of the following includes information on the composition of the team?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Using existing knowledge and creating new knowledge for a project is essentially the definition
of the Manage Project Knowledge process. When the knowledge that the project has is compared
to its knowledge needs, then the gaps in knowledge can be identified and addressed. Specifically,
the resource breakdown structure, as it pertains to the Manage Project Knowledge process,
includes information on the composition of the team and may help to understand what
knowledge is available as a group and what knowledge may be missing.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Bid documents**
Incorrect. Bid documents are used to solicit information, quotations, or proposal from
prospective sellers. First, it is not clear from the scenario if the project involves sellers.
Second, even if it does, the information included in the bid documents is limited to the work
outsourced to the sellers.
- **B Resource breakdown structure**
Correct. The resource breakdown structure is a hierarchical representation of resources by
category and type. The resource breakdown structure is one of the project documents that
serve as an input for the Manage Project Knowledge process described in the scenario. The
resource breakdown structure includes information on the composition of the team and may
help to understand what knowledge is available as a group and what knowledge is missing
- **C Quality metrics**
Incorrect. A quality metric is a description of a project or product attribute and the way the
Control Quality process will verify compliance to it. Quality metrics have little to do with
using and preservice knowledge on a project.
- **D To-complete performance index**
Incorrect. The to-complete performance index (TCPI) is a measure of the cost performance
that is required to be achieved with the remaining resources in order to meet a specified
management goal. The TCPI is just one piece of information, while the goal of the project
manager in the scenario provided is to use existing knowledge and create new knowledge
for the project. It does not seem reasonable that the TCPI can help in accomplishing this
goal.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 101

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 54 of 200
Question ID: 625210
- **A project manager is in the middle of executing a project when they discover the project is**
behind schedule. The project deadline cannot be extended, and the project sponsor will not
approve any scope or budget changes.
Which of the following is the best course of action for the project manager to take to complete
the project faster?
- **A Hire additional resources and work overtime**
- **B Tell the sponsor that the deadline cannot be met**
- **C Look at options for fast tracking the critical path**
- **D Level the resources**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What technique can the project manager use to shorten the project schedule without increasing
cost?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The project manager must complete the project faster without making any changes to the project
scope or budget. Therefore, the project manager's best course of action is to use a schedule
compression technique. Crashing is a schedule compression technique used to shorten the
schedule duration by adding additional resources, but this may result in increased cost. Since the
project sponsor will not approve any budget changes, crashing is not a good choice. Fast tracking
is a schedule compression technique in which activities or phases that are normally done in
sequence, are performed in parallel for at least a portion of their duration. Since fast tracking can

---

expedite the schedule without resulting in increased cost, fast tracking is the best answer among
the choices provided. Note, fast tracking may result in rework and increased risk.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Hire additional resources and work overtime**
Incorrect. Hiring additional resources and working overtime refers to crashing, a technique
used to shorten the schedule duration by adding resources. Although crashing is a schedule
compression technique, adding additional resources is expensive and could negatively
affect the project budget. Since the question states that the sponsor will not approve any
budget changes, crashing is not the best choice.
- **B Tell the sponsor that the deadline cannot be met**
Incorrect. Telling the sponsor that the required date cannot be met does nothing to address
the problem. A project manager's role is to help determine options and recommend
solutions to problems as they arise on a project.
- **C Look at options for fast tracking the critical path**
Correct. Fast tracking is a schedule compression technique in which activities that are
normally done in a sequence are performed in parallel to complete the project schedule in
a shorter time frame.
- **D Level the resources**
Incorrect. Resource leveling is a resource optimization technique. Since resource leveling
typically extends the schedule, this would not be a good choice.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 215
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
q Prev Next

PMP Exam 6
Question 55 of 200
Question ID: 612870
In order to support the continuous development of your project team, you schedule monthly
skill-building meetings. Lately, the meetings have become contentious and veered off topic.
What might you do to make the meetings more productive?
- **A Covering applicable human resources policies and procedures at the start of the meeting**
- **B Providing individual training opportunities rather than using a group setting**
- **C Canceling the meetings if they become counterproductive**
- **D Reviewing the team charter with the project team**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where might agreed-upon guidelines for meeting etiquette be found?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The team charter establishes clear expectations regarding acceptable behavior by project team
members. Discussing areas such as codes of conduct, communication, decision making, and
meeting etiquette allows team members to discover values that are important to one another. The
team charter can be reviewed and updated periodically to ensure a continued understanding of
the team ground rules. Therefore, of the available options, reviewing the team charter with the
project team is the best way to make the skill building meetings more productive.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Covering applicable human resources policies and procedures at the start of the meeting**
Incorrect. While covering policies and procedures may or may not be helpful in keeping the
meeting on track, using the guidelines to which the project team has developed and agreed
is a better option.
- **B Providing individual training opportunities rather than using a group setting**
Incorrect. While avoiding group situations may reduce opportunities for conflict, it also
deprives the project team members the opportunity to share best practices and learn from
each other. It is better to establish and follow agreed-upon guidelines for meeting conduct
rather than avoiding team interaction.
- **C Canceling the meetings if they become counterproductive**
Incorrect. Canceling the skill-building meetings is an extreme action that is not likely to be
necessary. It is better to seek a common understanding among the team members to keep
the meetings on track.
- **D Reviewing the team charter with the project team**
Correct. The team charter is a document that records the team values, agreements, and
operating guidelines, as well as establishing clear expectations regarding acceptable
behavior by project team members.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 319-320, 339

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 56 of 200
Question ID: 612781
The project manager on a project to build a manufacturing plant is having trouble getting the
attention of the company’s CEO, who is one of the project's stakeholders. However, the project’s
architect who is designing the plant and works with the project manager on a daily basis is a
close friend of the CEO.
Should the project manager exploit the architect’s relationship with the CEO to open lines of
communication?
- **A No. Exploiting the architect's relationship with the CEO is a violation of the PMI Code of**
Ethics and Professional Conduct.
- **B Yes. The project's architect is part of the team and must cooperate and help manage**
stakeholder engagement.
- **C Yes. There is nothing wrong with exploiting the architect's relationship with the CEO.**
- **D No. The project manager should stop trying to get the attention of the CEO.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Using a go-between for communications is normal.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Using other people to make a connection with a third party is fully acceptable. Networking is a
powerful tool that can be used to influence the actions of stakeholders and increase support for
the work and outcomes of the project, thus improving performance. Networking is an
interpersonal and team skill that can be used among the tools and techniques of many project
management processes, such as Manage Communications, the process implied by the scenario.
In this situation, if making that connection requires using a subordinate, care must be taken that

---

no one feels that there is some form of reciprocity required. The person in the middle cannot feel
coerced, or that they will get favorable treatment for the action. That said, the project manager
could ask the architect to help make the connection with the CEO.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A No. Exploiting the architect's relationship with the CEO is a violation of the PMI Code of**
Ethics and Professional Conduct.
Incorrect. The PMI Code of Ethics and Professional Conduct does not restrict a project
management practitioner from exploiting their relationship with stakeholders as long as
this action does not involve favoritism, coercion, self-interest, or the like.
- **B Yes. The project's architect is part of the team and must cooperate and help manage**
stakeholder engagement.
Incorrect. Just because the architect is part of the team does not mean that the architect
must act as the go-between with the CEO. If the architect is not willing to leverage a
personal connection in this way, they should not be forced nor should they get favorable
treatment for this action.
- **C Yes. There is nothing wrong with exploiting the architect's relationship with the CEO.**
Correct. Exploiting one's relationship with the project stakeholders is an example of
networking. Networking may help the project manager and the team influence the actions
of their stakeholders (e.g., the CEO), and increase stakeholder support for the work and
outcomes of the project, thus improving performance.
- **D No. The project manager should stop trying to get the attention of the CEO.**
Incorrect. The CEO is an important stakeholder of the project. Therefore, it is important for
the project manager to communicate and manage the engagement of the CEO as a
stakeholder.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 383, 534, 386

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 57 of 200
Question ID: 613108
- **A complex project to develop the prototype for a new communication satellite is underway. The**
project team is preparing checklists and detailed traceability matrices to be used later in the
project to determine if the quality objectives for the project have been achieved.
Which of the following is the project team preparing?
- **A Quality reports**
- **B Test and evaluation documents**
- **C Change requests**
- **D Organizational process assets**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Identify the best place to assemble these quality control documents as they are completed during
the Manage Quality process.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question indicates that you are in the Manage Quality process. Test and evaluation
documents are often used in complex projects with extensive regulatory or contractual
requirements. According to the scenario, the project is complex, and it is reasonable to assume
that there are extensive performance requirements. The numerous documents designed by the
team to ensure that these requirements are met will be assembled in detailed test and evaluation
documents as an output from the Manage Quality process and will be used later in the project as
an input to the Control Quality process.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Quality reports**
Incorrect. Quality reports are used to present findings, issues, and recommendations
concerning quality, but they do not typically contain the checklists and detailed traceability
matrices.
- **B Test and evaluation documents**
Correct. Test and evaluation documents are outputs of the Manage Quality process and
inputs to the Control Quality process. They are used to evaluate the achievement of quality
objectives and typically include checklists and other documents such as requirements
traceability matrices.
- **C Change requests**
Incorrect. While change requests are outputs of the Manage Quality process described in
the scenario, the question specifically focuses on the checklists and detailed traceability
matrices to determine if the quality objectives for the project have been achieved which is
best described by the test and evaluation documents.
- **D Organizational process assets**
Incorrect. Although organizational process assets (OPAs) may include checklists and
requirements traceability matrices used elsewhere in the organization or on previous
projects, it is not an appropriate location to assemble completed quality documents for
projects still in progress. Additionally, OPAs are not among the outputs of the Manage
Quality process implied by the scenario.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page 296

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 58 of 200
Question ID: 612773
- **A company is about to undertake a project that will use new technology. It is expected that the**
customer will request a very large number of changes throughout the entire project life cycle.
The project sponsor indicated that delivering incremental value to the customer frequently while
maintaining the cost baseline under control is of the utmost importance for the project.
Which of the following would help the most in addressing the frequent changes?
- **A Time-boxing**
- **B Integrated change control**
- **C Risk register**
- **D Quality control measurements**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What tool or technique can address frequent change?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

With the new technology used on the project, many changes anticipated from the customer,
keeping the cost baseline under control, and the need to deliver incremental value frequently,
selecting the right project management approach is essential. Such a project environment is best
addressed using the combination of agile and predictive methodologies. As far as project
scheduling is concerned, applying iterative schedule with a backlog to develop the product is a
common agile practice. The requirements are documented in user stories that are then prioritized
and refined just prior to their development, and the product features are built using time-boxed
periods of work, typically called iterations. This approach is often used to frequently deliver
incremental value to the customer, which is what was required by the project sponsor in the

---

question. Adaptive methodologies are better suited to projects with frequently changing project
requirements, such as in the scenario described. When using an adaptive life cycle, the
time-boxed periods for releases, waves, and iterations are specified. Time-boxed periods are
durations during which the team works steadily toward the completion of a goal. Therefore, of
the choices provided, using time-boxing to address frequent changes and delivering value to the
customer would help the most, making time-boxing the best answer to the question asked.
Note, agile projects typically have a fixed budget. Therefore, when functional product
increments are delivered frequently, the risk the project budget will be exceeded is low. The
reason being is that when the project runs out of budget, the project can be terminated at any
given moment, but the customer will still have the latest functioning product increment delivered
in the most recent iteration. This is the most likely reason the sponsor indicated that the cost
baseline should be kept under strict control.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Time-boxing**
Correct. Time-boxing is an effective tool that can be used on projects where requirements
are anticipated to change frequently. This approach is used on agile projects where the
requirements are documented in user stories that are prioritized and refined just before
being developed, and the product features are delivered using time-boxed periods of work.
- **B Integrated change control**
Incorrect. Integrated change control addresses scope creep. Still, it is typically a lengthy
process that does not always accommodate rapidly changing project requirements,
especially when frequently delivering incremental value to the customer is of the utmost
priority, as stated by the scenario.
- **C Risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register is a project document where outputs of the risk management
processes are documented. The risk register has little to do with the frequently changing
requirements.
- **D Quality control measurements**
Incorrect. Quality control measurements are the documented results of control quality
activities. While testing the changes to meet the project quality standards is necessary,

---

carrying out these activities does not address the essence of the question, which is
addressing frequent changes and delivering incremental value to the customer.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 177, 182
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Question 59 of 200
Question ID: 651322
There are many projects under the management of one program. The program manager requests
that before one of the projects wraps up that the project manager and the team review and
analyze the relationships between project variables that may have contributed to the project's
success. The program manager would like to apply those findings to other projects in the
program.
What technique are the project manager and team to use?
- **A Benchmarking**
- **B Earned value analysis**
- **C Regression analysis**
- **D Variance analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is being examined?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The program manager is requesting the project manager and team to identify relationships
between project variables to help predict, forecast, or understand outcomes in their project.
Regression analysis does just that. If relationships are modeled, they could be used by other
projects in the program to improve performance. Regression analysis estimates relationships
between independent variables (predictor or explanatory) and a dependent variable (response or
outcome). Knowing the connection between an independent variable(s) and a dependent variable
lets the project team predict what might occur based on the interrelations. This information may

---

help the program manager understand what project variables have contributed to the project's
success in order to apply those findings to other projects in the program.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Benchmarking**
Incorrect. Benchmarking is comparing one product or process with comparable
organizations' products and processes to identify targets and provide a basis for measuring
performance. That outcome is not sought by the program manager in this question.
- **B Earned value analysis**
Incorrect. Earned value analysis is a technique that compares the performance
measurement baseline to the actual schedule, cost, or scope performance. This technique is
not looking at variables and their relationships.
- **C Regression analysis**
Correct. Regression analysis is conducted to evaluate the interrelationships between
various project variables to determine if any independent variables are related to a
dependent variable and then uses that information to make predictions or forecasts based
on those variables.
- **D Variance analysis**
Incorrect. Variance analysis is examining the difference or variance between data points.
The program manager is not seeking to know the delta between data points but the
relationship between variables.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 126
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 6
Question 60 of 200
Question ID: 625209
You have been hired to take over a project in which the process of numerically analyzing
identified risks has just been completed. As you are reviewing the risk register, you see this
project has a lot of risks, and you are trying to quickly determine where to focus your efforts.
You want to use a graphical representation to compare the importance and impact of risks.
What tool would best meet your needs?
- **A A histogram**
- **B A Pareto diagram**
- **C A Gantt chart**
- **D A tornado diagram**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which kind of graph is used with sensitivity analysis in quantitative risk analysis?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The tornado diagram is a graphical display of a sensitivity analysis. The risks are ordered
vertically from the highest degree of uncertainty to the most stable. This type of graph assists the
project manager with determining which risks are most critical and need the most focus.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A A histogram**
Incorrect. A histogram shows the statistical distribution of results.
- **B A Pareto diagram**
Incorrect. A Pareto diagram shows results ordered by frequency of occurrence.
- **C A Gantt chart**
Incorrect. A Gantt chart is a bar chart depicting schedule information.
- **D A tornado diagram**
Correct. A tornado diagram is a special type of bar chart used in sensitivity analysis for
comparing the relative importance of variables. The risks are ordered from the highest
degree of uncertainty to the most stable thereby allowing a visual representation of the
risks.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 434

Question 61 of 200
Question ID: 651332
Your project is installing WiFi stations in rural areas. The response rate for the surveys sent out
to residents in the affected areas has been extremely low. Expectations were to have a majority of
them returned by this point in the project.
What most likely is the reason for this issue?
- **A This possibility was not entered as an identified risk in the risk register.**
- **B There was not enough budget for the WiFi stations.**
- **C There is a misunderstanding of the culture of the affected stakeholders.**
- **D The stakeholders do not have WiFi internet access.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Who is the most impacted by this issue?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

When executing a project, a project manager and the project team must utilize various skills.
Being culturally aware in order to communicate effectively with stakeholders is one of those
skills. When increasing stakeholder engagement, one must consider cultural differences,
preferences, and communication styles of stakeholders. The low response rate from the affected
stakeholders may be a result of the poor cultural awareness and carrying out of the project plans,
making it the most likely reason for the issue described in the scenario.

---

Note, the question does not imply the residents of the rural area are unaware of the technology.
It's the project manager who is unaware of the culture of the residents.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A This possibility was not entered as an identified risk in the risk register.**
Incorrect. Whether this possibility is listed in the risk register does not change the fact that
it occurred. It is not the reason for the issue. The only implication with this choice is if the
project did identify the risk, hopefully, there is a planned response.
- **B There was not enough budget for the WiFi stations.**
Incorrect. Stakeholder engagement is not affected by the project's budget based on the
information provided, so lack of budget for the WiFi stations is unlikely to have caused the
poor response rate of the survey.
- **C There is a misunderstanding of the culture of the affected stakeholders.**
Correct. The low stakeholder engagement may be due to various reasons with the
misunderstanding of the culture being highly probable.
- **D The stakeholders do not have WiFi internet access.**
Incorrect. The project is well aware that the stakeholders do not have internet access; the
objective of the project is to install WiFi stations in their area.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 527

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 62 of 200
Question ID: 651435
To ensure that units produced by a new manufacturing line meet customer specifications, a
project team has been requested to conduct attribute sampling on the first 100 units from the line.
What should the team do to comply with this request?
- **A Ensure that the correct number of units was produced**
- **B Conduct multicriteria decision analysis**
- **C Check the existence of a specific characteristic in each sample unit**
- **D Review the lessons learned register**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Attribute sampling will result in a conclusion that a unit either conforms to the specifications or
it does not. The result is either pass or fail.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The scenario suggests the project team is about to carry out the Control Quality process.
Depending on the project and the industry, the project team may need a working knowledge of
statistical control processes to evaluate data contained in the outputs of this process. Attribute
sampling is a method of measuring quality that consists of noting the presence (or absence) of
some characteristic (attribute) in each of the units under consideration. The scenario does not
specify what attribute should be tested. However, to answer the question correctly, this
information is not required. Basic understanding of attribute sampling may help in selecting the

---

correct answer choice: to comply with the request of conducting attribute sampling, the team
should check the existence of a characteristic in each unit.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Ensure that the correct number of units was produced**
Incorrect. Attribute sampling is a method to confirm the presence (or absence) of some
characteristic (attribute) in each unit rather than ensure that the correct number of units
was produced.
- **B Conduct multicriteria decision analysis**
Incorrect. Multicriteria decision analysis is an example of a decision-making technique,
which can be used as a tool in many project management processes. As it pertains to the
Control Quality process described in the scenario, multicriteria decision making is used to
evaluate several criteria when discussing alternatives that impact the project or product
quality. This tool is not used to ensure that the deliverables meet customer specifications.
- **C Check the existence of a specific characteristic in each sample unit**
Correct. Attribute sampling is a method of measuring quality that consists of noting the
presence (or absence) of some characteristic (attribute) in each of the units under
consideration. This answer choice meets the description of attribute sampling making this
choice the best answer to the question asked.
- **D Review the lessons learned register**
Incorrect. The lessons learned register is a project document used to record knowledge
gained during a project. This document is unlikely to help the team to ensure the units meet
customer specifications, nor the process of reviewing the lessons learned register resembles
the process of attribute sampling.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 274, 675, 699

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 63 of 200
Question ID: 612776
Your project team is about to begin the adjourning stage of team development.
How can you best support your team during this process?
- **A Reward the team with a celebration meeting and ensure that the team members are**
reassigned
- **B Conduct a kick-off meeting so the team can learn about the project and their roles and**
responsibilities
- **C Provide support as needed so the team can continue to function as a well-organized unit**
- **D Utilize conflict management skills to ensure the environment does not become**
counterproductive
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The adjourning stage of team development typically occurs during the Close Project or Phase
process.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question is in reference to the Tuckman ladder, which is one of the models used to describe
team development. This model includes five stages of development that teams may go through
including forming, storming, norming, performing, and adjourning. During the adjourning phase
of team development, the team completes the work and moves on from the project. This stage is
when staff is typically released as deliverables are completed or as part of the Close Project or
Phase process. Therefore, of the available choices, rewarding the team with a celebration

---

meeting and ensuring that the team members are reassigned is the best way for you, as the
project manager, to support the project team with the adjourning stage of team development.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Reward the team with a celebration meeting and ensure that the team members are**
reassigned
Correct. During the adjourning phase of team development, the team completes the work
and moves on from the project. This stage is when staff is typically released as deliverables
are completed or as part of the Close Project or Phase process.
- **B Conduct a kick-off meeting so the team can learn about the project and their roles and**
responsibilities
Incorrect. This answer choice best supports the forming, rather than adjourning, stage of
team development. During the forming stage, team members meet and learn about the
project and their formal roles and responsibilities.
- **C Provide support as needed so the team can continue to function as a well-organized unit**
Incorrect. This answer choice best supports the performing, rather than adjourning, stage
of team development. During the performing stage, the team functions as a well-organized
unit and work through issues smoothly and effectively.
- **D Utilize conflict management skills to ensure the environment does not become**
counterproductive
Incorrect. This answer choice best supports the storming, rather than adjourning, stage of
team development. During the storming stage, the team begins to address the project work,
technical decisions, and the project management approach. If the team members are not
collaborative, the environment can become counterproductive.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 338
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 64 of 200
Question ID: 613026
You are leading a meeting with a group of stakeholders to prioritize the product requirements for
your project. After several rounds of voting, no prioritized ranking of product requirements
attains more than 50% of the votes.
With the meeting at an impasse, what is your best course of action in this scenario assuming you
don't want to decide for the group?
- **A Continue the meeting until unanimity can be reached**
- **B Allow the majority to determine the prioritization of the requirements**
- **C Permit the plurality of voters to prioritize the requirements**
- **D Use autocratic decision making to set the priority of the requirements**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer choice allows the largest voting block in the group to make the decision?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

You, as the project manager, are using the decision-making technique of voting to determine a
prioritized ranking of product requirements. Without being able to establish a majority for the
requirements ranking, settling for a plurality may be the only viable option at this point. In the
plurality decision-making technique, the largest voting block in the group decides even if a
majority is not achieved. Permitting the plurality of voters to determine the prioritized ranking of
product requirements will appease the greatest number of stakeholders participating in the

---

meeting. Therefore, of the available options, the best course of action is to permit the plurality of
voters to determine the ranking of product requirements.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Continue the meeting until unanimity can be reached**
Incorrect. With the meeting at an impasse, continuing with the meeting until unanimity is
reached is not realistic. Unanimity would require all of the participants to agree to a
ranking of product requirements, and, in this scenario, no group has more than 50% of the
votes.
- **B Allow the majority to determine the prioritization of the requirements**
Incorrect. The question states that no prioritized ranking of product requirements has
attained more than 50% of the votes. A majority can only be reached when more than 50%
of the participants are in agreement. Therefore, there is no majority in this scenario.
- **C Permit the plurality of voters to prioritize the requirements**
Correct. You, as the project manager, are using the decision-making technique of voting to
determine a prioritized ranking of product requirements. Without being able to establish a
majority for the requirements ranking, settling for the plurality of votes may be the only
viable option at this point.
- **D Use autocratic decision making to set the priority of the requirements**
Incorrect. Autocratic decision making is a plausible choice when the meeting is at an
impasse. However, the question states you don't want to decide for the group, implying
autocratic decision making is not an option.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 144
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 65 of 200
Question ID: 612390
You are managing a multi-phase project to design and build a new attraction for an amusement
park. During the build phase, the project manager learns that a permit that was required before
the start of the build phase had been denied in the design phase and all work must stop until this
issue is resolved.
What did the project manager likely miss?
- **A Nothing, the project manager was informed too late, and it wasn't his fault this was not**
caught sooner
- **B Holding a phase gate review meeting at the end of the design phase**
- **C Allocating sufficient contingency reserves to allow for such issues if they arise**
- **D Including permitting experts as key stakeholders on the project team**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What would have provided a checkpoint before proceeding to the build stage?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

- **A phase gate, sometimes called phase review, stage gate, kill point, phase entrance or phase exit,**
is held at the end of a phase. The project's performance and progress are compared to project and
business documents. A decision, such as go/no-go, is made based on this review to continue to
the next phase, continue to the next phase with modification, end the project, remain in the phase
or repeat the phase or element of it. The question indicates that a project should have been

---

stopped before allowing the build phase to start when a key requirement, the approval of the
permit had been achieved.
Had the project manager held the phase gate review, the information about the denial of the
permit would have been communicated to the project stakeholders and a decision not to proceed
would have been made.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Nothing, the project manager was informed too late, and it wasn't his fault this was not**
caught sooner
Incorrect. It is the project manager's responsibility to know the requirements and exit
criteria of each phase and conduct a phase gate prior to move into the next phase. The
project manager is ultimately responsible for missing this critical issue and is responsible
for the project stoppage.
- **B Holding a phase gate review meeting at the end of the design phase**
Correct. A phase gate is held at the end of a phase to compare project performance to exit
criteria for that phase. It is very likely that the approval of the permit was an exit criterion
for the design phase and this was missed because no phase gate was conducted before
moving on to the build stage.
- **C Allocating sufficient contingency reserves to allow for such issues if they arise**
Incorrect. The is no mention in the question that the permit approval was a risk that had
been identified and required contingency reserves in the schedule to avoid this issue.
- **D Including permitting experts as key stakeholders on the project team**
Incorrect. There is nothing in the question that supports there was a lack of critical
knowledge or expertise but instead poor communication and/or failure to follow proper
procedures for a multi-phase project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 21, 81

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 66 of 200
Question ID: 612809
You are a project manager who is currently in the closing stage of a project. You want to make
sure that the project objectives are met before considering the project closed.
Which of the following should be reviewed before declaring the project closed?
- **A Project management plan**
- **B Requirements documentation**
- **C Physical resource assignments**
- **D Summary of the kick-off meeting**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Scope should be compared with one of these documents to determine if all of the project
objectives have been met.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question states you are carrying out the Close Project or Phase process. All of the answer
choices describe inputs to this process. However, only the project management plan contains the
three baselines (scope, schedule, cost) against which project performance is measured. The
project management plan, including its subsidiary plans and the baselines, are updated
throughout the project to include the latest understanding of project objectives and project
approval requirements. Therefore, among the choices provided, to make sure that the project
objectives are met before considering the project closed, you should review the project
management plan.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Project management plan**
Correct. The project management plan is the document that describes how the project will
be executed, monitored and controlled, and closed. The project management plan includes
all the subsidiary management plans and baselines for the project that covers all the
information needed for the project manager to determine whether the project has met its
objectives and can be closed, making this choice the best answer to the question asked.
- **B Requirements documentation**
Incorrect. Requirements documentation describes how individual requirements meet the
business need for the project. Requirement documentation does not contain project
objectives.
- **C Physical resource assignments**
Incorrect. Physical resource assignments are project documents that contain information
about the material, equipment, supplies, locations, and other physical resources that will be
used during the project. Physical resource assignments are not inputs of the Close Project
or Phase process nor are they used to understand whether the project objectives are met
before considering the project closed.
- **D Summary of the kick-off meeting**
Incorrect. The purpose of the kick-off meeting is to communicate the objectives of the
project, gain the commitment of the team for the project, and explain the roles and
responsibilities of each stakeholder. The summary of this meeting does not document the
criteria against which the project performance is measured, and it does not contain a
determination of whether project objectives are met.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 123, 125

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 67 of 200
Question ID: 613228
In your organization, the Manage Quality process has been a weakness in past projects. You want
to ensure that this process is implemented properly on your current project.
On which of the following would you focus the most to achieve this goal?
Top of Form
- **A Design an optimal, mature product and build confidence that future outputs will meet specified**
requirements
- **B Confirm that quality processes are used in a consistent manner and maximize project profitability**
for the organization
- **C Design an optimal, mature product and build confidence that future outputs will exceed specified**
requirements
- **D Improve the effectiveness of processes and confirm that quality processes are used by a majority**
of the team
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which goals are consistent with the PMBOK® Guide concept of project quality management?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The four goals of the Manage Quality process are:

---

● Design an optimal and mature product by implementing specific design guidelines,
● Build confidence that a future output will be completed in a manner that meets the specified
requirements and expectations,
● Confirm that the quality processes are used and that their use meets the quality objectives of
the project, and
● Improve the efficiency and effectiveness of processes and activities.
Maximizing profits and exceeding expectations may be corporate goals outside the project, but
neither are project management goals.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Design an optimal, mature product and build confidence that future outputs will meet**
specified requirements
Correct. Designing an optimal, mature product by implementing specific design guidelines
that address specific aspects of the project is one of the four goals of the Manage Quality
process. Building confidence that a future output will meet specified requirements is
another.
- **B Confirm that quality processes are used in a consistent manner and maximize project**
profitability for the organization
Incorrect. While confirming that quality processes are used is a goal of the Manage Quality
process, maximizing project profitability is not a goal of this process.
- **C Design an optimal, mature product and build confidence that future outputs will exceed**
specified requirements
Incorrect. Although designing an optimal, mature product by implementing specific design
guidelines is a goal of the Manage Quality process, exceeding requirements and
expectations is not a goal of this process. Quality is defined as the degree to which
requirements are met, not exceeded.
- **D Improve the effectiveness of processes and confirm that quality processes are used by a**
majority of the team
Incorrect. Improving the efficiency and effectiveness of processes is a goal of the Manage
Quality process; however, confirming that a majority of the team is using quality processes
is not. Because quality is the responsibility of everyone involved with the project, the goal is
to ensure everyone is using the appropriate quality processes.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page 290
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 68 of 200
Question ID: 612021
You are leading a project in a small startup company with decentralized purchasing. A supplier
informs you that they have excess inventory that can be purchased at a reduced price. You review
the project's inventory needs and find that most of the excess inventory offered by the supplier
can be used for the project.
What is your best course of action?
Top of Form
- **A Refer the supplier to the project sponsor for procurement**
- **B Negotiate and sign a procurement contract with the supplier**
- **C Refer the supplier to the procurement department**
- **D Refer the supplier to the project management office (PMO)**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How does decentralized purchasing affect your authority?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Decentralized purchasing is found in smaller organizations or startup companies, and those
without a purchasing, contracting, or procurement department. In such organizations, the project
manager may assume the purchasing authority role to negotiate and sign contracts directly. For
larger organizations with centralized purchasing, the actual procurement and contracting

---

functions may be carried out by a separate department whose role is to purchase, negotiate, and
sign contracts. In the scenario described, your company has decentralized purchasing. When a
supplier offers you discounted goods, you have the authority to complete the purchase.
Therefore, the next thing you should do is negotiate and sign the contract for the procurement of
the discounted supplies.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Refer the supplier to the project sponsor for procurement**
Incorrect. While you may want to discuss the procurement with the project sponsor, in a
decentralized purchasing environment, the project manager may assume the authority to
negotiate and sign contracts directly. Therefore, you would not need to involve the sponsor
in the procurement.
- **B Negotiate and sign a procurement contract with the supplier**
Correct. Your company uses decentralized purchasing, which means there is not a
purchasing, contracting, or procurement department. Therefore, negotiating and signing a
procurement contract with the supplier would be your best course of action.
- **C Refer the supplier to the procurement department**
Incorrect. A company with decentralized purchasing does not have a procurement
department. The project manager has the authority to negotiate and sign purchasing
agreements directly.
- **D Refer the supplier to the project management office (PMO)**
Incorrect. The PMO can centralize and standardize the management of projects. While
PMOs vary as to what role play in the organization, PMOs are typically not involved in
conducting procurements.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 462

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 69 of 200
Question ID: 650204
- **A project has been running smoothly and is well ahead of schedule. Despite a forecast which**
indicates that the project will finish within budget, the available capital for the project has been
exhausted, and the project activities must be suspended.
What might have prevented this situation?
Top of Form
- **A Performing a funding limit reconciliation**
- **B Including sufficient contingency reserves in the cost baseline**
- **C Providing an adequate project budget**
- **D Borrowing at a fixed interest rate rather than a variable rate**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Funding often occurs in incremental amounts.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

- **A funding limit reconciliation is a process of comparing the planned expenditure of project funds**
against any limits on the commitment of funds for the project to identify any variances between
the funding limits and the planned expenditures. The expenditure of funds should be reconciled
with any funding limits on the commitment of funds for the project. A variance between the
funding limits and the planned expenditures will sometimes necessitate the rescheduling of work

---

to level out the rate of expenditures. This is accomplished by placing imposed date constraints
for work into the project schedule.
In this scenario, the project is running well ahead of budget, which suggests that project funds
are being expended faster than anticipated. Project funding often occurs in incremental amounts.
While the project budget may be adequate for the project, if capital is expended faster than the
rate it is being provided for the project, the project could run out of 'available' capital. Therefore,
performing a funding limit reconciliation might have prevented this situation.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Performing a funding limit reconciliation**
Correct. Funding often occurs in incremental amounts. A variance between the funding
limits and the planned expenditures will sometimes necessitate the rescheduling of work to
level out the rate of expenditures. This is accomplished by placing imposed date constraints
for work into the project schedule.
- **B Including sufficient contingency reserves in the cost baseline**
Incorrect. Contingency reserves are time or money allocated in the schedule or cost
baseline for known risks with active response strategies. The question does not describe
any realized risks for which the contingency reserves were inadequate. Additionally, the
fact that the project is forecast to complete within budget suggests that contingency
reserves were sufficient.
- **C Providing an adequate project budget**
Incorrect. The question states that the project is forecast to finish within budget. Therefore,
the problem does not reside with the project budget.
- **D Borrowing at a fixed interest rate rather than a variable rate**
Incorrect. Assuming the project was funded by borrowing at a variable interest rate, an
extreme spike in interest rates would increase project expenses. However, the question
states that the project is anticipated to finish within budget. Therefore, in this scenario,
rising interest rates are not likely to be the cause for the project running out of available
funds.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 253

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 70 of 200
Question ID: 651338
The third iteration of the project has started. The team begins every day with a 15-minute stand
up meeting.
What is the primary value in such an arrangement?
Top of Form
- **A Forces the team members to be at the office at the beginning of each working day**
- **B Aligns the iteration with overall project road map to ensure appropriate velocity**
- **C Assists the team to communicate evolving details, needs, and status with greater frequency**
- **D Aids the team in assigning resources and responsibilities to the work scheduled for the day**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is gained from meeting as a team every day?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Stand up meetings are a valuable element of any project's communication plan. Regardless of the
determined frequency, length, and structure, conducting a reoccurring meeting amongst project
stakeholders can increase communication about issues, evolving trends, status, and many other
relevant discussions. Typically, in agile projects, these meetings are held daily for a timeboxed
15-minute time period and conducted standing up in a physically shared space.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Forces the team members to be at the office at the beginning of each working day**
Incorrect. The primary goal of daily stand up meetings is not to enforce attendance and
reprimand non-attendance. It acts as a way for the whole team to meet for a quick status
update, to coordinate, and to set the context for the day's work.
- **B Aligns the iteration with overall project road map to ensure appropriate velocity**
Incorrect. The primary purpose of the daily stand up meeting is not to align the iteration to
the project's road map. That effort is part of the iteration planning.
- **C Assists the team to communicate evolving details, needs, and status with greater frequency**
Correct. The daily stand up meetings foster communication in regularity to communicate
evolving details, status, and needs
- **D Aids the team in assigning resources and responsibilities to the work scheduled for the day**
Incorrect. This choice describes what may be an indirect outcome of some daily standup
meetings, but it is not the primary purpose of these meetings. Generally, resources and
responsibilities are not assigned through the daily stand up meetings. In some teams, they
are assigned as part of other planning meetings, or they are already assigned through the
user stories or pulled via a Kanban board.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 364, 386
Agile Practice Guide - First Edition, Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 53

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 71 of 200
Question ID: 613645
You are preparing to perform multiple iterations of your quantitative cost-schedule risk analysis
to evaluate the effects of individual project risks and other uncertainty sources to determine a
range of probable outcomes and risks for your project.
What analysis type will you use?
Top of Form
- **A Decision tree analysis**
- **B Alternatives analysis**
- **C Monte Carlo analysis**
- **D Sensitivity analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which analysis type uses software to simulate several thousand iterations of the project to
achieve a range of probable outcomes.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The Monte Carlo analysis uses iterative analysis to simulate the likelihood of a particular
outcome or risk associated with the project. Computer software is typically used to simulate
project activity several thousand times using random input for each iteration resulting in a range

---

of possible outcomes. This allows project managers the ability to evaluate and address risks
based on the probability distribution.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Decision tree analysis**
Incorrect. Decision tree analysis does not use multiple iterations to predict the possible
outcomes within a certain range. It instead shows several alternative paths, each with
associated costs and potential risks to assist in selecting the best course of action.
- **B Alternatives analysis**
Incorrect. Alternative analysis is a tool or technique used in several processes. This
analysis is a simple comparison of identified options used to select the best option for risk
response or the best approach for executing and performing the work of the project. It is
not an analysis designated to perform complex cost, schedule and probability evaluations.
- **C Monte Carlo analysis**
Correct. The Monte Carlo analysis uses a model to simulate the combined effect of
individual project risks and other sources of uncertainty to evaluate the potential impact on
achieving project objectives. The simulation involves several thousand iterations to
produce a range of possible outcomes.
- **D Sensitivity analysis**
Incorrect. The sensitivity analysis helps determine which projects risk or uncertainty
sources have the most potential impact on project outcomes. Rather than determining
outcomes and risks, this analysis correlates variations in elements of quantitative risk
analysis (Monte Carlo analysis) with variations in project outcomes.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 433

Question 72 of 200
Question ID: 612262
As a new project manager, you have just been assigned to a project and asked by the project
sponsor to create a draft of the project charter. The company has a project management office
(PMO), which is best described as supportive.
Unsure of the format the project charter should take, what should you do first?
Top of Form
- **A Since every project is unique, you should create the project charter from scratch**
- **B Download a project charter template from the Internet**
- **C Ask the PMO to prepare the project charter**
- **D Check the organizational process assets (OPAs)**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where is the best place to find an approved template for a project charter?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question states that you, as the project manager, need to create a project charter and are
unsure of the correct format. You should search for an approved version of a project charter
template that can serve as a starting point for the development of the project charter. Your
organizational process assets, e.g., the organizational knowledge bases would be a good place to
search for an approved version of a project charter template.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Since every project is unique, you should create the project charter from scratch**
Incorrect. Every project is unique, but it is beneficial to use the project charter template as
a starting point, which will save time and effort in the creation of the project charter.
- **B Download a project charter template from the Internet**
Incorrect. The Internet is a source for project management templates, including the project
charter. However, it is best to check internal resources for an approved version of a project
charter template first.
- **C Ask the PMO to prepare the project charter**
Incorrect. Although a supportive PMO may provide an approved project charter template
for you to use, but it is not likely to prepare the document for you, as the project manager.
- **D Check the organizational process assets (OPAs)**
Correct. The OPAs would likely have an approved version of a project charter template,
which can serve as a starting point for the development of the project charter.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**

Question 73 of 200
Question ID: 613051
- **A project manager is working with the team to ensure that all open issues are resolved and all**
deliverables have been accepted by the customer.
What process is the project manager conducting?
Top of Form
- **A Accept Project Deliverables**
- **B Control Procurements**
- **C Close Project or Phase**
- **D Manage Team**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project manager is in the process of finalizing all activities for the project.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question indicates that the project manager is ensuring all issues have been resolved and the
deliverables have been accepted. Accepted deliverables are an output from the Validate Scope
process, and the formal documentation of acceptance is forwarded to the Close Project or Phase
process. The project manager then verifies that all deliverables have been accepted as part of
project closure. Additionally, during project closure, the project manager reviews the issue log to

---

ensure that there are no open issues. Therefore, of the available choices, the Close Project or
Phase process is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Accept Project Deliverables**
Incorrect. 'Accept Project Deliverables' is not a project management process specified in
the PMBOK® Guide.
- **B Control Procurements**
Incorrect. There is not enough information in the question to determine if the project
involved vendors that would have then required сarrying out procurement-related
processes.
- **C Close Project or Phase**
Correct. Ensuring the deliverables are accepted and all open issues resolved is part of the
Close Project or Phase process.
- **D Manage Team**
Incorrect. Manage Team is the process of tracking team member performance, providing
feedback, resolving issues, and managing team changes to optimize project performance.
While the scenario indicates the project manager works with the team, the essence of this
work is focused on ensuring the issues are resolved and the deliverables accepted.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 123

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 74 of 200
Question ID: 612726
- **A project team is identifying and documenting the actions necessary to produce the project**
deliverables.
Which of the following may be created as a result of this process?
Top of Form
- **A Test and evaluation documents**
- **B The scope baseline**
- **C Resource breakdown structure**
- **D A milestone list**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Define Activities is the process of decomposing work packages into schedule activities.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Define Activities is the process of identifying and documenting the actions necessary to produce
the project deliverables. In this process, work packages are broken down into schedule activities
that provide a basis for estimating, scheduling, executing, monitoring and controlling project
work. The question reads, "Which of the following may be created as a result of this process?" In
other words, the question is asking to identify an output from the Define Activities process. Of

---

the choices provided, only the milestone list is one of the outputs of that process and is,
therefore, the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Test and evaluation documents**
Incorrect. Test and evaluation documents are project documents that describe the activities
used to determine if the product meets the quality objectives stated in the quality
management plan. These documents are created as an output of the Manage Quality
process, while according to the scenario, the project team is involved in the Define
Activities process.
- **B The scope baseline**
Incorrect. The scope baseline is the approved version of the scope statement, WBS, and the
WBS dictionary. As implied by the scenario, the project team is in the Define Activities
process. The scope baseline is an input to this process, while the question is asking about
an output.
- **C Resource breakdown structure**
Incorrect. The resource breakdown structure is a hierarchical representation of resources
by category and type. This document is created as an output of the Estimate Activity
Resources process while the scenario implies the Define Activities process is underway.
- **D A milestone list**
Correct. A milestone list identifies all project milestones and indicates whether the
milestone is mandatory, such as those required by contract, or optional, such as those
based on historical information. Milestones are similar to regular schedule activities, but
they have zero duration because they represent a significant point or event. A milestone list
is one of the possible outputs of the Define Activities process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 186

Question 75 of 200
Question ID: 613647
The sponsor informs you that the project charter you developed has been approved.
What should be your top priority at this point?
Top of Form
- **A Identifying project stakeholders**
- **B Acquiring the project team**
- **C Defining the project scope**
- **D Identifying project benefits**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Doing this early and often can increase the potential for project success.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The fact the project charter has just been approved implies the project is in initiation. Unless
stated otherwise in the scenario, the next logical step is stakeholder identification. Successfully
identifying, analyzing, and engaging stakeholders and effectively managing their expectations
and participation throughout the project life cycle is critical to project success. The ability of the
project manager to correctly identify and engage stakeholders in an appropriate way can mean
the difference between project success and failure. To increase the chances of success, the
process of stakeholder identification should commence as soon as possible after the project

---

charter has been approved and the project manager assigned. In the scenario described, the
project charter that was developed by the project manager has been approved. Therefore, of the
choices provided, Identifying project stakeholders is the top priority for the project manager.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Identifying project stakeholders**
Correct. A key concept for stakeholder management is identifying and engaging
stakeholders as soon as possible after the project charter is approved, the project manager
has been assigned, and the team begins to form. Engaging stakeholders early increases the
chances of project success and support from the stakeholder community.
- **B Acquiring the project team**
Incorrect. According to the scenario, the project is in the initiation, and the project charter
has just been approved. The next logical step is identifying stakeholders. While it is
possible that some of the project team members are acquired during project initiation using
the pre-assignment technique, nothing in the scenario suggests that pre-assigning team
members is more important than identifying stakeholders.
- **C Defining the project scope**
Incorrect. The project scope is defined as part of project planning, while according to the
scenario the project is still in initiation.
- **D Identifying project benefits**
Incorrect. Project benefits are identified and documented in the benefits management plan
which serves as one of the inputs to the Develop Project Charter process. The scenario
implies the project charter has already been approved, implying the project benefits have
been identified.

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 76 of 200
Question ID: 612366
- **A team leader informs the project manager that she does not have enough resources to fix a**
defect by the deadline.
In what project document would a project manager first record the lack of resources?
Top of Form
- **A Risk register**
- **B Physical resource assignments**
- **C Project team assignments**
- **D Issue log**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is a lack of resources?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

- **A lack of resources is an issue that should first be recorded in the project's issue log. The issue**
log is used to identify issues such as lack of resources, delays in supplies, low grades of raw
material, or any other condition or situation that may have an impact on the project objectives.
Corrective action as a result of a lack of resources may include updates to project management
plan or project documents, such as a risk register, physical resources assignments, and project

---

team assignments. Therefore, among the choices offered, capturing the lack of resources in the
issue log is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register is a project document created as part of the Identify Risks
process that provides information on threats and opportunities that may impact project
execution. It is unclear from the scenario whether or not the lack of resources is already
identified as a risk and on the risk register and, if not, whether the lack of resources should
be added to the risk register as part of the Monitor Risks process. In either case, the
resource issue should first be recorded in the issue log, so that the resource issue can be
investigated and perhaps resolved before further action is taken.
- **B Physical resource assignments**
Incorrect. Physical resources assignments is a project document that is created as an output
from the Acquire Resources process and records the material, equipment, supplies,
locations, and other physical resources that will be used during the project. The physical
resource assignments document describes the current state of resources assignments and
does not account for the lack of resources. Also, the scenario describes a situation during
monitoring and controlling processes, and Acquire Resources process is an executing
process.
- **C Project team assignments**
Incorrect. Project team assignments is an output of the Acquire Resources process that
records the team members and their roles and responsibilities for the project. Project team
assignments could include a project team directory, but it would not account for lack of
resources. Also, the scenario describes a situation during monitoring and controlling
processes, and Acquire Resources process is an executing process.
- **D Issue log**
Correct. The issue log is a project document where all the issues are recorded and tracked,
including resource related issues such as a lack of resources. The issue log will help the
project manager effectively track and manage issues, ensuring that they are investigated
and resolved. The issue log is updated as a result of monitoring and control activities
throughout the project's life cycle.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 354
Bottom of Form
