Question 77 of 200
Question ID: 612637
- **A project manager has gathered and reviewed the inputs necessary to begin the development of**
the scope management plan for a project to build a new residential complex.
What is the best course of action for the project manager to complete this process?
Top of Form
- **A Analyze stakeholders using the stakeholder engagement assessment matrix**
- **B Schedule a meeting with subject matter experts who have knowledge in construction**
- **C Define the actions and activities necessary to satisfy the exit criteria for the project**
- **D Have the procurement department send the bid documents to prospective sellers**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer choice describes tools and techniques that may be used during the Plan Scope
Management process?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the Plan Scope Management process is being performed with the
development of the scope management plan. Two of the tools and techniques associated with the
Plan Scope Management process include expert judgment and meetings. Expertise should be
considered from individuals or groups with specialized knowledge or training in the industry,
discipline, or application area relevant to the project. For example, in the scenario provided, the

---

project is supposed to build a new residential complex, implying construction is the relevant
industry. Therefore, holding a meeting with subject matter experts who have knowledge in
construction covers both tools and techniques mentioned above, expert judgment applicable to
the project and meetings. Therefore, of the available options, to complete the Plan Scope
Management process process described in the scenario, scheduling a meeting with subject matter
experts who have knowledge in construction is the best course of action for the project manager.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Analyze stakeholders using the stakeholder engagement assessment matrix**
Incorrect. The stakeholder engagement assessment matrix is a project document that
compares current and desired stakeholder engagement levels. Stakeholder analysis is part
of the Plan Stakeholder Engagement process, while based on the scenario described, the
project manager is developing the scope management plan.
- **B Schedule a meeting with subject matter experts who have knowledge in construction**
Correct. This answer choice describes two of the tools and techniques, which may be
beneficial in the development of the scope management plan, including expert judgment
and meetings.
- **C Define the actions and activities necessary to satisfy the exit criteria for the project**
Incorrect. Actions and activities necessary to satisfy the exit criteria for the project are
defined in the project charter and carried out as part of the Close Project or Phase process,
while the scenario describes the project manager who is developing the scope management
plan.
- **D Have the procurement department send the bid documents to prospective sellers**
Incorrect. Bid documents are used to solicit proposals from prospective sellers. According
to the scenario, the project is in planning. While the bid documents are developed during
project planning, the project manager is carrying out one of the Project Scope Management
Knowledge Area's processes, rather than one of the Project Procurement Management
Knowledge Area's processes.

- **A project manager is about to start the development of the project charter and needs to identify**

What tool or technique might be useful in gathering information on high-level assumptions and
constraints?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

charter, which implies that the Develop Project Charter process is just getting started. Interviews,
which is a data gathering technique, may be used during the Develop Project Charter process to
gather information on high-level requirements, assumptions or constraints, approval criteria, and
other information from stakeholders by talking to them directly. Therefore, of the available

---

choices, conducting interviews with the project sponsor and other relevant stakeholders is the
best answer to the question asked.

the assumption log is not available to serve as a source of information at this point in the
process.
- **B Conduct interviews with the project sponsor and other relevant stakeholders**

Project Charter process to gather information on high-level requirements, assumptions or
constraints, approval criteria, and other information from stakeholders by talking to them
directly.
- **C Analyze the risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register is created as an output of the Identify Risks process, which
occurs during project planning, whereas the question suggests that the project is still in the
initiation stage with the development of the project charter.
- **D Perform the Qualitative Risk Analysis process since the assumption log is an output of this**
process
Incorrect. The assumption log is an output of the Develop Project Charter process rather
than the Perform the Qualitative Risk Analysis process.

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 79 of 200
Question ID: 613117
You need to hire one contractor. You are leaning toward one who has an 80% chance of
delivering in one month with a cost of $5,000, and a 20% chance of delivering in two months
with a cost of $10,000. Another contractor has a 90% chance of delivering in one month with a
cost of $6,000, and a 10% chance of delivering in two months with a cost of $12,000.
What technique would you use to select the contractor?
Top of Form
- **A Monte Carlo analysis**
- **B Sensitivity analysis**
- **C Decision tree analysis**
- **D Influence analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

In this case, you have the quantified probabilities and impacts of the chances that two different
vendors will deliver in one month or two. Only one of the choices shown has a technique that
uses all that information to quantify risk.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Of the data analysis techniques used for the Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis process, only
decision trees are used to support the selection of several different courses of action, each of

---

which has potential opportunities and threats. The decision tree is evaluated by calculating the
expected monetary value of each branch, which involves multiplying the probability by the
impact of each chance and adding the results together.
In this scenario, you have the quantified probabilities and impacts of the chances that two
different vendors will deliver in one month or two. You can calculate the expected monetary
value (EMV) of each vendor's risks, and select the vendor with the highest EMV.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Monte Carlo analysis**
Incorrect. Monte Carlo analysis is a form of simulation, which is one of the data analysis
techniques used for the Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis process. However, the Monte
Carlo analysis simulates the combined effects of individual project risks or other sources of
uncertainty to output the probability of certain events occurring and the level of confidence
that a specific event will occur. The information given in the question is not enough to
complete a Monte Carlo analysis.
- **B Sensitivity analysis**
Incorrect. Sensitivity analysis helps to determine, which individual project risks or other
sources of uncertainty have the most potential impact on project outcomes. A typical
display of sensitivity analysis is the tornado diagram, which presents the correlation
coefficient for each risk that can influence the project outcome. The information given in
the question is not enough to complete a tornado diagram.
- **C Decision tree analysis**
Correct. Decision trees are used to support the selection of several different courses of
action, each of which has potential opportunities and threats. In this case, you have the
quantified probabilities and impacts of the chances that two different vendors will deliver in
one month or two. You can calculate the expected monetary value (EMV) of each vendor's
risks, and select the vendor with the highest EMV.
- **D Influence analysis**
Incorrect. Influence analysis is not a technique named in the PMBOK® Guide. On the
other hand, influence diagrams are one of the data analysis techniques that can be used in
the Perform Quantitative Risk Analysis process to represent a set of entities, outcomes, and
influences. The influence diagram can use ranges or probability distributions to represent
uncertainty. However, the information given in the question is not enough to complete an
influence diagram.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 435
Bottom of Form
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Bottom of Form Prev Next

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 80 of 200
Question ID: 612651
- **A company has been awarded a contract to design and build a new drone. The project manager is**
in the process of collecting product and project requirements.
Which of the following actions is least likely to be performed during this process?
Top of Form
- **A Determining if the performing organization has the infrastructure required to construct the drone**
- **B Studying the scope baseline for detailed product requirements**
- **C Researching knowledge gained from previous similar projects**
- **D Reviewing the contract for any product or project requirements**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The Create WBS process occurs after the Collect Requirements and Define Scope processes
have been completed.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the Collect Requirements process is being conducted. The incorrect
answer choices all represent actions that may be associated with inputs for the Collect
Requirements process. Note that the question is asking for the activity which is 'least' likely to be
performed during the Collect Requirements process. The scope baseline is the approved version
of a scope statement, work breakdown structure (WBS), and its associated WBS dictionary. The

---

scope baseline is created as an output of the Create WBS process which occurs after the Collect
Requirements and Define Scope processes have been completed. Thus, the scope baseline is not
yet available to serve as an input into the Collect Requirements process. Therefore, among the
available options, studying the scope baseline for detailed product requirements is the 'least'
likely action to be performed as part of the Collect Requirements process.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Determining if the performing organization has the infrastructure required to construct the**
drone
Incorrect. This answer choice describes an activity associated with the enterprise
environmental factors which may influence the Collect Requirements process. Enterprise
environmental factors including infrastructure may serve as an input into the Collect
Requirements process.
- **B Studying the scope baseline for detailed product requirements**
Correct. The scope baseline is created as an output of the Create WBS process which
occurs after the Collect Requirements and Define Scope processes have been completed.
Therefore, this answer choice describes an action that is 'least' likely to be performed as
part of the Collect Requirements process described by the question.
- **C Researching knowledge gained from previous similar projects**
Incorrect. This answer choice describes an activity associated with the lessons learned
repository. The lessons learned repository is a store of historical information about lessons
learned from past projects. The lessons learned repository is one of the organizational
process assets which may serve as an input to the Collect Requirements process.
- **D Reviewing the contract for any product or project requirements**
Incorrect. The question indicates that the performing organization has been contracted to
design and build the consumer drone. Therefore, an agreement must exist which may serve
as an important input into the Collect Requirements process. The contract should have
relevant information for product and project requirements which are needed for the Collect
Requirements process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 138, 141

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 81 of 200
Question ID: 625136
According to the original plan for a project, the first two activities (Select Site and Negotiate
Lease) should have been 100% complete, and the third activity (Perform Civil Works) should
have been 50% complete at this point in the project. However, only the first two activities have
been completed, and no work has been done on the third activity. The method used to determine
the earned value is based on percent complete.
Based on the following Gantt chart, what is the project's current CPI?
Top of Form
- **A 0.83**
- **B 1.2**
- **C 0.5**
- **D -$2,000**

---

Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The cost performance index (CPI) is earned value (EV) divided by actual cost (AC).
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The cost performance index (CPI) is earned value (EV) divided by actual cost (AC): CPI = EV /
AC. The EV is the sum of the planned value of the completed work. In the scenario described,
the first two activities with $5,000 value have been completed so far in the project, so the EV =
$5,000 + $5,000 = $10,000. The actual cost for each activity is provided in the chart and can be
calculated as the sum of the actual costs of the first two activities valued at $6,000 each, so the
AC = $6,000 + $6,000 = $12,000. Note, since the scenario mentions that the method used to
determine the earned value is based on percent complete, the earned value of a partially
completed work package is calculated by multiplying the planned value of the work package by
its the percent complete.
The calculations are as follows:
CPI = EV / AC
EV = EV of activity 1 + EV of activity 2 = $5,000 + $5,000 = $10,000
AC = AC of activity 1 + AC of activity 2 = $6,000 + $6,000 = $12,000
CPI = EV / AC = $10,000 / $12,000 = 0.83
Therefore, the correct answer for CPI is 0.83.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A 0.83**
Correct. The cost performance index (CPI) is earned value (EV) divided by actual cost
(AC). The EV is the sum of the planned value of the completed work. The first two activities
were planned at $5,000 each, so the EV is $10,000. The actual cost is provided in the chart
at $12,000. Therefore, CPI = EV / AC = $10,000 / $12,000 = 0.83
- **B 1.2**
Incorrect. The cost performance index (CPI) is earned value (EV) divided by actual cost
(AC). The value of 1.2 provided in this answer choice is a result of the incorrectly applied
formula where the numerator and denominator are transposed.

---

- **C 0.5**
Incorrect. The value of 0.5 in this answer choice represents the schedule performance index
(SPI) which is the earned value (EV) divided by the planned value (PV). SPI = $10,000 /
$20,000 = 0.5. However, the question is asking for the CPI and not the SPI.
- **D -$2,000**
Incorrect. The value of -$2,000 in this answer choice represents the cost variance (CV)
which is the earned value (EV) minus actual cost (AC). CV = EV - AC = $10,000 - $12,000
= -$2,000. However, the question is asking for the CPI and not the CV.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 263, 267
Practice Standard for Earned Value Management - Second Edition, Project Management
Institute Inc., 2011, Page(s) 38-39
https://www.project-management-prepcast.com/pmp-formulas

PMP Exam Simulator

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 82 of 200
Question ID: 612843
You are managing a project with extensive regulatory oversight. The project is behind schedule,
and a team member has proposed a way to automate the key inspections of the deliverable,
saving considerable time and likely putting the project back on schedule. Unfortunately, only one
team member is certified to run the automated test equipment, and certifying additional people
will take a long time.
What should you do?
Top of Form
- **A Reject the automation option because it is unacceptable to add risk to a project in a highly**
regulated environment
- **B Exploit the opportunity by taking advantage of the automation option, update the risk register,**
and determine the most appropriate risk response
- **C Get the project back on schedule by requiring the inspection team to increase productivity by**
adding overtime
- **D Inform the sponsor that the organization has failed to provide enough key staff and that the**
project will be seriously delayed
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How should the project manager act when the project is experiencing challenges?
Correct Answer: B

---


**Explanation:**

The scenario implies that the Manage Quality process is being performed. Your team has
identified a way to exploit the inspection issue by introducing automation. However, this
introduces a secondary threat posed by having a single certified operator. The project manager
should handle this like any other risk: record it in the risk register, determine the best response
option, and move forward proactively.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Reject the automation option because it is unacceptable to add risk to a project in a highly**
regulated environment
Incorrect. Proactively managing risk is an important part of the project managers role in
any environment. This includes handling opportunities such as automation and threats such
as staffing issues.
- **B Exploit the opportunity by taking advantage of the automation option, update the risk**
register, and determine the most appropriate risk response
Correct. Your team has identified a way to exploit the inspection issue by automation.
However, you must immediately record the threat posed by having a single certified
operator and find the best way to avoid, mitigate, or transfer the risk.
- **C Get the project back on schedule by requiring the inspection team to increase productivity**
by adding overtime
Incorrect. The inspection team has already been appropriately trained and tasked per the
provisions of the quality management plan. Forcing them to work overtime will likely result
in resentment, lower morale, and may lead to attrition.
- **D Inform the sponsor that the organization has failed to provide enough key staff and that the**
project will be seriously delayed
Incorrect. In situations that are within the authority of the project manager (which is likely
the case here), it is the project manager's responsibility to find options, make
recommendations, and take action. Playing the blame game is not an appropriate response.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 297, 417, 439

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 83 of 200
Question ID: 612674
- **A client has just rejected the deliverables stating that they do not meet the intended need. The**
project manager realizes that the customer's requirements were not clearly understood.
How could the project manager have avoided this situation?
Top of Form
- **A Conducted an inspection of the deliverables during the Validate Scope process**
- **B Validated the deliverables before they are verified**
- **C Conducted the Validate Scope process before the Control Quality process**
- **D Collaborated with a business analysis professional**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer choice represents an action that might have better aligned the project requirements
with the client's business needs?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Eliciting, documenting, and managing stakeholder requirements takes place within the Project
Scope Management processes. Trends and emerging practices for Project Scope Management
include a focus on collaborating with business analysis professionals to elicit, document, and
manage stakeholder requirements to meet project objectives. When a business analyst is assigned
to a project, requirement-related activities become the responsibility of that role. Utilizing the

---

expertise of a business analyst, in this scenario, most likely would have created better alignment
between the project requirements and the business need for the client.
The incorrect answer choices represent actions, which would not have influenced how the
requirements were gathered. The scenario describes the Validate Scope process in action. In
terms of sequence, typically the Control Quality occurs prior to Validate Scope. Control Quality
has verified deliverables as outputs. Validate Scope in turn, utilizes verified deliverables as
inputs and results in accepted deliverables or change requests in case defect repair or other
changes are required. Therefore, of the available options, collaborating with a business analysis
professional is the best response.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Conducted an inspection of the deliverables during the Validate Scope process**
Incorrect. During the Validate Scope process, the verified deliverables are inspected by the
customer to determine if the deliverables meet requirements and product acceptance
criteria. This scenario describes the Validate Scope process activities in action and
therefore this choice is not the way to prevent the client from rejecting the deliverable.
- **B Validated the deliverables before they are verified**
Incorrect. Verified deliverables are project deliverables that are completed and checked for
correctness through the Control Quality process. The verified deliverables serve as an input
into the Validate Scope process. Validating the deliverables before they are verified would
mean the deliverables would not be checked for correctness prior to seeking approval from
the client.
- **C Conducted the Validate Scope process before the Control Quality process**
Incorrect. The Control Quality process is generally performed before the Validate Scope
process, although the two processes may be performed in parallel. The deliverables are
verified as part of the Control Quality process, and then the verified deliverables serve as
an input into the Validate Scope process. Thus, the Validate Scope process should never
precede the Control Quality process.
- **D Collaborated with a business analysis professional**
Correct. Trends and emerging practices for Project Scope Management include a focus on
collaborating with business analysis professionals to elicit, document, and manage
stakeholder requirements in order to meet project objectives. Utilizing the expertise of a
business analyst most likely would have created better alignment between the project
requirements and the business need for the client.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 132

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 84 of 200
Question ID: 612239
An agile software development project consists of four releases, with features incrementally
added with each release. Due to an excessive number of defects found by users after the first
release, the risk response plan was implemented, which involved more rigorous testing by the
project team. After the second release, the client has reported two bugs.
What must first be done to determine the effectiveness of the implemented risk response?
Top of Form
- **A Schedule a release retrospective**
- **B Complete a sensitivity analysis**
- **C Conduct technical performance analysis**
- **D Perform a reserve analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How should the project manager compare actual results against targets?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Technical performance analysis compares technical accomplishments during project execution to
the schedule of technical achievement. It requires the definition of objective, quantifiable
measures of technical performance, which can be used to compare actual results against targets.
Such technical performance measures may include weight, transaction times, number of

---

delivered defects, storage capacity, etc. In this scenario, technical performance analysis should be
used to compare actual results, such as delivered defects, against performance targets. The next
logical step is to conduct technical performance analysis.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Schedule a release retrospective**
Incorrect. A release retrospective is a scheduled review to record lessons learned from a
release. Knowledge gained may include the effectiveness of a risk response to a realized
risk. However, an analysis must first be performed on the data regarding delivered defects
before any conclusions can be drawn regarding the effectiveness of the risk response.
- **B Complete a sensitivity analysis**
Incorrect. Sensitivity analysis is an analysis technique to determine which individual
project risks or other sources of uncertainty have the most potential impact on project
outcomes, by correlating variations in project outcomes with variations in elements of a
quantitative risk analysis model. A sensitivity analysis is not used to determine the
effectiveness of a risk response.
- **C Conduct technical performance analysis**
Correct. Technical performance analysis can be used to compare actual results, such as
delivered defects, against targets. The results of the technical performance analysis can
provide context for the raw data that has been collected.
- **D Perform a reserve analysis**
Incorrect. Reserve analysis may be performed to determine if the remaining reserves are
sufficient for the risk remaining in the project. The question is asking about the
effectiveness of a risk response rather than an evaluation of the remaining reserves.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 456

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 85 of 200
Question ID: 650601
- **A project manager is in the process of determining the budget for a new project that will acquire**
specialty parts from an overseas vendor to reduce the cost. Recently, the government of the
country where the vendor is located announced a change in economic policy that involves
sharply increasing their money supply to stimulate their economy.
What should the project manager do in this situation?
Top of Form
- **A Modify the business case**
- **B Increase the management reserves**
- **C Account for changes in the exchange rates**
- **D Change the organization's budget policies**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How might changes in economic policy affect the cost of goods acquired from foreign countries?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Any significant changes in a country's economic policy would likely affect the currency
exchange rates. As a result, the cost of goods bought from that country would also change. When
relying on goods from abroad, the fluctuations of currencies need to be understood and built into

---

the Determine Budget process. Therefore, in this situation, the project manager needs to account
for changes in the exchange rates when determining the project budget.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Modify the business case**
Incorrect. The business case for the project may be affected by a change in the economic
policy of a country where a key vendor is located. However, the project sponsor, not the
project manager, typically develops and maintains the business case.
- **B Increase the management reserves**
Incorrect. Management reserves are set aside to address project risks that are unforeseen,
otherwise referred to as unknown-unknowns. The question describes a situation which is
known, and the project manager should address this risk with a planned risk response that
may include establishing contingency reserves, not management reserves.
- **C Account for changes in the exchange rates**
Correct. Changes in a country’s economic condition can cause fluctuations in exchange
rates. Changes in exchange rates will affect the cost of goods purchased overseas. The
project manager will need to account for these fluctuations in exchange rates when
determining the project budget.
- **D Change the organization's budget policies**
Incorrect. Budgeting policies define how the budget is developed. The scenario does not
suggest that there is an issue with the organization's budget policies. Additionally, the
project manager may make recommendations but does not likely have the authority to
change the organization's budget policies.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 251

Question 86 of 200
Question ID: 613751
As part of the planning process, the project manager conducts a meeting with some of the key
stakeholders. The purpose of the meeting is to identify the risks associated with the new project.
The meeting is highly productive with all members making valuable contributions. At the
conclusion of the meeting, a list of risks and potential risk owners has been identified.
Where should the project manager capture this information?
Top of Form
- **A RACI chart**
- **B Requirements traceability matrix**
- **C Risk register**
- **D Risk assessment log**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What output of the Identify Risks process contains a list of identified risks and potential owners
of those risks?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question describes the project management process of Identify Risks. The risk register is an
output of the Identify Risks process. This document contains a list of identified risks along with

---

the potential owners of those risks. The risk register is the document that is created as a result of
the project meeting.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A RACI chart**
Incorrect. A RACI chart is a common type of responsibility assignment matrix that uses
responsible, accountable, consult, and inform statuses to define the involvement of
stakeholders in project activities. A RACI chart does not contain a list of identified risks
and potential risk owners.
- **B Requirements traceability matrix**
Incorrect. A requirements traceability matrix is a grid that links product requirements from
their origin to the deliverables that satisfy them. The requirements traceability matrix does
not contain a list of identified risks and potential risk owners.
- **C Risk register**
Correct. The risk register is an output of the Identify Risks process. This document contains
a list of identified risks along with the potential owners of those risks.
- **D Risk assessment log**
Incorrect. A 'risk assessment log' is a fake term made up for this question.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 417

Question 87 of 200
Question ID: 612451
With the project charter approved, you now need to identify the high-level strategic and
operational assumptions and constraints and document them in the assumption log.
What should you do?
Top of Form
- **A Ask the project sponsor to provide the information**
- **B Perform the Identify Assumptions and Constraints process**
- **C Read the project management plan**
- **D Refer to the business case**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The high-level strategic and operational assumptions and constraints should have been identified
during pre-project work.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

High-level strategic and operational assumptions and constraints are normally identified in the
business case before the project is initiated and is used to inform the development of the project
charter. Lower-level activity and task assumptions are generated throughout the project such as
defining technical specifications, estimates, risks, etc. The assumption log is used to record all
assumptions and constraints throughout the project life cycle. Therefore, of the available options,

---

you should check the business case to identify the high-level strategic and operational
assumptions and constraints.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Ask the project sponsor to provide the information**
Incorrect. The project sponsor may not have the relevant information that you require.
Project managers should use the readily available resources before escalating issues to the
project sponsor. High-level strategic and operational assumptions and constraints are
typically identified as part of pre-project work, which should be available to a project
manager.
- **B Perform the Identify Assumptions and Constraints process**
Incorrect. 'Identify Assumptions and Constraints' is a fake project management process
made up for this question.
- **C Read the project management plan**
Incorrect. The question suggests that the project is still in the initiation stage; therefore, the
project management plan has yet to be developed.
- **D Refer to the business case**
Correct. The business case is created during pre-project work and should contain the
high-level strategic and operational assumptions and constraints.

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 88 of 200
Question ID: 651340
- **A multiyear construction project is scheduled to purchase tons of steel over the course of the**
project. After the first year, a large tariff was unexpectedly placed on imported steel, sending
prices up. The risk response plan is being implemented with little success. It is deemed that the
procurement agreement needs to be revised to an FP-EPA contract.
What would be the most likely resulting output of implementing the risk response?
Top of Form
- **A Control procurements**
- **B Change request**
- **C Cost variance**
- **D Risk avoidance**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is an output of the Implement Risk Responses process?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

As work is being done on the project, risks that become realized must be addressed. The
Implement Risk Responses process addresses the risks. Sometimes, the response is not
completely effective or results in requiring changes to components of the project management
plan. In this scenario, the procurement documents, including the agreement, possibly need to

---

change. Changes to an agreement are done using the contract change control system. Hence as an
output of the process, a change request is required to revise the procurement agreements. The
change request would then be reviewed as part of the Perform Integrated Change Control
process. The FP-EPA (Fixed Price with Economic Price Adjustment) contract is a fixed-price
contract with a special provision allowing for predefined final adjustments to the contract price
due to changed conditions, such as inflation change or cost increases or decreases for specific
commodities.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Control procurements**
Incorrect. The process of Control Procurements is connected to the Implement Risk
Responses process in this scenario, but it is not the output of implementing the risk
response.
- **B Change request**
Correct. The output of implementing risk responses in this scenario is a change request.
The project team is recommending a change to the procurement agreements to an FP-EPA
contract.
- **C Cost variance**
Incorrect. There may be a cost variance due to the change in the price of steel, but not as a
result of implementing a risk response.
- **D Risk avoidance**
Incorrect. Risk avoidance is a risk response strategy where the team acts to eliminate the
threat or protect from its impact. In this case, the team is mitigating the risk to reduce the
impact on the project in case of cost increases or decreases of specific commodities.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 451, 499, 702

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 89 of 200
Question ID: 612693
You are thirteen weeks into a project that was planned to be completed in one year. From a
schedule perspective, one-quarter of the work has already been completed.
Based on earned schedule theory, what is your best course of action?
Top of Form
- **A Submit a change request to revise the schedule baseline**
- **B Continue to monitor progress to ensure the project stays on track**
- **C Perform a reserve analysis to determine if there are adequate schedule reserves to cover the**
shortfall
- **D Crash the schedule to bring the schedule back into alignment with project goals**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Using earned schedule theory, the schedule variance is the earned schedule (ES) minus actual
time (AT).
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Earned schedule (ES) is an extension of the theory and practice of earned value management
(EVM), which is one of the trends and emerging practices in project cost management. Earned
schedule theory replaces the schedule variance measures used in traditional EVM (earned value -
planned value) with earned schedule (ES) and actual time (AT). Using the alternate equation for

---

calculating schedule variance ES - AT, if the amount of earned schedule is greater than 0, then
the project is considered ahead of schedule.
In this scenario, the project was scheduled for one year (52 weeks), and one-quarter of the
scheduled work has been completed which represents the earned schedule (ES) of 13 weeks. The
actual time (AT) is presented as 13 weeks. The schedule variance is the earned schedule (ES)
minus actual time (AT) or SV = 13 - 13 = 0. Thus, using earned schedule theory, the schedule
variance indicates that the project is on schedule. The incorrect answer choices represent actions
that might be taken if the project is running behind schedule. Therefore, of the available options,
the best course of action for you, as the project manager, is to continue to monitor progress to
ensure the project stays on track.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Submit a change request to revise the schedule baseline**
Incorrect. The question indicates that 13 weeks into the project, 13 weeks of the scheduled
work has been completed (1/4 x 52). Thus, the project is running on schedule. Therefore,
there is no reason to submit a change request to revise the schedule baseline based on the
information presented by the question.
- **B Continue to monitor progress to ensure the project stays on track**
Correct. The project was scheduled for one year (52 weeks), and one-quarter of the
scheduled work has been completed. In other words, thirteen weeks into the project,
thirteen weeks of the scheduled work has been completed. Therefore, the project is
currently on schedule.
- **C Perform a reserve analysis to determine if there are adequate schedule reserves to cover**
the shortfall
Incorrect. The question indicates that thirteen weeks into the project, thirteen weeks of the
scheduled work has been completed. Since the project is currently on schedule, there is no
schedule shortfall that needs to be addressed with schedule reserves.
- **D Crash the schedule to bring the schedule back into alignment with project goals**
Incorrect. The question indicates that thirteen weeks into the project, thirteen weeks of the
scheduled work has been completed (1/4 x 52). Thus, the project is running on schedule.
Crashing the schedule to shorten the schedule duration is not necessary with the project on
schedule, and this action would likely increase costs and introduce additional project risks.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 233
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 90 of 200
Question ID: 612519
- **A company runs dozens of types of projects covering a wide range of technical areas in multiple**
countries. They are losing track of who has worked on various projects and might have highly
specialized knowledge that can be used in other projects.
Which of the following would address this issue?
Top of Form
- **A A common change control process**
- **B A video conferencing system**
- **C Monthly face-to-face meetings**
- **D A centralized person responsible for knowledge management**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The solution must address issues globally.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Some organizations assign a team or individual as a specialist in knowledge management. A
centralized person or group responsible for knowledge management may allow the company to
keep track of who in the organization has critical skills that can help on other projects as well as
coordinate those activities. Video conferencing and face-to-face meetings may help identify
those people and skills but would not address the long-term needs. A common change control

---

process has little or no relevance to knowledge management. Therefore, of the available
responses, having a centralized person responsible for knowledge management is the best answer
to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A A common change control process**
Incorrect. A common change control process may help to address uniformity and
communication of changes, but it cannot act as a repository for the company’s knowledge
sources and track who in the company possesses specific knowledge and experience.
- **B A video conferencing system**
Incorrect. A video conferencing system may be used to identify those in the company with
specific knowledge and experience, but it cannot act as a repository for corporate
knowledge sources and track who in the company possesses specific knowledge and
experience.
- **C Monthly face-to-face meetings**
Incorrect. Monthly face-to-face meetings may be used to get to know the team or
employee’s capabilities better, but it cannot act as a repository for corporate knowledge
sources and track who in the company possesses specific knowledge and experience.
- **D A centralized person responsible for knowledge management**
Correct. As the organization is looking for a solution across multiple projects spanning
many geographic regions, a centralized person or group being responsible for knowledge
management may be a viable solution.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 101

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 91 of 200
Question ID: 612901
You have just taken over a project in the middle of the fourth of five phases. The project is
running behind schedule which is attributed to poor performance of the project team. You want
to improve their performance and avoid repeating past mistakes.
What should you do first?
Top of Form
- **A Review the project team assignments**
- **B Examine the lessons learned register**
- **C Check out the team charter**
- **D Meet with the team and ask for their input**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where might you find information on knowledge gained during a project?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question implies that you are about to carry out the Develop Team process. Since you are
new to the project, it is best to familiarize yourself with any knowledge gained thus far in the
project concerning team development. The lessons learned register is a project document used to
record knowledge gained during a project so that it can be used to improve performance in the
current project and entered into the lessons learned repository. The best source for understanding

---

what has not worked well thus far in the project, so the mistakes are not repeated, is the lessons
learned register. Note that you should also review the lessons learned repository in addition to the
lessons learned register, to understand what has been effective and ineffective for past projects,
but the lessons learned repository was not listed as an answer choice. Therefore, of the available
options, examining the lessons learned register to avoid repeating past mistakes is the best
answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Review the project team assignments**
Incorrect. Project team assignments is a document that may help the project manager
identify the team members and their roles and responsibilities. However, this information is
unlikely to help the project manager improve the team member performance and avoid
repeating past mistakes.
- **B Examine the lessons learned register**
Correct. The lessons learned register is a project document used to record knowledge
gained during a project so that it can be used to improve performance. The lessons learned
register is the best source to learn about mistakes made earlier in the project.
- **C Check out the team charter**
Incorrect. The team charter is a document that records the team values, agreements, and
operating guidelines, as well as establishing clear expectations regarding acceptable
behavior by project team members. The team charter does not have information that may
help identify issues that caused poor team performance.
- **D Meet with the team and ask for their input**
Incorrect. Seeking feedback from the project team is a good idea. However, first, this
information may be biased as it reflects only the point of view of the team members;
second, you, as the project manager, will be better prepared for the upcoming discussions
by first reviewing the lessons learned from earlier in the project, thus saving time and
helping guide the sessions for greater productivity.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 339

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 92 of 200
Question ID: 612215
You are leading an infrastructure development project, which is about halfway complete. In
accordance with the risk management plan, you hold regular risk review meetings.
Which of the following are you least likely to do during this meeting?
Top of Form
- **A Examine and document the effectiveness of risk responses**
- **B Discuss the merits of a request submitted to modify the risk management plan**
- **C Identify secondary risks that arise from risk responses**
- **D Close risks that are outdated**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer choice represents an activity that is more appropriate for a change control board
(CCB) meeting than a risk review meeting?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Risk reviews are regularly scheduled meetings that examine and document the effectiveness of
risk responses in dealing with overall project risk and with identified individual project risks.
Risk reviews may also result in the identification of new individual project risks (including
secondary risks that arise from risks responses), reassessment of current risks, the closing of risks
that are outdated, issues that have arisen as the result of risks that have occurred, and

---

identification of lessons to be learned for implementation in the current project or future projects.
Risk reviews are commonly used as part of the Monitor Risks process.
Keep in mind that the question is asking for the activity that is 'least' likely to be conducted
during a risk review meeting. The merits of a change request submitted to modify the risk
management plan is a topic of discussion that is more appropriate for a meeting of the change
control board (CCB) than a risk review meeting. During a CCB meeting, change requests are
examined to determine whether to approve, deny, or defer the request. Therefore, of the available
choices, a discussion of the merits of a request submitted to modify the risk management plan is
the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Examine and document the effectiveness of risk responses**
Incorrect. Risk reviews should examine and document the effectiveness of risk responses in
dealing with overall project risk and with identified individual project risks.
- **B Discuss the merits of a request submitted to modify the risk management plan**
Correct. This answer choice describes an activity that is more appropriate for a meeting of
the change control board (CCB). When the CCB meets, they determine whether to approve,
deny, or defer change requests.
- **C Identify secondary risks that arise from risk responses**
Incorrect. Secondary risks may arise from the implementation of risk responses. These
secondary risks may be identified as part of a risk review meeting and may be included on
the agenda.
- **D Close risks that are outdated**
Incorrect. The risk review meeting is an appropriate venue for closing outdated risks.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 457
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 93 of 200
Question ID: 612297
- **A project manager is drafting a document which will formally authorize an expansive corporate**
restructuring project and needs to gather high-level information from various stakeholders. Due
to the sensitive and confidential nature of the project, the project manager feels the stakeholders
will speak more candidly if the discussions are conducted privately.
What is the best course of action?
Top of Form
- **A Conduct a small focus group**
- **B Schedule an interview with each of the relevant stakeholders**
- **C Facilitate a brainstorming session**
- **D Ask each of the key stakeholders to complete a survey**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project manager is drafting the project charter.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the project manager is drafting the project charter, the document which
formally authorizes the existence of a project. Data gathering techniques that may be useful in
the Develop Project Charter process include brainstorming, focus groups, and interviews.
Interviews may help obtain information on high-level requirements, assumptions or constraints,

---

approval criteria, and other information from stakeholders by talking to them directly, in a
one-on-one setting. Since the question describes private discussions as the most appropriate
approach, of the available options, scheduling an interview with each of the relevant stakeholders
provides the best approach.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Conduct a small focus group**
Incorrect. Focus groups bring stakeholders together in a group setting to gather
information more conversationally. However, the question indicates that the discussions
should be held privately rather than a group setting.
- **B Schedule an interview with each of the relevant stakeholders**
Correct. Interviews are used in the Develop Project Charter process to obtain information
on high-level requirements, assumptions or constraints, approval criteria, and other
information from stakeholders by talking to them directly.
- **C Facilitate a brainstorming session**
Incorrect. Brainstorming is a data gathering technique which is conducted in a group
environment. However, the question states that the stakeholders will speak more candidly if
the discussions are conducted privately. Therefore, gathering information in a group setting
is not the best approach in the scenario described.
- **D Ask each of the key stakeholders to complete a survey**
Incorrect. A survey may or may not be structured to maintain confidentiality. However, the
question indicates that the most appropriate approach in this situation is to conduct a
private discussion with the relevant stakeholders. Completing a survey is a form of one-way
communication rather than a discussion.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 80

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 94 of 200
Question ID: 610064
You have tasked the project team with identifying and documenting the specific activities
required to produce a quality door panel. The team's work will result in schedule activities that
can provide a basis for estimating, scheduling, executing, monitoring and controlling the project
work.
Which of the following tools and techniques is least likely to be used during this process?
Top of Form
- **A Decomposition**
- **B Rolling wave planning**
- **C Leads and lags**
- **D Expert judgment**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which tool or technique is used as part of the Sequence Activities process rather than the Define
Activities process? Note, the question is looking for the 'least likely' choice.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

In the scenario, the project is in the Define Activities process where work packages are
decomposed into schedule activities that provide a basis for estimating, scheduling, executing,
monitoring and controlling project work. Decomposition, rolling wave planning, and expert

---

judgment are tools and techniques used in the Define Activities process. The question is asking
which of the answer choices is the 'least likely' to be performed during the Define Activities
process. Since all of the answer choices except leads and lags are tools and techniques used in
the Define Activities process, leads and lags is the correct answer.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Decomposition**
Incorrect. In the scenario, the project is in the Define Activities process. Decomposition, a
tool and technique of the Define Activities process, is used for dividing and subdividing
deliverables into manageable parts. The question implies that the project team is using
decomposition to identify and document the activities required to produce the door panel.
Therefore, decomposition is an incorrect answer.
- **B Rolling wave planning**
Incorrect. Rolling wave planning is an iterative planning technique where work required in
the near-term is planned in detail, and future work is planned at a higher level. The project
is in the Define Activities process, and while rolling wave planning is not explicitly
mentioned in the scenario, it is a tool and technique that can be used in that process. Since
the question asks which option is 'least likely' to be performed in the Define Activities
process and rolling wave planning is a tool and technique of the process, rolling wave
planning is not the best answer to the question asked.
- **C Leads and lags**
Correct. Leads and lags are a tool and technique used during the Sequence Activities
process to produce a project schedule network diagram. Since the scenario describes the
project as being in the Define Activities process, and leads and lags are used in the
Sequence Activities process, it is unlikely that leads and lags would be used. Therefore,
leads and lags is the correct answer.
- **D Expert judgment**
Incorrect. Expert judgment is judgment provided by individuals or groups that have
knowledge and expertise in a subject matter. The scenario implies the project is in the
Define Activities process. Even though the scenario does not mention expert judgment
explicitly, it is a tool and technique of the Define Activities process, and 'could' be used as
part of the process. Therefore, expert judgment is not the correct answer.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 184-185, 192

Question 95 of 200
Question ID: 613752
You are facilitating a meeting with several subject matter experts and the project team. The goal
of this meeting is to obtain a comprehensive list of individual project risks and sources of overall
project risk. The free-form style of the meeting is proving to be highly productive with active
participation from all of the meeting participants.
Which tool or technique is being used in this scenario?
Top of Form
- **A Bidder conference**
- **B Risk register**
- **C Brainstorming**
- **D Monitor Risks**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What data gathering technique utilizes a facilitated meeting during the Identify Risks process to
produce a comprehensive list of individual project risks and sources of overall project risk?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Based on the scenario described, the project team is carrying out the Identify Risks process.
Brainstorming is one of the tools and techniques used during the Identify Risks process. The goal
of a brainstorming meeting during the Identify Risks process is to obtain a comprehensive list of

---

individual project risks and sources of overall project risk. Brainstorming is the data gathering
technique that is being utilized by the project team.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Bidder conference**
Incorrect. A bidder conference is a meeting with prospective sellers prior to the preparation
of a bid or proposal. The question implies that the team is performing the project
management process of Identify Risks. A bidder conference is one of the tools and
techniques associated with the Conduct Procurements process, but it is not used during the
Identify Risks process.
- **B Risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register is a repository that contains details of identified project risks.
The question implies that the project team is performing the project management process of
Identify Risks and is asking for a tool or technique associated with this process. The risk
register is an output of the Identify Risks process and is not a tool or technique.
- **C Brainstorming**
Correct. Brainstorming is one of the tools and techniques used in the project management
process of Identify Risks. The goal of a brainstorming meeting during the Identify Risks
process is to obtain a comprehensive list of individual project risks and sources of overall
project risk.
- **D Monitor Risks**
Incorrect. The question states that the project is in the planning stage. The Monitor Risks
process is part of the Monitoring and Controlling Process Group rather than the Planning
Process Group. Additionally, the question is asking for a tool or technique and Monitor
Risks is a project management process rather than a tool or technique.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 414

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 96 of 200
Question ID: 612774
During a demonstration of progress on the development of a new sales tool, a regional
salesperson expresses concern that a requested feature was not part of the demo or the
requirements. The project manager points out the exclusion of the feature in the project charter.
What was the project manager trying to do in documenting the exclusion?
Top of Form
- **A Trying to eliminate the features that the project manager did not like**
- **B Pointing out areas where change requests would be accepted**
- **C Defining the in-scope items of the project's next phase**
- **D Preventing scope creep**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How might a project exclusion help manage stakeholder expectations and control scope?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Project exclusions are recorded in the project charter to identify what is excluded from the
project. Explicitly stating what is out of scope for the project helps manage stakeholders'
expectations and can reduce scope creep. Project exclusions may be used for requirements in
which stakeholders have expressed interest, but are explicitly excluded from the project for

---

technical, business, or other reasons. Therefore, of the choices available, preventing scope creep
is the best response.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Trying to eliminate the features that the project manager did not like**
Incorrect. Exclusions are in the project charter to explicitly remove specific elements or
create bounds for the project, not to serve the whims of a project manager.
- **B Pointing out areas where change requests would be accepted**
Incorrect. Although the project charter may contain project exclusions to establish what is
out of scope for the project, it does not typically define areas where change requests are
accepted. A change requests can come from any aspect of the project. Additionally, the
question is describing a specific project exclusion rather than a limitation on change
requests.
- **C Defining the in-scope items of the project's next phase**
Incorrect. The exception items may or may not be included in a follow-on project phase if
there even is one. There is no connection between the exceptions and follow-on projects or
phases. Additionally, the question is describing a specific project exclusion rather than a
description of what is in scope for the project or phase.
- **D Preventing scope creep**
Correct. Exclusions clarify what is out of scope and quite often mentions requirements that
were discussed but explicitly not included in the project for technical, business or other
reasons.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 154

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 97 of 200
Question ID: 651335
- **A website refresh was supposed to be released in tandem with another project’s deliverable.**
However, that deliverable is now three weeks behind schedule. The risk response plan was
updated a few months ago to address this possibility, though some project team members now
feel that the delay does not impact the website refresh as once thought.
What is the best course of action for the website refresh project team?
Top of Form
- **A Re-evaluate the risk and modify the planned response if needed**
- **B Implement the risk response plan immediately**
- **C Submit a change request to the change control board**
- **D Avoid the risk by moving forward in the project as scheduled**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Is the identified risk the same as the realized risk?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

When risks are identified and planned for/against, there are plenty of unknowns. Risks are
uncertainties. Once a potential risk is realized, that risk is no longer uncertain but certain. That
realized risk may or may not differ from expectations. Verifying to confirm the risk is what was
expected and validating that the planned risk response is still the best option as it increases the

---

chances that the implemented response is effective and appropriate. Some modification could be
needed in light of new information, variables, and conditions.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Re-evaluate the risk and modify the planned response if needed**
Correct. Information and variables may have changed in the time the risk response was
planned. The plans were based on possible outcomes. The actual realized risks may differ.
Therefore, evaluating the risk and the planned response first is the best action. Note, if the
modification to the risk response plan will affect project constraints, a change request may
be required.
- **B Implement the risk response plan immediately**
Incorrect. Planned risk responses may be reviewed and evaluated based on actual
occurrences. The response may be implemented exactly as planned, but it may not. The
team should factor in the variables surrounding the realized risk.
- **C Submit a change request to the change control board**
Incorrect. Unless the planned risk response requires changes that must be approved by the
change control board, then no request for change is required. Nothing in this scenario
states that a request for change is required.
- **D Avoid the risk by moving forward in the project as scheduled**
Incorrect. A risk exists and has been realized. Pretending it does not exist does not make it
go away.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 451

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 98 of 200
Question ID: 651321
The company has been sold. Consequently, there is a major shift in direction and strategy. A
multiphase project has been canceled during execution of its final phase, and no more budget or
work is to be spent on the project. The PMO has assigned the project manager to manage another
project.
Before moving over to the other project, what must the project manager do?
Top of Form
- **A Communicate the status of the project to the team and produce a final report**
- **B Gain senior managers' approval to manage another project**
- **C Procure the rest of the items on the contract agreement with the supplier**
- **D Complete the final phase of the project**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Who else knows about the cancellation?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

When a project is terminated prematurely, then all the stakeholders must be made aware of the
situation and the remaining activities. It is extremely likely that the project sponsor(s) are already
aware of the project's closure. Nonetheless, they should be provided a final report of what has
occurred up to this point of the project and other relevant information. The project team and

---

other stakeholders should also be communicated with, and other closing actions should be
performed.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Communicate the status of the project to the team and produce a final report**
Correct. Communication is critical in closing a project, especially one that concludes
prematurely. Communicating the performance, status, and closing details to the team is
needed before moving on to other projects.
- **B Gain senior managers' approval to manage another project**
Incorrect. The project management office (PMO) has assigned the project manager to
manage another project implying this decision has likely been agreed upon by all relevant
managers and sponsors.
- **C Procure the rest of the items on the contract agreement with the supplier**
Incorrect. Procurement agreements with suppliers should contain riders or terms that
account for project cancellations and other unexpected outcomes. A properly negotiated
contract should not require a project to purchase items that are no longer needed.
- **D Complete the final phase of the project**
Incorrect. The project has been canceled, including all its subsequent phases. There is no
longer budget or resources assigned to continue the work of the project beyond the current
phase.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 127

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 99 of 200
Question ID: 612784
After a thorough inspection, the team member is about to mark a finished product deliverable as
passing verification. However, a customer executive passes by, examines the product, and starts
angrily screaming how its dials only go to '10' when they were supposed to go to '12'. The team
member looks up the specification, which indicates the maximum number on the dial should be
'10'.
What should the team member do next?
Top of Form
- **A Reject the deliverable and send it to rework**
- **B Mark the deliverable as passing verification**
- **C Do nothing and escalate the verification to a manager**
- **D Tell the customer executive to stop screaming and that the customer executive is wrong**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

When is the appropriate time for a customer to reject a deliverable?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The scenario describes a team member who is conducting inspections as part of the Control
Quality process. The team member's job in this situation is to ensure the deliverable conforms to
the specification. With an angry stakeholder, an appropriate proactive approach would have been

---

for the team member to listen, try to calm the executive down rather than risk further aggravating
the situation by saying outright that the customer executive is wrong. Perhaps the team member
can note the customer executive’s concerns and explain the Validate Scope process. However,
such an approach was not provided as an option. Based on the information in the scenario, the
finished product deliverable conforms to the specifications, and therefore, it is best that the team
member mark the deliverable as passing validation. The customer executive would have the
chance to formally reject the deliverable and provide reasons for the rejection.
If necessary, there may need to be a change request process required if there is a genuine need
for the dials to go up to '12'. There is not many details and information on these 'dials'. However,
this information is not required to select the correct answer. Prospective PMP aspirants have to
keep in mind that questions on the real exam can be short and vague. In such situations, we
recommend making reasonable assumptions based on the information available in the scenario
and, of the choices given, selecting the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Reject the deliverable and send it to rework**
Incorrect. According to the information provided in the scenario, the team member has
verified that the deliverable conforms to the specifications. Therefore, it can be marked as
verified, and there is nothing to rework.
- **B Mark the deliverable as passing verification**
Correct. Based on the scenario described, the item conforms to the specifications. The
customer executive has the opportunity to formally accept or reject the completed project
deliverable during the Validate Scope process.
- **C Do nothing and escalate the verification to a manager**
Incorrect. The team member who is inspecting the deliverable has a clear direction. It is up
to the team member to inspect the deliverable to determine if it meets specifications. The
inspector can do no more than simply escalate the verification to a manager. Based on the
information provided in the scenario, the team member has verified that the deliverable
conforms to the specifications. Therefore, it can be marked as verified.
- **D Tell the customer executive to stop screaming and that the customer executive is wrong**
Incorrect. This approach is quite direct. It may backfire and escalate the situation further.
The team member should exercise discretion. A better answer would have been for the team
member to listen, note the customer executive’s concerns and explain that during the

---

Validate Scope process, the customer executive would have the chance to formally reject the
deliverable and provide reasons for the rejection.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 298

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 100 of 200
Question ID: 613478
To complete some of the project activities, the project manager supplements the physical
resources assigned to the project with those outside the control of the project team but available
from within the organization.
What should the project manager do?
Top of Form
- **A Share the resource usage reports with project stakeholders**
- **B Conduct an assumption and constraint analysis**
- **C Send the procurement statement of work to prospective sellers**
- **D Update the enterprise environmental factors**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where should the usage of the resources that are outside the control of the project team be
documented?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the project manager has performed the Acquire Resources process.
Enterprise environmental factors are conditions, not under the immediate control of the team,
that influence, constrain, or direct the project. Enterprise environmental factors that may be
updated during the Acquire Resources process include resource availability within the

---

organization and the amount of the organization's consumable resources that have been used.
Company resources are generally not under the immediate control of the project team until they
have been assigned to the project. Thus, the necessary supplemental resources in this scenario are
considered enterprise environmental factors. Therefore, of the available options, updating the
enterprise environmental factors is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Share the resource usage reports with project stakeholders**
Incorrect. While keeping project stakeholders informed about the project's progress is a
good practice, it is unlikely that every time resources are used for project activities, a
report should be sent. Additionally, a 'resource usage report' is a made-up term.
- **B Conduct an assumption and constraint analysis**
Incorrect. Assumption and constraint analysis is a technique used in the Identify Risks
process to explore the validity of assumptions and constraints to determine which pose a
risk to the project. This technique is not used during the Acquire Resources process
described by the scenario.
- **C Send the procurement statement of work to prospective sellers**
Incorrect. There is not enough information in the question to determine if the project
involves procurements. Additionally, the action described by this answer choice makes no
sense within the context of the scenario.
- **D Update the enterprise environmental factors**
Correct. Enterprise environmental factors that may be updated during the Acquire
Resources process include resource availability within the organization and the amount of
the consumable organizational resources that have been used.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 335

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 101 of 200
Question ID: 612756
You have just performed a variance analysis for your project and determined that the CPI is 0.9
and the SPI is 1.2. This project is considered high profile, and it is critical that you meet all
project objectives.
Based on the variance analysis, what should you do next?
Top of Form
- **A Reduce the product features to bring costs back into alignment with the project budget**
- **B Crash the schedule to bring the schedule in line with project objectives**
- **C Conduct further research to isolate and understand the variance from the cost baseline**
- **D Release one of the developers to reduce costs**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project is running over budget and ahead of schedule.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question states that the cost performance index (CPI) is 0.9 and the schedule performance
index (SPI) is 1.2, which indicates that the project is running over budget and ahead of schedule.
Thus, you, as the project manager need to ensure that costs are brought back into alignment with
the cost baseline by the end of the project. Having just performed the variance analysis, you
should now seek to isolate and understand the variance in order to ensure the appropriate action

---

is taken. For example, it is possible that the cause of the cost variance is the result of a one-time
unexpected expenditure early in the project with recent trend analysis indicating that the project
should finish within the cost baseline and no action is necessary. In any case, you should not take
action until the issue is fully understood along with the impacts of any efforts to further control
costs. Therefore, of the available choices, conducting further research to isolate and understand
the variance from the cost baseline is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Reduce the product features to bring costs back into alignment with the project budget**
Incorrect. Cutting features from the product means that the project will not meet the scope
baseline as originally planned. The question states that it is critical that the project meet
'all' project objectives which would include the project scope. The project manager should
first attempt to bring costs back into alignment with the cost baseline before reducing
scope. Additionally, an approved change request is required to modify the scope baseline.
- **B Crash the schedule to bring the schedule in line with project objectives**
Incorrect. The question states that the schedule performance index (SPI) is 1.2 and the cost
performance index (CPI) is 0.9, which indicates that the project is running ahead of
schedule and over budget. Crashing the schedule will likely increase project costs which
will increase the cost variance.
- **C Conduct further research to isolate and understand the variance from the cost baseline**
Correct. The question indicates that the project is currently running over budget. Project
cost control includes monitoring cost performance to isolate and understand variances
from the approved cost baseline. Before action is taken, you, as the project manager, should
fully understand the issue along with the impacts of any efforts to further control costs.
- **D Release one of the developers to reduce costs**
Incorrect. Releasing one of the developers might decrease the cost variance going forward,
especially considering the project is running ahead of schedule. However, this is a
premature action and may impact other project constraints if the tasks assigned to the
developer cannot be performed by anyone else. First, the project manager should seek to
understand the cause of the cost variance to ensure that the appropriate action is taken,
which may or may not include releasing one of the developers.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 259, 262
