Question 127 of 200
Question ID: 613359
- **A project manager is assigned to lead an online gaming website development project that**
requires extensive and specialized graphics and animations. The company has never needed this
talent set on previous projects, so the project manager has to go outside for contractors.
Where can the project manager look to obtain rough estimates for this work package?
Top of Form
- **A Cost estimating templates**
- **B Analogous estimates**
- **C Enterprise environmental factors**
- **D Cost estimating policies**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The performing organization does not have relevant historical information.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question indicates that the company does not have prior experience with the required
resources. Hence, the company will not have any relevant historical information to provide a
rough cost estimate. The incorrect answer choices represent organizational process assets, which
are not likely to provide useful information as the company does not have prior experience with
these resources. Therefore, the project manager may need to look outside the organization and

---

rely on enterprise environmental factors such as commercially published databases to get this
information.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Cost estimating templates**
Incorrect. Templates are among the organizational process assets. The company is unlikely
to have a cost estimating template with comparable data as the company has never used
these types of resources.
- **B Analogous estimates**
Incorrect. Analogous estimating is a technique for estimating the duration or cost of an
activity or a project using historical data from a similar activity or project. However, the
question states that the performing organization does not have any analogous projects
since they have never used these types of resources.
- **C Enterprise environmental factors**
Correct. Since the performing organization does not possess relevant cost information for
the required resources, the project manager might use commercially published databases
that would have this information.
- **D Cost estimating policies**
Incorrect. Company policies and procedures are generally considered organizational
process assets. Cost estimating policies and procedures may be helpful in providing
guidance on how to estimate costs but are unlikely to provide the rough cost estimate.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 243

PMP Exam 6

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 128 of 200
Question ID: 612719
- **A project manager is in the process of developing a project team to enhance project performance.**
Which of the following activities is the project manager least likely to perform in support of this
resource management process?
Top of Form
- **A Recognizing and rewarding good performance**
- **B Creating an environment that facilitates teamwork**
- **C Ensuring that the resources are available as planned**
- **D Providing timely feedback and support as needed**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer choice describes an activity more likely to be associated with the Control
Resources process rather than the Develop Team process?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the project manager is conducting the Develop Team process. Project
managers require the skills to identify, build, maintain, motivate, lead, and inspire project teams
to achieve high team performance, and meet the project's objectives. Teamwork is a critical
factor for project success, and developing effective project teams is one of the primary
responsibilities of the project manager. Project managers should create an environment that

---

facilitates teamwork and continually motivates the team by providing challenges and
opportunities, providing timely feedback and support as needed, and recognizing and rewarding
good performance.
On the other hand, Control Resources is the process of ensuring that the physical resources
assigned and allocated to the project are available as planned. The question is asking which
activity the project manager is least likely to perform as part of the Develop Team process. Don't
be distracted by the 'resource management process' mentioned in the scenario that may deceive
you from selecting the correct answer. Both team members and physical resources are managed
using the processes of the Project Resource Management Knowledge Area. However, ensuring
that the assigned resources are available as planned is not part of the Develop Team process and
is, therefore, the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Recognizing and rewarding good performance**
Incorrect. Recognizing and rewarding good performance aids in team development by
reinforcing desired traits and actions, so the project team is encouraged to continue and
further develop the desired behaviors.
- **B Creating an environment that facilitates teamwork**
Incorrect. To develop a project team, the project manager must create a team environment
where individual team members can benefit from the knowledge and experience of the other
team members.
- **C Ensuring that the resources are available as planned**
Correct. Control Resources is the process of ensuring that the resources assigned and
allocated to the project are available as planned. This answer choice represents the action
that the project manager is least likely to perform in support of the Develop Team process
implied by the scenario.
- **D Providing timely feedback and support as needed**
Incorrect. Timely feedback and support are crucial to developing a productive team.
Feedback fosters development by guiding the team member to achieve personal and
professional growth.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 336-337, 352

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 129 of 200
Question ID: 610091
After lengthy and thorough discussions, the change control board (CCB) rejects a change request
to update design despite the fact the project manager, who is also a member of the CCB, supports
the change. The stakeholder who submitted the change request is unhappy with the decision and
demands that the project manager updates the design anyway.
How should the project manager respond?
Top of Form
- **A Instruct the designers to update the design**
- **B Re-communicate the decision of the CCB to the project stakeholder and state that the decision is**
final
- **C Tell the CCB they are making a big mistake and continue to support the stakeholder's argument**
- **D Tell the stakeholder that they should present their case directly to the CCB**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The change control board made a decision.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The PMBOK® Guide defines the change control board (CCB) as "a formally chartered group
responsible for reviewing, evaluating, approving, deferring, or rejecting changes to the project
and for recording and communicating such decisions." Unless there is an individual or a group

---

that has the authority to overrule the CCB's decision (this information would have been
documented in the change management plan), the CCB has the final authority to decide what, if
any, changes can be made to the project deliverables. Based on the scenario described, it can be
reasonably assumed that the change has passed through all the necessary steps, and the decision
to reject has been made based on the best judgment of all involved parties. Once the decision is
made, all project work should abide by that decision. Trying to persuade the CCB to revert their
decision would not be the best use of time of the project manager, the CCB members, or the
stakeholder. Therefore, among the choices given, re-communicating the decision of the CCB to
the stakeholder and stating that the decision is final would be the best course of action for the
project manager to take in this situation even though the project manager supports the change.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Instruct the designers to update the design**
Incorrect. The change control board did not approve the change. There is not enough
information in the question to determine if the project manager has the authority to
overrule the decision of the CCB, and it is unlikely that the project manager would have
this authority.
- **B Re-communicate the decision of the CCB to the project stakeholder and state that the**
decision is final
Correct. According to the scenario, the stakeholder who initiated the request is unhappy
with the CCB's decision implying the decision has already been communicated. However, of
the choices provided, re-communicating the decision and stating that the decision is final is
the best answer of the choices available.
- **C Tell the CCB they are making a big mistake and continue to support the stakeholder's**
argument
Incorrect. The project manager is a member of the CCB and would have already expressed
support for the change during the CCB meeting. However, based on the outcome of the
meeting, it can be inferred that the project manager was unsuccessful in persuading the
CCB to approve the change. Therefore, continuing arguing for the change is not the best
use of the project resources.
- **D Tell the stakeholder that they should present their case directly to the CCB**
Incorrect. Advising the stakeholder to go to the CCB would not be the best use of project
resources as the CCB's decision is final. Neither the project manager nor an individual

---

staffer should try persuading the CCB to change their decision that has been made based
on all available information and their best judgment.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 115
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam 6

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 130 of 200
Question ID: 612722
During the execution of a project to construct a new power plant, an environmental group has
successfully lobbied the government to revise regulations to reduce the environmental impact of
the plant. The required changes to the project significantly increase its cost, thereby risking the
project's termination.
What might the project manager have done differently to avoid this situation?
Top of Form
- **A Ensured that the initial plant design met existing regulations**
- **B Reviewed the lessons learned repository from past projects**
- **C Identified the environmental group as a project stakeholder**
- **D Developed a response to the risk of changing regulations**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How might the regulators and the environmental group have been engaged before the start of the
project?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

In this scenario, an environmental group successfully lobbied for the government to revise
existing regulations, and the project was forced to incur the additional compliance costs
associated with the revised regulations, which now threatens the project. One of the trends and

---

emerging practices in Project Stakeholder Management includes identifying all stakeholders and
not just a limited set. Broader definitions of stakeholders are being developed that expand the
traditional categories of employees, suppliers, and shareholders to include groups such as
regulators, lobby groups, and environmentalists. Identifying these groups as stakeholders during
project initiation, and then engaging them prior to project execution would have helped in the
understanding of the benefits of the project, which may have prevented the regulations from
being changed during project execution. Even if these groups still wanted changes made to the
plant's design, the negative effects on the project could have been mitigated by incorporating
their recommendations before project execution began. The incorrect answer choices either
address the issue after the fact or were already done. Therefore, of the available options,
identifying all stakeholders and not just a limited set is the best response.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Ensured that the initial plant design met existing regulations**
Incorrect. The question states that government regulations were changed as the result of
lobbying efforts by an environmental group. There is no indication in the question
suggesting that the initial plant design did not meet 'existing' regulations.
- **B Reviewed the lessons learned repository from past projects**
Incorrect. The situation described in the scenario suggests the government regulations have
been changed during the course of the current project. Therefore, reviewed the lessons
learned repository from past projects would not have the information to help the current
project.
- **C Identified the environmental group as a project stakeholder**
Correct. Identifying the relevant regulators and environmental lobby groups, as
stakeholders during project initiation, and then engaging them prior to project execution
would have helped in the understanding of the benefits of the project, which may have
prevented the regulations from being changed during project execution. Even if these
groups still wanted changes made to the plant's design, the negative effects on the project
could have been mitigated by incorporating their recommendations before project
execution began.
- **D Developed a response to the risk of changing regulations**
Incorrect. Identifying the risk and developing the response could have helped in addressing
the risk, however, it is unlikely that this would have avoided the situation described in the
scenario.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 505

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 131 of 200
Question ID: 612835
You are managing a hazardous waste cleanup project at a manufacturing plant. A major
milestone is due to be complete in two weeks. Based on your project plans filed with a municipal
authority and a federal agency, both authorities have notified you that their inspectors will visit
the site the week after your milestone.
To avoid fines, rework, and related delays, what is your best course of action?
Top of Form
- **A Ask the agencies to postpone their inspections another week**
- **B Invite the inspectors to a milestone party to win them over**
- **C Hold sitewide training to get your staff ready to inspect**
- **D Conduct an equivalent inspection to verify the deliverables**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

An inspection by a key stakeholder like a government agency is an act of scope validation. What
input is always required to Validate Scope?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The Control Quality process is concerned with the correctness of the work and meeting quality
requirements. Verified deliverables are an output of this process and an input to the Validate
Scope process which will be carried out by the project team together with the municipal

---

authority and the federal agency to determine if the acceptance criteria have been met.
Inspections can be used among the tools and techniques of both the Control Quality process and
the Validate Scope process. Therefore, prior to the inspection of the Validate Scope process, to
avoid fines, rework, and related delays, and verify the deliverables, conducting an equivalent
inspection as part of the Control Quality process is the best course of action for you, as the
project manager, to take.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Ask the agencies to postpone their inspections another week**
Incorrect. Having filed your cleanup plans with both authorities, you should already have
planned for contingencies related to their inspections. Nothing in the scenario described
indicates that a postponement is needed.
- **B Invite the inspectors to a milestone party to win them over**
Incorrect. The deliverable work should pass inspection without any help from
entertainments that might raise ethics concerns. Any networking you do should be
unquestionable, not to 'win over' inspectors, but to foster professional connection,
alignment, and collaboration.
- **C Hold sitewide training to get your staff ready to inspect**
Incorrect. This close to a milestone, your team should already be experienced and trained
to do their jobs. Your plans to meet inspection requirements should be well underway.
Holding an unplanned sitewide training session may waste precious time.
- **D Conduct an equivalent inspection to verify the deliverables**
Correct. As a tool of the Control Quality process, inspections compare performance against
the quality requirements and give the project team a chance to resolve any issues in a
timely manner. The inspections of the Control Quality process will result in verified
deliverables that may be presented for the inspections of the relevant stakeholders in the
Validate Scope process to result in the accepted deliverables.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 166, 303, 305

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 132 of 200
Question ID: 612848
While doing some analysis on project costs, you notice that a few team members have completed
their work but have not been released from the project.
Which of the following should you consult to learn more about the procedure for releasing team
members?
Top of Form
- **A Resource breakdown structure**
- **B RACI chart**
- **C Resource management plan**
- **D Project team assignments**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the key plan that contains guidance on how all project resources should be categorized,
allocated, managed, and released?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Although the scenario indicates that the project is in the Control Costs process, the question is
asking about the outputs of the Plan Resource Management process. The resource management
plan describes how all resource requirements are met on a project, for both team and physical
resources. It includes information detailing the timing and method for the release of team

---

members. The other answer choices provide a variety of resource-related information, but they
do not include release procedures.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Resource breakdown structure**
Incorrect. The resource breakdown structure is a hierarchal list of team and physical
resources related by category and resource type. It does not provide guidance on resource
release procedures.
- **B RACI chart**
Incorrect. RACI charts are a common type of responsibility assignment matrix that lists
resource assignments. However, they do not contain resource release procedures.
- **C Resource management plan**
Correct. The resource management plan contains guidance on how project resources
should be categorized, allocated, managed, and released, making this choice the best
answer to the question asked.
- **D Project team assignments**
Incorrect. Documentation of project team assignments records the team members and their
roles and responsibilities for the project. However, it does not include resource release
procedures.

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 318

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 133 of 200
Question ID: 612737
The following affect the project schedule: the parts for the system are manufactured in another
country, shipped by ocean freighter, and need to go through customs before they can be sent to
the site. In addition, the site requires some structural renovations before the new system can be
installed. Lastly, the external vendor is responsible for integrating the new system with the
organization's information system.
Which of the following best describes these prerequisites?
Top of Form
- **A Mandatory internal dependencies**
- **B Mandatory external dependencies**
- **C Leads and lags**
- **D Discretionary external dependencies**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Prerequisites in project scheduling can be characterized by being mandatory or discretionary and
internal or external.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Identifying and documenting relationships between project activities is required to develop a
project schedule. A dependency occurs when one activity has to be completed before another

---

activity can start. The dependency can be either mandatory or discretionary. A mandatory
dependency is required legally, contractually or by the nature of the work. A discretionary
dependency means the sequence is generally accepted to be done a certain way, but not required.
Dependencies are also characterized by being external - out of the control of the project team, or
internal - within the control of the project team. The activities described in this scenario are all
external as the project team has no control over their completion. The activities are also
mandatory as they are required to be completed in a particular order. Therefore, the prerequisites
presented in the question are best described by mandatory external dependencies making them
the best answer the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Mandatory internal dependencies**
Incorrect. Mandatory internal dependencies are actions that are required to be completed
before the next operation can be started and are within the control of the project team. In
this scenario, the actions (prerequisites) described are: the parts being manufactured
abroad, the site needing structural renovations, and the external vendor being responsible
for the integration between the systems. None of these actions are within the control of the
project team; therefore, they are considered mandatory external dependencies rather than
mandatory internal dependencies.
- **B Mandatory external dependencies**
Correct. Mandatory external dependencies are actions that are required to be completed
before the next step can be started and are outside the control of the project team. In this
scenario, the parts being manufactured abroad and must pass through local customs before
being shipped to the site. This action (prerequisite) is outside the control of the project
team. The situation is the same with the required renovations and the interface; neither of
which can be controlled by the project team. Therefore, mandatory external dependencies
best describe the prerequisites presented by the question.
- **C Leads and lags**
Incorrect. A lead is the amount of time a successor activity can be advanced with respect to
its predecessor activity. A lag is the amount of time a successor activity will be delayed with
respect to its predecessor activity. The question describes dependencies. Leads and lags are
not dependencies and therefore are an incorrect answer.
- **D Discretionary external dependencies**
Incorrect. External discretionary dependencies are actions that are sequenced in a way that
was established based on best practices or where a specific sequence is considered the

---

norm but are not required and are outside the control of the project team. The prerequisites
mentioned in the scenario are not flexible and must be performed before the next activity
can begin. Therefore, discretionary external dependencies not the best answer.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 191-192
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 134 of 200
Question ID: 613166
During project execution, many approved changes requested by one of the project stakeholders
have shifted the direction of the project. It turned out the stakeholder was not effectively engaged
in project planning even though the stakeholder holds substantial power in the organization and
is very interested in the project.
What could the project manager have done earlier in the project to avoid this situation?
Top of Form
- **A Excluded the stakeholder from the project to avoid scope creep**
- **B Identified the individual as a stakeholder for inclusion in the stakeholder register**
- **C Categorized stakeholders with data representation techniques when developing the stakeholder**
register
- **D Nothing could have been done to avoid this situation since the stakeholder holds substantial**
power in the organization
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The stakeholder was not categorized as interested and powerful in the stakeholder register.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question states that, during project planning, the stakeholder was not effectively engaged,
and is asking what might have been done earlier in the project, which suggests that the cause of

---

the problem occurred during project initiation. The stakeholder register is developed during
project initiation as an output of the Identify Stakeholders process. A data representation
technique that may be used in this process includes stakeholder mapping and representation.
Stakeholder mapping and representation is a method of categorizing stakeholders that can assist
the team in building relationships with the identified project stakeholders. The power and interest
grid is one of the common methods used to categorize stakeholders for small projects. Had the
stakeholder been categorized as very interested and powerful, this information would have
assisted the project team in building a better relationship and more effectively engaging the
stakeholder in project planning. Therefore, of the available choices, to avoid the situation
described in the scenario, the use of a data representation technique when developing the
stakeholder register is what the project manager could have done differently.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Excluded the stakeholder from the project to avoid scope creep**
Incorrect. It is unlikely that a project manager would be able to exclude a very interested
and powerful stakeholder from a project. Additionally, if a stakeholder wields considerable
power over a project, it is best to build a relationship and effectively engage the
stakeholder to ensure their continued support for the project. Additionally, scope creep
refers to the 'uncontrolled' expansion of the project, whereas the question states that the
change requests were approved.
- **B Identified the individual as a stakeholder for inclusion in the stakeholder register**
Incorrect. The question suggests that the problem was that the stakeholder was not
categorized as being very interested and powerful in the stakeholder register, rather than
not being identified at all.
- **C Categorized stakeholders with data representation techniques when developing the**
stakeholder register
Correct. Stakeholder mapping and representation is a data representation technique that
serves as a method to categorize stakeholders. Categorization of stakeholders assists the
team in building relationships with the identified project stakeholders. The power and
interest grid is one of the common methods used to categorize stakeholders for small
projects. Having the stakeholder categorized properly and in a timely manner could have
avoided the situation described in the scenario.
- **D Nothing could have been done to avoid this situation since the stakeholder holds**
substantial power in the organization

---

Incorrect. Regardless of the power kept by the stakeholder in the organization, a proper
application of the project management processes could have helped the project manager
avoid the situation described in the scenario. Another answer choice provides an example
of what could have been done, making the current choice not the best answer.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 512

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 135 of 200
Question ID: 613539
You are trying to decide on a way to implement a company-wide initiative. A proposed solution
costs $120 million but has a 60% chance of saving $200 million and a 40% chance of saving
only $90 million.
What does $36 million represent?
Top of Form
- **A Level of confidence that you will save $200 million**
- **B Net path value for saving $200 million**
- **C Expected monetary value (EMV)**
- **D Earned Value (EV)**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

You have enough information to perform a decision tree analysis.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

EMV for a project is calculated by multiplying the value of each possible outcome by its
probability of occurrence and adding the products together. A common use of this type of
calculation is in decision tree analysis, a technique used in the Perform Quantitative Risk
Analysis process.

---

Given the details in this scenario, the solution has a chance of having two quantified outcomes.
For each outcome, you multiply the probability by the impact value, accounting for the amount
that must be invested in the solution.
Net Path Value 1 = 0.60 x (200-120) = 0.60 x 80 = 48
Net Path Value 2 = 0.40 x (90-120) = 0.40 x -30 = -12
Then, to calculate the expected monetary value of the proposed solution, you add the two net
path values together. If one of the values is negative, of course, you subtract.
Expected Monetary Value = 48 - 12 = $36 million

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Level of confidence that you will save $200 million**
Incorrect. When performing a simulation like the Monte Carlo analysis, you can calculate
the level of confidence, which is usually presented in the form of a percentage. Since the
$36 million is a dollar value, it does not represent the level of confidence.
- **B Net path value for saving $200 million**
Incorrect. Certainly, decision tree analysis involves finding the net path value. For each
outcome, you multiply the probability by the impact value, accounting for the amount that
must be invested in the solution. In this case: 0.60 x (200-120) = 0.60 x 80 = 48. Therefore,
the $36 million in question does not represent this net path value.
- **C Expected monetary value (EMV)**
Correct. Given the details in this scenario, you have enough information to perform a
decision tree analysis. To do so, you calculate the expected monetary value (EMV) of this
solution as follows: [0.60 x (200-120)] + [0.40 x (90-120)] = $36 million. Therefore, this
amount represents the EMV.
- **D Earned Value (EV)**
Incorrect. Earned value is defined as the measure of work performed expressed in terms of
the budget authorized for that work. It is used to assess project performance and progress
in the earned value management (EVM) methodology for the processes to Control Costs
and Control Schedule. This scenario indicates that the relevant process is Perform
Quantitative Risk Analysis, and the details in this question are not relevant to the progress
of execution in EVM.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 435
Bottom of Form
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Bottom of Form Prev Next

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 136 of 200
Question ID: 612851
- **A project manager is leading a project to design and manufacture a new product. As part of the**
process to define and document the stakeholders' needs for the project, the project manager
wants to determine the critical characteristics of the new product.
What is the best course of action for the project manager?
Top of Form
- **A Invite software developers to a joint application design/development (JAD) session**
- **B Collect customer needs using the quality function deployment (QFD) technique**
- **C Analyze the project schedule network diagram and quality control measurements**
- **D Gather the customer requirements from the requirements traceability matrix**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which of the answer choices represents a tool or technique of the Collect Requirements process
that is used in the manufacturing industry?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the project manager is currently performing the Collect Requirements
process. In the manufacturing industry, quality function deployment (QFD) is a facilitation
technique that helps determine the critical characteristics for new product development. QFD
starts by collecting customer needs, also known as the voice of the customer (VOC). These needs

---

are then objectively sorted and prioritized, and goals are set for achieving them. Therefore, of the
available choices, using quality function deployment (QFD) as a methodology to determine and
prioritize customer requirements is the best response.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Invite software developers to a joint application design/development (JAD) session**
Incorrect. A joint application design/development (JAD) session is typically used in the
software development industry rather than the manufacturing industry.
- **B Collect customer needs using the quality function deployment (QFD) technique**
Correct. QFD is a facilitation technique that helps determine the critical characteristics by
collecting customer needs and then objectively sorting and prioritizing them.
- **C Analyze the project schedule network diagram and quality control measurements**
Incorrect. According to the scenario, the project manager is performing the Collect
Requirement process. The project schedule network diagram is developed later in project
planning. Quality control measurements are the documented results of control quality
activities, which are carried out as part of the Control Quality process.
- **D Gather the customer requirements from the requirements traceability matrix**
Incorrect. The requirements traceability matrix is a grid that links product requirements
from their origin to the deliverables that satisfy them. The question suggests that the
Collect Requirements process is underway, and the requirements traceability matrix is an
output of this process. Customer requirements must first be gathered before the information
can be recorded in the requirements traceability matrix.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 145

Question 137 of 200
Question ID: 613763
Your team has finished identifying risks for your project and is now analyzing the quality of risk
data.
What should be done next?
Top of Form
- **A Creating a fallback plan**
- **B Developing a probability and impact matrix**
- **C Conducting a criticality analysis**
- **D Running a Monte Carlo simulation**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which of the following is a technique used in the Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis process?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The scenario describes a project team performing qualitative risk analysis - they have already
finished identifying project risks and are now analyzing the quality of risk data. The next step in
the Project Risk Management Knowledge Area is to discuss the probability and impact of the
identified risks. The risks need to be ranked or prioritized. This can be done by assigning each
risk to a priority level using a probability and impact matrix, which is one of the tools and
techniques of the Perform Qualitative Analysis process. In doing so, the project team can

---

determine which of the identified project risks have the highest priority and require further
analysis and action. The other answer choices would typically be performed in subsequent risk
management processes.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Creating a fallback plan**
Incorrect. In this scenario, the project team is performing qualitative risk analysis.
Creating a fallback plan does not occur until the Plan Risk Responses process, and
therefore is an incorrect choice.
- **B Developing a probability and impact matrix**
Correct. After identifying the risks and assessing the quality of risk data the project team
should discuss the probability and impact of the identified risks, and assign a priority level
using a probability and impact matrix – a technique used in the Perform Qualitative
Analysis process. By completing this step, the project team can determine which of the
identified risks have the highest priority and require further analysis and action.
- **C Conducting a criticality analysis**
Incorrect. A criticality analysis is a type of simulation technique used in quantitative
schedule risk analysis, not qualitative risk analysis described by the scenario.
- **D Running a Monte Carlo simulation**
Incorrect. The scenario describes a project team performing qualitative risk analysis. A
Monte Carlo simulation is a technique used in quantitative risk analysis to evaluate the
potential impact of individual project risks on achieving project objectives.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 425, 433-434, 439, 445

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 138 of 200
Question ID: 651423
You leave a meeting where the stakeholders accepted some of the project deliverables. The
quality engineer approaches you and lets you know that certain quality checks were not done.
What is your best action as the project manager?
Top of Form
- **A Instruct the engineer to run the checks on the next set of deliverables**
- **B Submit a change request to repair the issues reported by the quality engineer**
- **C Inform the stakeholders that the deliverables were not verified**
- **D Tell the engineer it's OK because the scope has been validated and formally accepted**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Is everything complete and correct?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The Validate Scope process is the process of seeking formal acceptance of the deliverables. To
achieve formal acceptance, the project team should assure all decision makers that the scope is
not only complete but also meets quality standards set by the project. Not verifying that all
deliverables fulfill the quality standards before or during formal acceptance of the deliverables is
dishonest and risks quality issues after delivery, which reflects poorly on the project team and
project organization. In this scenario, more quality checks were needed. Those checks should

---

still be performed even though the scope has been accepted by stakeholders. The stakeholders
should be informed that the deliverables were not verified.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Instruct the engineer to run the checks on the next set of deliverables**
Incorrect. The quality checks were planned for those deliverables. The checks should be
run on those deliverables as well as the next set.
- **B Submit a change request to repair the issues reported by the quality engineer**
Incorrect. The quality engineer did not raise any issues that require to be repaired. The
quality engineer raised a general issue that the deliverables have not been verified.
Submitting a change request at this point is a premature action.
- **C Inform the stakeholders that the deliverables were not verified**
Correct. Informing the stakeholders that the deliverables were not verified is aligned with
the value of honesty of the PMI Code of Ethics and Professional Conduct that reads, among
the others, "We provide accurate information in a timely manner."
- **D Tell the engineer it's OK because the scope has been validated and formally accepted**
Incorrect. If deliverables are complete but not correct, then the project manager has not
fulfilled the objective of the project. Quality checks should still take place even though the
deliverables were accepted to assure correctness.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 164-165; see also The PMI Code of Ethics and
Professional Conduct, Honesty

Question 139 of 200
Question ID: 651334
As the project progresses, the project manager realizes more regular meetings with the project
crew working at the customer's location is required.
To ensure this need is properly documented, which of the following should be updated?
Top of Form
- **A Performance report**
- **B Project charter**
- **C Risk register**
- **D Project schedule**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What has been changed or altered?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

While managing the communications of the project, there are commonly adjustments and
updates to the communications, such as in this case with the increase of scheduled meetings with
project resources (the project team that is on the customer's site). As more activities are
scheduled, the project schedule is updated to reflect the updates and to communicate new
information to other stakeholders. The project schedule is a project document. Project documents

---

can be updated as an outcome of the Manage Communications process described in the scenario.
In other words, project documents updates are an output of this process.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Performance report**
Incorrect. A performance report is a representation of work performance compiled in
project documents, intended to generate decisions, action, or awareness. The project
manager is changing the frequency of meetings held with part of the project team and is not
directly affecting the project's team performance such that an update of the performance
report is required.
- **B Project charter**
Incorrect. The project charter is used to authorize a project. It is not a project document
that must be updated for low-level activities and decisions within the management of a
project.
- **C Risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register is a repository that records the outputs of the risk management
process. Since there are no new risks identified, nor any noted changes to the information
known or responses to existing risks, the risk register needs not to be updated.
- **D Project schedule**
Correct. The project schedule presents linked activities with planned dates, durations,
milestones, and resources. Scheduling more meetings between the project manager and
part of the project team should be reflected in the project schedule and communicated to
others.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 387

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 140 of 200
Question ID: 613036
- **A project manager is leading a focus group to determine requirements for a project to create**
thermal protection tiles for a new spacecraft. One of the stakeholders, who is the subject matter
expert in the industry, states that the tiles must be tested and certified to withstand 3,000 degrees
Fahrenheit.
What should the project manager do with this information?
Top of Form
- **A Add the risk of the tiles being unable to stand 3,000 degrees Fahrenheit to the risk register**
- **B Record the information in the requirements documentation as a quality requirement**
- **C Ensure the requirement is listed in the project charter and the work breakdown structure**
- **D Capture the requirement in the stakeholder register under the name of the stakeholder**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Requirements can be grouped into classifications allowing for further refinement and detail as
the requirements are elaborated.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the project manager is performing the Collect Requirements process.
Outputs of this process include the requirements documentation and the requirements traceability
matrix. The requirements documentation describes how individual requirements meet the

---

business need for the project. Requirements can be grouped into classifications allowing for
further refinement and detail as the requirements are elaborated. Among these classifications are
quality requirements. Quality requirements capture any condition or criteria needed to validate
the successful completion of a project deliverable. Tests and certifications, as in this scenario, are
examples of quality requirements. Therefore, of the available choices, the project manager
should record the information in the requirements documentation as a quality requirement.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Add the risk of the tiles being unable to stand 3,000 degrees Fahrenheit to the risk register**
Incorrect. According to the scenario, having the tiles being able to stand 3,000 degrees
Fahrenheit is a requirement, not a risk. If later in the project it will be assumed that the
tiles are unable to withstand his temperature, the risk register can be updated with this
information.
- **B Record the information in the requirements documentation as a quality requirement**
Correct. Quality requirements capture any condition or criteria needed to validate the
successful completion of a project deliverable. Tests and certifications, as in this scenario,
are examples of quality requirements.
- **C Ensure the requirement is listed in the project charter and the work breakdown structure**
Incorrect. Adding the thermal test as a work package to the work breakdown structure will
likely be needed. However, adding this requirement to the project charter makes little sense
since the project charter contains high-level requirements and serves as an input to the
Collect Requirements process implied by the scenario. The results of this process are
detailed requirements which are recorded in the requirements documentation and
requirements traceability matrix.
- **D Capture the requirement in the stakeholder register under the name of the stakeholder**
Incorrect. The stakeholder register is a project document that records information about the
identification, assessment, and classification of project stakeholders. This document does
not specify the requirements requested by the stakeholders.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 147-148

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 141 of 200
Question ID: 613379
Project execution is just getting underway, and the project team is still in the forming stage of
team development.
What might the project manager do first?
Top of Form
- **A Create the team charter for the team**
- **B Create the project resource management plan**
- **C Schedule a team building meeting**
- **D Move the team to the performing stage of team development**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The forming stage of team development is where the team members meet and learn about the
project and their formal roles and responsibilities. Team members tend to be independent and not
as open in this phase.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The forming stage of team development is where the team members meet and learn about the
project and their formal roles and responsibilities. Team members tend to be independent and not
as open in this phase. Team building is conducting activities that enhance the team's social
relations and build a collaborative and cooperative working environment. The objective of a

---

team building meeting is to help individual team members work together effectively. The
incorrect answer choices represent actions that should have been completed earlier in the project
or are inappropriate. Therefore, of the available options, scheduling a team-building meeting is
the best way for the project manager to guide the project team through the forming stage of team
development.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Create the team charter for the team**
Incorrect. The team charter works best when it is created by the project team, or the project
team at least has input into its creation. The project manager should not create the team
charter 'for' the project team.
- **B Create the project resource management plan**
Incorrect. The question states that project execution is just getting underway. The resource
management plan is created as an output of the Plan Resource Management process as
part of project planning. With project execution underway, the project management plan,
including the resource management plan, should already exist.
- **C Schedule a team building meeting**
Correct. Team building is conducting activities that enhance the team's social relations and
build a collaborative and cooperative working environment. The objective of a team
building meeting is to help individual team members work together effectively, which is an
appropriate strategy to guide the project team through the forming stage of team
development.
- **D Move the team to the performing stage of team development**
Incorrect. While performing is the most advanced stage of team development, the project
manager cannot just 'move' the team to that stage. The project manager can help the team
to develop. But even this process will typically happen gradually and unlikely skip the
storming and norming stages which come after the forming one.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 338, 341-342

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 142 of 200
Question ID: 613632
With the work packages defined, your project team needs to identify the specific activities that
must be performed. Since some parameters have yet to be determined, the team is finding it
difficult to do detailed planning. You request the team to proceed with what information they do
have, knowing that they must revisit this process and update the activity list once these
parameters are determined.
What technique is being used in this scenario?
Top of Form
- **A Decomposition**
- **B Rolling wave planning**
- **C Expert judgment**
- **D Progressive elaboration**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the iterative planning technique in which the work to be accomplished in the near term is
planned in detail, while work further in the future is planned at a higher level?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

In this scenario, the project team must define the activities to be performed to complete the work
packages but cannot do detailed planning until the location of the construction site is known. To

---

manage this uncertainty without delaying the project schedule, the project team will proceed with
the information they currently have but continue decomposing the work packages and updating
the activity list once the construction site location is determined. This is an example of rolling
wave planning - an iterative planning technique in which the work to be accomplished in the near
term is planned in detail, while work further in the future is planned at a higher level. Although
expert judgment, decomposition, and progressive elaboration are also used in this scenario,
rolling wave planning provides the most precise definition and is, therefore, the best answer
choice.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Decomposition**
Incorrect. Decomposition is a technique used for dividing and subdividing the project
deliverables into activities, which represent the effort needed to complete a work package.
The project team is using decomposition to begin creating their activity list; however, since
the detailed planning of the construction work cannot be done at this stage in the project,
the team is using the rolling wave planning technique.
- **B Rolling wave planning**
Correct. The scenario described is an example of rolling wave planning - an iterative
planning technique in which the work to be accomplished in the near term is planned in
detail, while work further in the future is planned at a higher level. As more is known about
upcoming events in the near term, work packages can be decomposed into activities to the
required level of detail.
- **C Expert judgment**
Incorrect. Although there is an element of expert judgment being applied here, the primary
technique being described is rolling wave planning - a technique used in the Define
Activities process.
- **D Progressive elaboration**
Incorrect. Rolling wave planning is a form of progressive elaboration. Since rolling wave
planning provides a more precise definition of what the project team is doing, progressive
elaboration is not the best answer to the question asked. Answer choices on the real exam
may be very close to each other. When two or more choices look like the correct answer,
always select the one that more accurately addresses the question asked.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 184-185

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 143 of 200
Question ID: 613182
- **A new developer joins the project. However, her productivity is limited since she lacks the**
competency in one of the programming languages. This language is not only used on this project
but will also be required on future projects. Training costs were not included in the project
budget, and the project CPI is 0.75.
What is the best course of action for the project manager?
Top of Form
- **A Submit a change request to update the development approach**
- **B Seek approval for the performing organization to absorb the training costs**
- **C Stop using this programming language on this project**
- **D Terminate the employment of the new developer and find a replacement**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How might the new developer be trained without incurring costs to the project?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question describes a situation where a project team member lacks an important competency.
One of the tools and techniques associated with the Develop Team process is training. Training
the new developer in the lacking programming language will enhance the productivity of the
project team. According to the scenario, the project CPI is 0.75 implying the project is over

---

budget, therefore, absorbing the required training costs is problematic for the project. However,
there is another alternative which will not affect the project budget. Training costs may be
supported by the performing organization if the added skills will be useful for future projects
which is the case in the situation presented. Therefore, the best course of action is to seek
approval for the performing organization to absorb the training costs as it will help the current
project and may benefit future projects.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Submit a change request to update the development approach**
Incorrect. The development approach is a component of the project management plan that
describes a development approach selected for the project, such as predictive, iterative,
agile, or a hybrid model. The development approach is unlikely to change as a result of a
developer being unable to code in a specific programming language.
- **B Seek approval for the performing organization to absorb the training costs**
Correct. The project manager should seek alternatives in addressing the gap in skillset,
which will not affect the project budget. In this case, training costs may be supported by the
performing organization if the added skills will be useful for future projects.
- **C Stop using this programming language on this project**
Incorrect. If the programming language were becoming obsolete or does not fit in with the
organization's technical strategy, then this choice might make sense. However, the question
does not support such obsolescence or trend. It states that future projects are also expected
to utilize this language. Just because a new developer lacks competence in a programming
language, does not mean that the project should cease to use it.
- **D Terminate the employment of the new developer and find a replacement**
Incorrect. This answer choice represents an extreme action, which should not be necessary.
Although the rationale is unknown from the question, a decision was made to add the new
developer to the project team. The project manager should devise a strategy to develop the
new team member to enhance productivity.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 342

Question ID: 613105
- **A project is re-roofing five houses in a staggered timeline using different teams. Each team**
properly documented all the issues and solutions. The first two houses are complete. Both
experienced problems with the installation of the flashing, which required rework. Now, the
project manager sees the same issue for the third house, which is delaying the project.
What might be going wrong?
Top of Form
- **A The customer is causing scope creep.**
- **B The rental company defined their requirements wrong.**
- **C The project teams are not reviewing the project documentation.**
- **D The scope management plan needs to be correct to reflect the right flashing.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How should the follow-on project teams learn from the prior projects' issues?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question states that the first two project teams encountered a problem on the project and that
all issues and solutions were properly documented. This description indicates that the flashing
problems were captured in the issue log and the knowledge gained was recorded in the lessons
learned register. If the third project team had reviewed these documents, they could have avoided

---

or mitigated the problem and prevented the project from running behind schedule. The primary
purpose of the lessons learned register is to avoid repeating the same mistakes. Therefore, in this
scenario, the third project most likely did not review the project documents.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The customer is causing scope creep.**
Incorrect. The question does not provide any information that the customer has caused any
scope creep. There is no mention of the customer asking for any uncontrolled expansion of
product or project scope without adjustments to time, cost, and resources.
- **B The rental company defined their requirements wrong.**
Incorrect. There is not enough information to determine if the requirements were flawed.
More importantly, it appears that the problem is recurring which suggests that the
knowledge gained from earlier in the project is not being used to improve performance.
- **C The project teams are not reviewing the project documentation.**
Correct. The question states that the teams thoroughly documented issues and solutions,
which means the issue log and lessons learned register should have included this issue
along with the solution. It appears that the third team did not review these project
documents in order to avoid the same problems.
- **D The scope management plan needs to be correct to reflect the right flashing.**
Incorrect. The scope management plan is a component of the project or program
management plan that describes how the scope will be defined, developed, monitored,
controlled, and validated. The scope management plan describes processes rather than the
actual project scope.

Question 145 of 200
Question ID: 612309
You are managing a project to clean up hazardous waste at a manufacturing plant. A contractor
discovered a leak that threatened to seep into the ground near a water supply. A change request
was approved, and your employees implemented corrective measures to remove the defective
container and all affected soil.
What process is involved in your next task to verify the corrective actions were effective?
Top of Form
- **A Direct and Manage Project Work**
- **B Monitor and Control Project Work**
- **C Control Procurements**
- **D Control Quality**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Keep in mind that your staff has implemented the changes. What process has approved change
requests as an input? What knowledge area is this? What process group is it?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The scenario indicates that project execution is well underway. Additionally, monitoring has
been going on, as well as the integrated change control, which is involved in the Monitoring and
Controlling process group that occurs throughout the project.

---

Since your own employees implemented the approved change request, their implementation
should be verified, confirmed for completeness, retested, and certified as correct. You may use
contractors to perform the monitoring. However, the task is to monitor the performance of your
own employees. Verifying that your employees' implementation of the approved change request
was effective falls under Control Quality.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Direct and Manage Project Work**
Incorrect. While approved change requests are inputs to the Direct and Manage Project
process, the task is to implement the corrective or preventive action and defect repairs. In
the scenario given, this process has already taken place.
- **B Monitor and Control Project Work**
Incorrect. The task for the Monitor and Control Project Work process is to track, review,
and report the overall progress to meet the project performance objectives. This is not the
best answer to the question, which specifically asks for the process that verifies the
effectiveness of the implementation of an approved change request.
- **C Control Procurements**
Incorrect. Although it was a contractor who discovered the leak, the corrective action was
implemented by your own employees. Therefore, the task to verify the effectiveness of
implementing the approved change request is not specific to the Control Procurements
process.
- **D Control Quality**
Correct. Since your own employees implemented the approved change request, the task is to
monitor the performance of your own employees. Verifying that your employees'
implementation of the approved change request was effective falls under Control Quality.

Question ID: 612917
After spending two months analyzing and categorizing numerous customer complaints to
ascertain their root causes, the project team has discovered that many of the category
assignments of the complaints are incorrect. Fortunately, you have identified a new tool that uses
artificial intelligence to automate the categorization with near-perfect accuracy.
Where should you record your experience working with this tool?
Top of Form
- **A Lesson learned register**
- **B Requirements documentation**
- **C Test and evaluation documents**
- **D Resource management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which document or plan is used to capture experience gained?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question implies that you are involved with the Manage Quality process, and updates to the
lessons learned register is a process output. In this case, you have discovered a new tool that will
save a lot of time and greatly improve accuracy, and it is important to share the discovery. The

---

lessons learned register serves as the record for everything you and the team discover that can
help improve project performance.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Lesson learned register**
Correct. The lessons learned register serves as the record for any lessons learned that can
help improve project performance. A new tool that can reduce errors and rework should be
detailed there.
- **B Requirements documentation**
Incorrect. Requirements documentation provides descriptions of how individual
requirements meet the business need for the project. Unless specific project tools are
required by the customer or sponsor, they would not be detailed here. Based on the
scenario, the tool has been discovered by you during project execution, suggesting the tool
was not specified in the requirements.

Incorrect. Test and evaluation documents describe the activities used to determine if the
product or result meets quality objectives. These documents do not typically capture details
on the tools to be used.
- **D Resource management plan**
Incorrect. The resource management plan describes how resources will be acquired,
allocated, monitored and controlled. It does not typically include details on individual tools
used during project execution.

Question 147 of 200
Question ID: 613444
- **A total of 20 risks were identified during the project, 17 of these have become issues, most of**
which were successfully managed. With the project in the closing stage, the project manager
decides to update the lessons learned register with information about the way risks were
managed on the project.
Which of the following would be the most important to include in the lessons learned register so
that other project managers can benefit from the experiences on the project?
Top of Form
- **A Lessons learned about the number of risks on a project**
- **B Knowledge gained about the risk response plans and what did and did not work well**
- **C Lessons learned about the resources who worked on risks**
- **D Knowledge gained about how risks were identified**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The foundation of continuous improvement is learning from past mistakes.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Although the lessons learned register only affects the current project, the knowledge gained will
be transferred to the lessons learned repository where it will be available to improve the
performance of future projects. All of the answer choices represent information that might be

---

included in the lessons learned register, so the answer choice that represents the information that
will be of greatest value to future projects should be selected.
The question indicates that 'most' of the realized risks were managed successfully. Since some of
the realized risks were not successfully managed, it will be crucial to capture what did not work
well (in addition to what did work well), so the mistakes made with the risk response plans are
not repeated on future projects. The foundation of continuous improvement is learning from past
mistakes. Therefore, of the available choices, the most important information to include in the
lessons learned register is the knowledge gained about the risk response plans and what did and
did not work well.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Lessons learned about the number of risks on a project**
Incorrect. The number of risks will be highly variable from project to project. Therefore,
this information is not likely to be as beneficial to future projects compared with the
mistakes that were made with the response plans.
- **B Knowledge gained about the risk response plans and what did and did not work well**
Correct. The question indicates that 'most' of the realized risks were managed successfully.
Since some of the realized risks were not successfully managed, it will be crucial to capture
what did not work well (in addition to what did work well), so the mistakes made with the
risk response plans are not repeated on future projects.
- **C Lessons learned about the resources who worked on risks**
Incorrect. It might be noteworthy to include risk owners in the lessons learned register so
they can be consulted during future projects. However, personnel may leave the company
and memories fade over time. It will be more important to capture information on 'how' the
risks were managed rather than 'who' managed them.
- **D Knowledge gained about how risks were identified**
Incorrect. Any knowledge gained about how the risks were identified should be included in
the lessons learned register. However, the question suggests that the 17 issues faced during
the project were among the 20 identified risks. Therefore, there are not likely to be
significant learnings regarding the risk identification process.

PMP Exam 6

Question 148 of 200
Question ID: 613161
The customer is frustrated that the first prototype of a drone to detect forest fires is missing the
latest technology of infrared detection systems. The purchasing manager demands a meeting to
discuss that unwillingness of the development team to adapt to technology changes.
Which of the following should the project manager do before the meeting?
Top of Form
- **A Review the requirements documentation**
- **B List all the customer change requests to show the purchasing manager that they are requesting**
too many changes
- **C Tell the development team to change the infrared detection system**
- **D Determine why the development team is not being responsive to the customer's demands**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project manager should first determine if there has been a deviation in the agreed-upon
scope.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

In this scenario, the customer is demanding a revision to the infrared detection system. Either the
prototype was not built according to the agreed-upon scope, or the customer is demanding a
change to the deliverable. The project manager needs first to determine which is the case. The

---

requirements documentation is used in the Control Scope process to detect any deviation in the
agreed-upon scope for the project or product. This action represents the best way to prepare for
the meeting with the purchasing manager. If the prototype was not built to specifications, then a
change request will need to be issued to take the necessary corrective action to bring the
deliverable back into alignment with the plan. If the purchasing manager is requesting a change,
then a change request will need to be submitted to update the scope baseline and possibly the
other baselines. Thus, the result of the meeting with the purchasing manager will likely result in
a change request, but the project manager must first understand whether or not a deviation has
taken place. Therefore, of choices offered, reviewing the requirements documentation is the
correct response.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Review the requirements documentation**
Correct. Prior to the meeting, the project manager should prepare by reviewing the
requirements documentation. The requirements documentation can be used to detect any
deviation from the product requirements.
- **B List all the customer change requests to show the purchasing manager that they are**
requesting too many changes
Incorrect. The project manager must maintain an open mind and present objective data.
The customer may have a valid point. Listing all the changes is an aggressive approach
that will probably antagonize the customer further.
- **C Tell the development team to change the infrared detection system**
Incorrect. Changing the design of the deliverables requires an approved change request. A
change request must first be submitted and approved before this direction can be given to
the development team.
- **D Determine why the development team is not being responsive to the customer's demands**
Incorrect. The development is responsible for creating the project's deliverables as
documented in the scope baseline. If the customer is requesting a change in scope, the
development team is not likely to be authorized to approve such a change. The development
team should be responsive to approved change requests rather than customer demands to
avoid scope creep.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 169-170

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 149 of 200
Question ID: 612009
Your company was awarded a contract that includes a 10% bonus payment if the project is
completed two months early. You consider several options to exploit this opportunity.
What is the best course of action for you to increase the chances of receiving the bonus?
Top of Form
- **A Reduce project scope**
- **B Level resources**
- **C Crash the schedule**
- **D Purchase insurance**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

In which schedule compression technique are resources added to the critical path to shorten the
project duration?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

This question involves two project management Knowledge Areas, Risk Management and
Schedule Management. Crashing is an example of a schedule compression technique that can be
used during the Develop Schedule process. This technique may help exploit the opportunity by
adding more resources to the critical path. The processes of the Project Risk Management
Knowledge Area aim to develop options and strategies to capture opportunities (positive risks)

---

and minimize the effects of threats (or negative risks). In the scenario described, you have been
presented with a chance to collect a bonus payment for early project completion. A contingency
reserve including amounts of time, money, or resources to take advantage of the opportunity
should be established. The opportunity to collect the bonus payment is within reach; therefore,
the best course of action in this situation is to crash the schedule to shorten the critical path.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Reduce project scope**
Incorrect. While reducing project scope will likely shorten the project duration, it is
reasonable to assume that this course of action would not be acceptable by the customer.
- **B Level resources**
Incorrect. Resource leveling is a schedule optimization technique in which start and finish
dates are adjusted based on resource constraints with the goal of balancing the demand for
resources with the available supply. Resource leveling can often cause the original critical
path to change, typically to increase, while your goal is to shorten the critical path to
secure the bonus.
- **C Crash the schedule**
Correct. Crashing is the schedule compression technique used to shorten the schedule
duration for the least incremental cost by adding resources. Since your goal is to complete
the project earlier to secure the bonus by adding more resources to the critical path,
crashing the schedule is what you should do next.
- **D Purchase insurance**
Incorrect. Purchasing insurance is an example of a transfer strategy to address threats. The
scenario implies there is an opportunity for the project rather than a threat.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 215, 397, 444
Bottom of Form

Question 150 of 200
Question ID: 613692
You are very concerned about the substantial percentage of failures during the latest major
inspection. Because of the high number of potential causes, you would like the team to conduct a
detailed investigation. Estimates are that the investigation will delay the project for 4-6 weeks.
This is a problem because the project is already substantially behind schedule.
What should you do?
Top of Form
- **A Use the integrated change control system to request a change to the schedule baseline**
- **B Proceed with the investigation, and notify the project stakeholders**
- **C Delay the investigation until another major inspection can be conducted**
- **D Update the schedule baseline and proceed with the investigation immediately**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How can you be proactive and follow the required process?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

According to the scenario provided, you are performing the Manage Quality process. Significant
quality failures are a big deal because they indicate that you are not meeting requirements
consistently. And, in this complex project, a thorough investigation is probably the only way to
determine the root cause/s. Because the investigation will delay the project substantially, the

---

schedule baseline needs to be updated. You need to submit a change request and receive approval
before you can make substantial changes to any of the baselines - including the schedule.
Note: it is reasonable to assume that the additional 4-6 weeks of work will require additional
project resources. Therefore, it is likely that the cost baseline will have to be updated to reflect
the costs of the investigation, and the scope baseline will have to be updated to describe the
scope this investigation represents. One may argue that if the issue described in the scenario has
been identified as a risk during project planning, and a contingency reserve has been allocated to
cover the corresponding risk response, no updates to the baselines would be required, and only
the project schedule would have to be adjusted without a need for a change request. While this
statement may be true, there is not enough information in the question to make this
determination.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Use the integrated change control system to request a change to the schedule baseline**
Correct. Because the investigation will delay the project substantially, the schedule
baseline needs to be updated. And, because the project is baselined, you will need to use
the project's change control process.
- **B Proceed with the investigation, and notify the project stakeholders**
Incorrect. Although it is always a good idea to keep your stakeholders informed, the
schedule baseline must be updated before proceeding with an investigation that will
substantially delay the project.
- **C Delay the investigation until another major inspection can be conducted**
Incorrect. Your job as the project manager is to keep the project moving forward to meet all
requirements, including those for scope, schedule, and cost. When something unforeseen
requires a delay, it is important to deal with the circumstances in a proactive manner.
- **D Update the schedule baseline and proceed with the investigation immediately**
Incorrect. A schedule baseline is a configurable element, and this means that a change
request is required to update it.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 297, 83, 217
