Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 151 of 200
Question ID: 651436
Midway into project execution, a buyer has informed the seller that starting the next month, the
payments will be released at the beginning, instead of the end, of each month. The seller
welcomes the change as it would be beneficial for their company.
What should the seller do?
Top of Form
- **A Do nothing as the change is beneficial**
- **B Provide the deliverables at the beginning of each month**
- **C Update the procurement management plan**
- **D Ask the buyer to issue a change request to the contract**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The payment schedule is typically specified in the terms and conditions of the agreement
between the buyer and the seller.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

It can be inferred from the scenario, that the project is in the Control Procurements process.
Change requests are an input to this process and can include modifications to the terms and
conditions of the contract, including the procurement statement of work, pricing, and
descriptions of the products, service, or results to be produced. The payment schedule is typically

---

specified in the terms and conditions of the contract. Based on the scenario, it is reasonable to
assume that the contract specifies that the payments are to be released at the end of each month.
Now, as the procurement procedures in the buyer's organizations have changed, the contract
should be updated with the new payment schedule. The change should be agreed upon by both
parties. According to the scenario, the seller welcomes the change, implying the seller agrees.
Therefore, the next logical step for the seller is to ask the buyer to issue a change request to
modify the contract.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Do nothing as the change is beneficial**
Incorrect. The payment schedule is typically specified in the terms and conditions of the
contract. Regardless of whether the change is beneficial or not, it should be documented as
a formal change request and, if approved, implemented in the contract by either amending
it or modifying its terms and conditions. Doing nothing may harm both parties if contested
changes around payments arise.
- **B Provide the deliverables at the beginning of each month**
Incorrect. There is not enough information in the scenario to determine what is the current
timetable of the deliverables and whether or not the change to the payment schedule will
also require the seller to change the timing of their deliverables.
- **C Update the procurement management plan**
Incorrect. On projects involving procurements, the buyer develops the procurement
management plan. The question is asking what the seller should do. The seller is not
supposed to update the procurement management plan of the buyer. The seller may have
their own procurement management plan to handle the procurements with their third
parties. However, this information is not provided, and the way the question is worded
implies this answer choice refers to the buyer's plan.
- **D Ask the buyer to issue a change request to the contract**
Correct. Approved change requests are inputs to the Control Procurements process
described in the scenario. A change to the terms and conditions of the contract, such as the
modification of the payment schedule, should be documented as a formal change request. If
the request is approved, the contract will be updated.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 496

Question 152 of 200
Question ID: 612942
You are planning to use a lot of expensive specialty tools in a year-long aviation project. You
want to plan for the quantity and types of the tools needed, as well as track their availability
throughout the project.
Which of the following processes would you use to estimate the type and quantity of these tools?
Top of Form
- **A Define Scope**
- **B Determine Budget**
- **C Monitor and Control Project Work**
- **D Estimate Activity Resources**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Choose the process that will determine the types and quantities of materials, equipment, and
supplies necessary to accomplish the project work.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The scenario implies you are planning resources for your project. The objective is to determine
specific types and quantities of tools, which are physical resources. Estimate Activity Resources
is the process where you estimate all the resources needed for the project based on your previous
work of identifying project scope and individual activities needed to complete it. The Estimate

---

Activity Resources process may be performed iteratively throughout the project as you gain
experience with the resources and their utilization. The key output of this process will be the
resource requirements documentation.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Define Scope**
Incorrect. Define Scope is the process of developing a detailed description of the project
and product. This process is fairly high-level and does not include the determination of
specific tool types and quantities.
- **B Determine Budget**
Incorrect. Determine Budget is the process of aggregating the estimated costs of individual
activities or work packages to establish an authorized cost baseline. The Determine Budget
process can take place only after you identify the specific tool types and quantities, making
this choice an incorrect answer.
- **C Monitor and Control Project Work**
Incorrect. Monitor and Control Project Work is the process of tracking, reviewing, and
reporting the overall progress to meet the performance objectives defined in the project
plan. While you would track tool availability here, determination of types and quantities
occurs elsewhere.
- **D Estimate Activity Resources**
Correct. Estimate Activity Resources is the process of estimating team resources and the
type and quantities of material, equipment, and supplies necessary to do the job. The
specialty tools required for this project are some of the equipment covered in this process.

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 153 of 200
Question ID: 612748
Due to a force majeure, the authorized project budget is no longer attainable. Despite this, the
project manager talks directly to the customer and obtains from them additional funding that
allows the project to proceed. The situation comes to the attention of the project management
office who, after conferring with the CCB, puts an immediate halt to the project.
How could this situation have been avoided?
Top of Form
- **A The project manager should have avoided the force majeure**
- **B The project manager should have controlled costs to meet the authorized budget**
- **C The project manager should have conducted the Perform Integrated Change Control process**
- **D The project manager should have terminated the project when it was clear that the project**
objectives would not be met
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

- **A force majeure refers to a contract clause that provides relief from liabilities when a contract**
cannot be fulfilled as a result of natural or unavoidable catastrophes.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question indicates that a change control board (CCB) has been authorized for the project.
The CCB is a formally chartered group responsible for the disposition of change requests. Any

---

increase in the authorized budget can only be approved through the Perform Integrated Change
Control Process. Although the client, or authorized representative, should be included as a
member of the CCB, the client alone cannot approve the request to increase the authorized
project budget. Therefore, the question suggests that the project manager failed to conduct the
Perform Integrated Change Control Process. It can be assumed that the project management
office (PMO) conferred with the CCB and realized that the change management plan was not
followed and stopped the project. Therefore, of the available options, the best response is that the
project manager should have conducted the Perform Integrated Change Control process. It is
worth mentioning that, in addition to the project budget, it is highly likely that the schedule
baseline would have to be adjusted and possibly the scope baseline, but the question only
addressed the project budget.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The project manager should have avoided the force majeure**
Incorrect. A force majeure refers to a contract clause that provides relief from liabilities
when a contract cannot be fulfilled as a result of natural or unavoidable catastrophes. As
such, it is unlikely that the project manager could have avoided the circumstances caused
by the force majeure.
- **B The project manager should have controlled costs to meet the authorized budget**
Incorrect. A project manager is responsible for controlling costs and meeting project
objectives. However, there are extreme circumstances that are beyond the control of the
project manager. In the case of a force majeure, the project objectives are not likely to be
met.
- **C The project manager should have conducted the Perform Integrated Change Control**
process
Correct. The question indicates a change control board (CCB) exists on the project. The
CCB is a formally chartered group responsible for the disposition of change requests. If the
project manager used the Perform Integrated Change Control process to obtain additional
funds for the project, the situation described in the scenario could have likely been avoided.
It does not mean the funds would have been approved, but at least the PMO would not have
put an immediate halt to the project.
- **D The project manager should have terminated the project when it was clear that the project**
objectives would not be met
Incorrect. Terminating the project at this point in the project is a premature action. Even
though the project objectives cannot be met, the client and performing organization can

---

still reach an agreement to adjust the project goals and continue with the project. A project
manager can make recommendations but lacks the authority to terminate a project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 259

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 154 of 200
Question ID: 613221
During the planning of a project to build a new smartphone model, the project manager gets
information from a regional sales representative that the desire for a major feature is waning.
Earlier, during project initiation, the demand for the feature was so high that it was considered a
must-have feature. The project manager wants to validate the findings to ensure this trend is not
just a local anomaly.
What should the project manager do next?
Top of Form
- **A Use a checklist to make sure the data is correct**
- **B Send a survey or questionnaire to the sales groups in other regions**
- **C Perform an alternative analysis to see whether people still want the feature**
- **D Conduct a trend analysis to find what trends are popular**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project manager needs to reach a large crowd quickly and get a specific answer.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The scenario implies the project manager is in the Collect Requirements process. Questionnaires
and surveys are an example of the data gathering techniques that can be used in this process.
Questionnaires and surveys are written sets of questions designed to quickly accumulate

---

information from a large number of respondents. Questionnaires and surveys are most
appropriate with varied audiences, when a quick turnaround is needed, when respondents are
geographically dispersed, and where statistical analysis could be appropriate. By reaching out to
the other regional sales representatives with a survey or questionnaire, the project manager can
quickly gather data from a geographically diverse group followed by an analysis of the data to
determine if the local trend is just an anomaly or part of a larger shift in customer demand.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Use a checklist to make sure the data is correct**
Incorrect. Checklists are a data gathering technique but are typically used to ensure that a
set of required steps have been performed. A checklist would not be very effective in
determining the quality or accuracy of subjective data.
- **B Send a survey or questionnaire to the sales groups in other regions**
Correct. By reaching out to the other regional sales representatives with a survey or
questionnaire, the project manager can gather data from a geographically diverse group
followed by an analysis of the data to determine if the local trend is just an anomaly or part
of a larger shift in customer demand.
- **C Perform an alternative analysis to see whether people still want the feature**
Incorrect. An alternative analysis is a technique used to evaluate identified options in order
to select the options or approaches to use to execute and perform the work of the project.
However, in this case, the project manager needs to first gather the data before it can be
analyzed.
- **D Conduct a trend analysis to find what trends are popular**
Incorrect. Trend Analysis is an analytical technique that uses mathematical models to
forecast future outcomes based on historical results. In this scenario, the project manager
needs first to employ a data gathering technique. Until data is gathered, there can be no
data to input into a mathematical model.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 143

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 155 of 200
Question ID: 613084
- **A project has a 90% chance of making $200,000 profit and a 10% chance of incurring a loss of**
$50,000.
If you calculate the expected monetary value, what is the expected outcome of the project?
- **A Profit**
- **B Loss**
- **C Cannot be determined**
- **D Break even**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Find the total profit and loss and calculate the difference.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Expected monetary value is calculated using the formula EMV = Probability x Impact for both
the opportunity and the threat.
● Total profit = 0.90 x $200,000 = $180,000
● Total loss = 0.10 x -$50,000 = -$5,000
● EMV = $180,000 - $5,000 = $175,000
Therefore, the project is predicted to make a profit.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Profit**
Correct. EMV = (0.90 x $200,000) + (0.10 x -$50,000) = $180,000 - $5,000 = $175,000,
which remains a positive value and therefore is a profit.
- **B Loss**
Incorrect. If you calculate the expected monetary value, the result is still a positive value
and therefore is a profit.
- **C Cannot be determined**
Incorrect. The question has all the information required to calculate the expected monetary
value.
- **D Break even**
Incorrect. There is nothing in this scenario to indicate the project will merely break even.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 435

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 156 of 200
Question ID: 612692
- **A project team is in the process of defining how the project costs will be estimated, budgeted,**
managed, monitored and controlled. The team members feel they don't have enough knowledge
to complete this process and decide to hire an expert to assist them with the task.
Expertise in which of the following areas will be the least helpful for the team to complete the
process they are performing?
Top of Form
- **A Risk response strategies**
- **B Previous similar projects**
- **C Cost estimating and budgeting**
- **D Earned value management**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer choice is an example of expert judgment that is not applicable to the Plan Cost
Management process?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Defining how the project costs will be estimated, budgeted, managed, monitored, and controlled
is the Plan Cost Management process. Hence, the question implies the team is performing the
Plan Cost Management process. Expert judgment is among the tools and techniques that can be

---

used as part of this process. Expertise in previous similar projects, costs estimating and
budgeting, and earned value management are examples of expert judgment as it pertains to the
Plan Cost Management process. The question is asking to select the answer choice that
represents expertise which will be the 'least' helpful in completing this process. Expertise in risk
response strategies is an example of expert judgment that is most helpful with the Plan Risk
Responses process, not the Plan Cost Management process, making risk response strategies the
best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Risk response strategies**
Correct. The question implies that the project team is creating the cost management plan.
Expertise in risk response strategies is an example of expert judgment that will be more
applicable to the development of the risk management plan rather than the cost
management plan.
- **B Previous similar projects**
Incorrect. Knowledge in previous similar projects may help the project team with the Plan
Cost Management process as implied by the question. For example, the cost management
plan from a past similar project might be used as a good starting point to build the cost
management plan for the current project. Additionally, any knowledge gained from
previous projects may point to mistakes made in cost management and how to avoid them,
as well as any best practices.
- **C Cost estimating and budgeting**
Incorrect. The scenario suggests that the development of the cost management plan is
underway. The cost management plan defines how project costs will be estimated and
budgeted. Hence, expertise in cost estimating and budgeting will be of great value to the
project team.
- **D Earned value management**
Incorrect. According to the scenario, the team is performing the Plan Cost Management
process. Earned value management (EVM) rules of performance measurement are set
during the Plan Cost Management process. For example, the cost management plan
establishes the EVM techniques (e.g., weighted milestones, fixed-formula, percent
complete, etc.) to be employed.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 237, 235, 441

PMP Exam 6

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 157 of 200
Question ID: 612269
During a risk review meeting, the project manager learns that the company is considering a new
policy that would prohibit the use of overtime. If approved, this restriction will represent a new
constraint for the project.
Where should this newly identified constraint be documented?
Top of Form
- **A The constraint register**
- **B The risk register**
- **C The assumption log**
- **D The issue log**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What project document is used to record all assumptions and constraints throughout the project
life cycle?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

- **A risk review meeting is conducted as part of the Monitor Risks process. The risk register,**
assumption log, and issue log, among others, may be updated as a result of this process. The
question describes a situation which may need to be documented in some or all of these project
documents. The assumption log (sometimes referred to as the assumptions and constraints log) is

---

a project document used to record all assumptions and constraints throughout the project life
cycle. Since the question asks where the newly identified 'constraint' should be documented, it is
best to choose the document that specifically deals with 'constraints'. Therefore, of the choices
offered, the assumption log is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The constraint register**
Incorrect. 'Constraint register' is a fake project document made up for this question.
- **B The risk register**
Incorrect. A restriction in the flexibility of work hours of the project team may represent a
new risk to the project which should be captured in the risk register. However, the question
is specifically asking where the newly identified constraint should be documented rather
than the risk.
- **C The assumption log**
Correct. The assumption log (sometimes referred to as the assumptions and constraints log)
is a project document used to record all assumptions and constraints throughout the project
life cycle.
- **D The issue log**
Incorrect. The issue log is a project document where information about issues is recorded
and monitored. If approved, the new policy will "transform" from a constraint to an issue,
thus warranting to be captured in the issue log. However, until then, the scenario describes
a constraint that has not yet realized and become an issue. Therefore, documenting this
newly identified constraint in the issue log is premature.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 458

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 158 of 200
Question ID: 613180
You are creating the stakeholder register for a product development project with a multinational
corporation. You have already categorized the stakeholders according to their power and interest
level. However, you think it would be beneficial to incorporate a geographical component as an
added dimension, which will help in the development of communication strategies.
What should you do next?
Top of Form
- **A Use a stakeholder cube to categorize the stakeholders**
- **B Develop a power and interest grid to include all of the dimensions**
- **C Create a salience model to refine the stakeholder classifications**
- **D Update the stakeholder engagement plan to incorporate a three-dimensional model of**
stakeholders
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

- **A third dimension needs to be added to the existing power/interest grid.**
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that you, as the project manager, have completed a power/interest grid in
the development of the stakeholder register and need to add the third dimension of geography. A
stakeholder cube is a refinement of a grid model. This model combines the grid elements into a

---

three-dimensional model that can be useful to project managers and teams in identifying and
engaging their stakeholder community. It provides a model with multiple dimensions to improve
the depiction of the stakeholder community as a multidimensional entity and assists with the
development of communication strategies. The geographical component described in the
scenario can be the third dimension you are looking for in the process of the stakeholders'
categorization. Therefore, of the available options, using a stakeholder cube to categorize the
stakeholders is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Use a stakeholder cube to categorize the stakeholders**
Correct. A stakeholder cube is a refinement of a grid model, which combines the grid
elements into a three-dimensional model that can be useful to project managers and teams
in identifying and engaging their stakeholder community. The stakeholder cube can be used
to add the geographical component to the power and interest level, thus creating the
three-dimensional model to help in the development of communication strategies.
- **B Develop a power and interest grid to include all of the dimensions**
Incorrect. The question states that you have already categorized the stakeholders according
to the power and interest level. The inclusion of a third dimension cannot be accomplished
with a grid model, and a three-dimensional model must be used.
- **C Create a salience model to refine the stakeholder classifications**
Incorrect. A salience model describes classes of stakeholders based on assessments of their
power, urgency, and legitimacy. Whereas, the question is asking about a stakeholder
classification model which can add the third dimension of geography to an existing
power/interest grid.
- **D Update the stakeholder engagement plan to incorporate a three-dimensional model of**
stakeholders
Incorrect. According to the scenario, you are creating the stakeholder register. The
stakeholder register is created during the first iteration of the Identify Stakeholders process.
The stakeholder engagement plan is not created until later in the project during project
planning. Therefore, updating the stakeholder engagement plan cannot be what is done
next.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 512-513

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 159 of 200
Question ID: 610066
- **A project manager does most of her communicating with team members, internal project**
stakeholders, and external project stakeholders via email. The project manager incorporates
specific techniques when composing her emails to reduce any misunderstandings.
Which of the following is not considered one of these techniques?
- **A Concise expression**
- **B Clear purpose directed to the needs of the reader**
- **C Controlled flow of words and ideas**
- **D Communications register**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Misunderstandings can be reduced by using the 5Cs of written communication.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The scenario describes the use of techniques that will aid in the reduction of misunderstandings
in written communication specifically. These techniques are known as the 5Cs of written
communication:
1. Correct grammar and spelling
2. Concise expression and elimination of excess words
3. Clear purpose and expression directed to the needs of the reader
4. Coherent, logical flow of ideas

---

5. Controlled flow of words and ideas
However, the question asks which answer is 'not' a technique that will aid in the reduction of
misunderstandings in written communication, or in other words, which answer is not one of the
5Cs of written communication. 'Communications register' is not one of the 5Cs components.
Actually, 'communications register' is a made-up term.
Note, the term 'tools and techniques' used in this question to describe the 5Cs does not refer to
the traditional meaning of tools and techniques of the project management processes. We are
using this term as we consider it to be a reasonable description of the components comprising the
5Cs.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Concise expression**
Incorrect. A concise, well-crafted message reduces the opportunities for misunderstanding
the intent of the communication. Since the question is asking what is 'not' a technique used
in written communication, this choice is an incorrect answer.
- **B Clear purpose directed to the needs of the reader**
Incorrect. Ensuring that the needs and interests of the audience are factored into the
message will help reduce misunderstanding by the reader. Therefore, this is not a correct
answer choice.
- **C Controlled flow of words and ideas**
Incorrect. Controlling the flow of words and ideas by including graphics or summaries will
enhance the likelihood the message will be correctly interpreted and understood by the
reader. This answer choice is incorrect because the question is asking for a technique that
will 'not' aid in written communication.
- **D Communications register**
Correct. 'Communications register' is a made-up term, making this choice the best answer
to the question asked.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 362-363

Question 160 of 200
Question ID: 612241
During a project, the project manager introduces a new column to the risk register. This
modification proves to be beneficial in monitoring project risks. The project manager documents
the best practice in the lessons learned register and plans to transfer this information to the
lessons learned repository.
What else might the project manager do to ensure this best practice is considered for future
projects?
Top of Form
- **A Add a note to the best practices log for future reference**
- **B Record the information in the issue log**
- **C Submit a change request to update the risk management plan**
- **D Update the organizational process assets**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How might a template influence future projects?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that a best practice was developed, which can improve the performance of
the Monitor Risks process. Updates to the organizational process assets are one of the outputs of
the Monitor Risks process. Organizational process assets may include templates for project forms

---

and documents. In this case, a template of the revised risk register may be added to the
organizational process assets or the existing risk register template could be updated to the revised
version. Organizational process assets, including templates, serve as inputs for future projects.
The incorrect answer choices represent actions that may or may not influence the current project
but would not directly affect future projects. Therefore, among the available choices, updating
the organizational process assets with a revised risk register template is the best answer to the
question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Add a note to the best practices log for future reference**
Incorrect. 'Best practices log' is a fake project document made up for this question. Best
practices are an example of lessons learned which should be captured in the lessons
learned register.
- **B Record the information in the issue log**
Incorrect. The issue log is a project document where information about issues is recorded
and monitored. The issue log may be used for the current project but does not directly affect
future projects. Additionally, best practices are not recorded in the issue log.
- **C Submit a change request to update the risk management plan**
Incorrect. An approved change request is required to update the risk management plan, as
it is a component of the project management plan. However, the risk management plan is
only relevant to the current project and does not directly affect future projects.
- **D Update the organizational process assets**
Correct. Organizational process assets may include templates for project forms and
documents. In this case, a template of the revised risk register may be added to the
organizational process assets, or the existing risk register template could be updated to the
revised version.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 458

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 161 of 200
Question ID: 613589
- **A company has just completed a project. A few weeks later, the company's representative calls**
the consultant who served as the project manager to get some additional details on the project
including pitfalls and best practices to be used for future projects. The representative states that
they searched the project files, but the information was not there.
What might the consultant have missed?
Top of Form
- **A Meeting with the relevant stakeholders from the company and providing the information in**
person before leaving for another assignment
- **B Archiving the project documents and materials in the organizational process assets of the**
company
- **C Nothing, since the knowledge gained during the project lead by an external consultant is**
considered proprietary and owned by the consultant
- **D Updating all of the project related documents and marking them as final versions**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The lessons learned register should be finalized and transferred to the lessons learned repository
of the company as part of the Close Project or Phase process.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**


---

All project documents may be updated and marked as final versions as a result of project closure.
Of particular importance is the lessons learned register, which is finalized to include final
information on phase or project closure. The finalized lessons learned register, which may
include pitfalls and best practices, is then transferred to the lessons learned repository during the
Close Project or Phase process. In this manner, the project documents and materials, including
the lessons learned repository, is archived as an organizational process asset of the performing
organization for use on future projects. Therefore, of the available options, archiving the project
documents and materials is most likely what the project management consultant missed during
project closure.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Meeting with the relevant stakeholders from the company and providing the information**
in person before leaving for another assignment
Incorrect. There is nothing wrong with meeting with the stakeholders to provide
information on best practices if the company chooses so. However, regardless of this
meeting, the knowledge gained during the project should still be captured in the lessons
learned register and then transferred to the lessons learned repository as an organizational
process asset of the company which is the performing organization in the scenario
described.
- **B Archiving the project documents and materials in the organizational process assets of the**
company
Correct. The lessons learned register, which may include pitfalls and best practices to be
considered for future projects, should be finalized and then transferred to the lessons
learned repository as an organizational process asset during the Close Project or Phase
process. Archiving the project documents and materials in the company's organizational
process assets was the activity which the project management consultant most likely
missed.
- **C Nothing, since the knowledge gained during the project lead by an external consultant is**
considered proprietary and owned by the consultant
Incorrect. The terms and conditions of the contract will determine ownership of the results
derived from the project including any documents and knowledge gained. The mere fact
that the project manager was contracted as an external consultant rather than hired as an
employee is not relevant in determining ownership for any aspect of the results of the
project.
- **D Updating all of the project related documents and marking them as final versions**

---

Incorrect. The action of updating the project related documents and marking them as final
versions alone would not preserve the documents as organizational process assets to be
available for use in future projects of the company.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 127-128

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 162 of 200
Question ID: 612757
- **A small project has been running for about a month when the project manager finds licenses for**
a powerful scheduling tool that left unused from another large project. The project manager got
an approval to assign the unused licenses to his small project at no charge. But now, there is a
need for a dedicated team member to feed the project information into the scheduling tool,
requiring additional time and budget that were not originally planned.
What is the most likely problem in the scenario described?
Top of Form
- **A The information of the current project that needs to be fed into the scheduling tool is too detailed**
- **B The scheduling tool from the large project is too sophisticated for the size of the current project**
- **C The scheduling method initially selected for the current project was fundamentally wrong**
- **D Nothing is wrong in the scenario described. Anything unplanned can happen on any project.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The question describes a small project and a sophisticated scheduling tool.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The scheduling model consists of the project information, the scheduling tool, and the scheduling
method. A scheduling tool provides schedule component names, definitions, structural
relationships, and formats that support the application of a scheduling method. There is no

---

information provided to indicate that the project information and scheduling method is an issue.
However, the fact that a dedicated team member is required to use the tool suggests that the tool
takes some time and effort to use. The tool is probably requiring more work than is practical for
the project, and the time and effort needed to manage the tool is probably better spent elsewhere.
Therefore, in this scenario, the scheduling tool is likely too sophisticated for the size of the
project.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The information of the current project that needs to be fed into the scheduling tool is too**
detailed
Incorrect. The question states that the current project is small, so the project information is
not likely to be very detailed. However, the tool that has been used on the large project is
likely configured to be fed with a lot of detailed information, which is either unavailable
and/or not needed for the small project.
- **B The scheduling tool from the large project is too sophisticated for the size of the current**
project
Correct. Not all projects need specific scheduling software. Some can use a spreadsheet or
other simple tools. The fact that a dedicated team member is required to use the tool
indicates that the tool takes a great deal of effort to operate, implying extra time and
money. Even though there was no cost associated with the scheduling tool, the time and
effort needed for the tool is probably better spent elsewhere.
- **C The scheduling method initially selected for the current project was fundamentally wrong**
Incorrect. The scheduling method is the methodology used for scheduling the project, such
as the critical path method or an agile approach. There is not enough information in the
scenario to determine is the scheduling method selected for the project was wrong (whether
fundamentally or not).
- **D Nothing is wrong in the scenario described. Anything unplanned can happen on any**
project.
Incorrect. While it's true that anything can happen on any project, applying proper project
management practices may avoid or, at least, reduce risks of things going wrong. It is
evident from the scenario that implementing the tool from another project caused problems
for the current project. It seems that the scheduling tool taken from the large project was
too sophisticated for the size of the current project, thus incurring unplanned costs.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 175-176

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 163 of 200
Question ID: 612921
After a series of mergers and acquisitions, you are managing a multi-phase rebranding project.
After the project deliverables have already been formally accepted, an executive branding
authority finds several instances of non-compliance in print, digital, and office sign samples, and
wants to meet with those who signed off on them.
Where would you find out details on who signed off and what they signed off on?
Top of Form
- **A Stakeholder engagement assessment matrix**
- **B Lessons learned register**
- **C Quality control measurements**
- **D Requirements documentation**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

As an output, the Validate Scope process updates three project documents, only one of which
commonly has detail including stakeholders and cases where requirements could be waived.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The scenario indicates that the Validate Scope process has been completed, which resulted in
accepted deliverables as one of its outputs. As part of this process, the deliverables are inspected
and, if found to be meeting the acceptance criteria, are formally signed off by the customer,

---

sponsor, or authorized stakeholder. These sign-offs are captured in requirements documentation
which is one of the inputs to the Close Project or Phase process. The requirements should be
unambiguous (measurable and testable), complete, and consistent apart from being traceable and
acceptable to stakeholders. The formal sign off is documented in the requirements
documentation, which is a set of project documents that is updated with the results of scope
validation. Of particular interest is when the actual results are better than the requirement or
where a requirement was waived. The format may range from a simple document listing all the
requirements categorized by stakeholder and priority, to more elaborate forms containing an
executive summary, detailed descriptions, and attachments. Considering the possibility that
stakeholders, attachments, and waivers are included, requirements documentation is the best
place to look up who signed off on the deliverables and details of the requirements in order to
prepare for the meetings.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Stakeholder engagement assessment matrix**
Incorrect. The stakeholder engagement assessment matrix is a tool used in the Plan
Stakeholder Engagement process. It shows the desired engagement levels. Since this tool
does not involve stakeholder sign-offs of verified deliverables or detailed requirements, the
stakeholder engagement assessment matrix is not the correct answer.
- **B Lessons learned register**
Incorrect. The lessons learned register is a project document that is updated with the
challenges encountered and how they could have been avoided, as well as approaches that
worked well. It is possible that inconsistencies among verified deliverables might be
discussed in the lessons learned register. However, this project document may not provide
the detailed requirements and of who signed off and why.
- **C Quality control measurements**
Incorrect. Quality control measurements are the documented results of control quality
activities. Quality control measurements are one of the outputs of the Control Quality
process. These results do not specify who signed off on the accepted deliverables and what
they signed off on.
- **D Requirements documentation**
Correct. The requirements documentation may describe the stakeholders, attachments, and
waivers involved with requirements at various stages of development, verification, and
validation. Therefore, the requirements documentation is the best place to look up who

---

signed off on a deliverable and more details on what they signed off on in order to prepare
for these meetings.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 166-167, 147, 131

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 164 of 200
Question ID: 614005
The following table contains information about the durations in days and predecessor activities
on a project schedule.
What is the free float of activity C, assuming that work starts on day one?
- **A 0 days**

---

- **B 6 days**
- **C 7 days**
- **D 17 days**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

If the activity in question is not on the critical path, the free float is calculated by subtracting the
early finish date of the activity from the early start of the earliest of its successors. However,
since the values in this formula are only the early start and early finish, you only need to conduct
a forward pass.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Free float refers to the amount of time an activity can be delayed without affecting the early start
date of subsequent dependent activities. If the activity in question is on the critical path, total
float is zero and therefore free float will also be zero. If an activity is not on the critical path, then
to calculate its free float, you have to complete a forward pass on the project schedule network
diagram to establish the two variables of this formula:
Free Float = Early Start of Next Activity – Early Finish of Current Activity – 1
Critical Path. The first thing to establish is whether the activity in question is on the critical
path. Knowing the predecessors for each activity, simply list all the possible sequences and add
up the durations for each path:

---

Since Start-D-E-F-G-Finish has the longest duration, it is the critical path. Activity C is not on
the critical path. Therefore, its float is not automatically zero.
Project Schedule Network Diagram. To calculate activity C’s free float, the next step is to
create a project schedule network diagram where you map the durations from the activity list
table included in the question, and then determine the early start date and early finish date for
each activity. This is accomplished using a technique called a 'forward pass'.
We suggest using the following format in each of the activity nodes to properly answer this type
of questions.

---

Forward Pass Formulas. Unless the question tells you otherwise, it should be assumed that
work starts on day 1. This 'start on day one' convention gives us the following formulas:
● ES = 1
For any activities where the Start milestone is the predecessor, work starts on day 1. In
this scenario, the Start milestone serves as a predecessor for activities A, D, and H. So for
these activity nodes, the early start date is 1.
● EF = ES + D - 1
The next step in the forward pass is to fill in the early finish date. For example, on
activity A the early start is 1, its duration is 4, and we subtract 1 to account for starting on
day one. As a result, the early finish for activity A is 1 + 4 - 1 = 4.
● ES = previous EF + 1
The next step is to fill in the early start for the next activity node. Taking activity B for
example, we use the early finish of activity A (4) and then add 1 to account for work
starting on day 1. As a result, the early start of activity B is 4 + 1 = 5. We continue filling
in the activity node's early finish using the formula EF = ES + D - 1. Then we continue
filling in an early start and early finish on subsequent activity nodes until we get to
convergence or the Finish milestone.
● ES = higher previous EF +1 (in case of convergence)
- **A convergence occurs where an activity has multiple predecessors. To find the early start**
on the receiving node of convergence, we must determine the previous early finish. But
with two or more predecessors, we have a choice of early finish values. The rule of
thumb is to use the previous EF with a higher value. In this scenario, we have a
convergence where both activity C and activity F serve as predecessors to activity G. The
early finish of activity C is 8. The early finish of activity F is 15. The higher value of
early finish is 15, so we choose this value and then add 1 to account for work starting on
day one. Computing the early start of activity G, the result is 15 + 1 = 16.
Note: this rule for convergence on a forward pass has a counterpart for divergence when
performing a backward pass to fill the late finish and late start dates across the bottom of each
node. However, a backward pass is not necessary to answer this question.
Following is the project schedule network diagram after completing a forward pass.

---

Now that you know the early start date and early finish date of each project activity, you can
apply the formula to determine the free float for any activity.
Free float of current activity = Early Start of next activity – Early Finish of current activity – 1
Free float of activity C = 16 - 8 - 1 = 7

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A 0 days**
Incorrect. An activity has a free float of zero when either the activity is on the critical path
or if the calculation based on the forward and backward pass analysis through the schedule
network results in zero. Neither of those is correct for activity C, making this choice an
incorrect answer.
- **B 6 days**

---

Incorrect. If you picked this answer, you might have assumed that work starts on day zero,
in which case the free float formula does not subtract 1. Instead, the formula would be
Early Start of Next Activity – Early Finish of Current Activity. However, since the question
did not specify a start day convention, it should be assumed that work starts on day 1.
- **C 7 days**
Correct. After performing a forward pass on the project schedule network diagram, you can
establish the values for the free float formula, assuming that work starts on day 1: Early
Start of Next Activity – Early Finish of Current Activity – 1. For activity C, the free float is
16 - 8 - 1 = 7, making this choice the correct answer.
- **D 17 days**
Incorrect. 17 days is the duration of the critical path and not the free float of activity C.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 210-211; see also PMI® Practice Standard for
Scheduling – Second Edition

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 165 of 200
Question ID: 612779
- **A project is underway to build a prototype street sweeper. When viewing the dashboard of the**
prototype, the project manager sees a row of USB ports, which were not in the specifications.
The engineer says that they were added because everyone has a cell phone and needs USB
connections.
What should the project manager do?
Top of Form
- **A Nothing. The engineer is responsible for the details of the requirements.**
- **B Make sure that the quality assurance department has test procedures for the USB ports**
- **C Tell the engineer that the USB ports should be removed**
- **D Check the project charter to see if there is an exclusion for this feature**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

New requirements cannot be added in an uncontrolled manner.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The situation described by the question represents scope creep. Scope creep is the uncontrolled
expansion to product or project scope without adjustments to time, cost, and resources. There
may be valid reasons that USB ports are not in the specification, such as a rule that drivers
should not use cell phones while working. Even though the USB ports have already been added,

---

allowing them to remain will add risks to the project which have not been accounted for during
risk planning. Therefore, of the available options, the best course of action for the project
manager is to have the USB ports removed to keep the project in alignment with the approved
scope baseline.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Nothing. The engineer is responsible for the details of the requirements.**
Incorrect. The details that the engineer is supposed to develop would be around the type of
USB ports if they were a requirement. However, the engineer should not add a project
requirement, which is a form of scope creep. If the engineer feels that an important project
requirement was missed, then a change request should be submitted to include the USB
ports in the project scope.
- **B Make sure that the quality assurance department has test procedures for the USB ports**
Incorrect. The question suggests that the USB ports were not included in the approved
scope baseline, and the requirement was added without following the change control
process. Thus, the USB ports represent scope creep. Making sure that test procedures are
available for the USB ports implies that the scope creep will be accepted rather than
following the established change control process, which is contrary to project management
accepted practices.
- **C Tell the engineer that the USB ports should be removed**
Correct. The engineer cannot add scope to the project without following the established
change control process. There may be valid reasons that USB ports are not in the
specification, such as a rule that drivers should not use cell phones while working.
- **D Check the project charter to see if there is an exclusion for this feature**
Incorrect. A project exclusion is captured in the project charter to identify what is excluded
from the project. Explicitly stating what is out of scope for the project helps manage
stakeholders' expectations and can reduce scope creep. Regardless of whether or not there
is an exclusion for this feature, the engineer added the USB ports without the benefit of the
integrated change control process. Therefore, at this point, it is not relevant whether or not
the feature was specifically excluded, as the scope creep should be addressed either way.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 168

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 166 of 200
Question ID: 613323
- **A project manager is looking for guidelines on how the project she has been leading should be**
closed. The project is internal to the organization.
What is the best course of action for the project manager?
Top of Form
- **A Consult the project management office**
- **B Check the organization process assets**
- **C Review the project charter**
- **D Internal projects do not require closure**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where might the project manager find the established procedures for project closure?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The organizational process assets serve as one of the inputs to the Close Project or Phase process
implied by the scenario. The organizational process assets may contain project closure guidelines
or requirements (e.g., lessons learned, final project audits, project evaluations, product
validations, acceptance criteria, resource reassignment, team performance appraisals, and
knowledge transfer). Therefore, among the answer options presented, checking the organization
process assets is the best course of action for the project manager.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Consult the project management office**
Incorrect. The project management office (PMO) is an organizational structure that
standardizes the project-related governance processes and facilitates the sharing of
resources, methodologies, tools, and techniques. Consulting the PMO is a plausible answer
choice. However, the guidelines on how projects should be closed are typically available in
the organizational process assets, which is provided in another answer choice, making the
current choice not the best answer to the question asked.
- **B Check the organization process assets**
Correct. Organizational process assets may include the corporate policies, procedures, and
guidelines on project closure that can be used by the project manager to understand how
the project she is leading should be closed.
- **C Review the project charter**
Incorrect. As it pertains to project closure, the project charter documents the project
success criteria, the approval requirements, and who will sign off on the project. The
project charter does not contain procedures for project closure.
- **D Internal projects do not require closure**
Incorrect. Project closure is required for all projects regardless of whether they are internal
or external to the performing organization.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 126

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 167 of 200
Question ID: 651437
The organization has just completed a project. Management wants to understand if the cost
forecasting models that were used on the project can be adjusted and used for future projects.
Which of the following techniques is best to use to address management's question?
Top of Form
- **A Product analysis**
- **B Trend analysis**
- **C Schedule network analysis**
- **D Source selection analysis**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Patterns can be found in the models.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Trend analysis is an analytical technique that uses mathematical models to forecast future
outcomes based on historical results. It can be used to anticipate possible future behavior. Trend
analysis is a technique used in various knowledge areas (e.g., integration, scope, schedule, cost,
resources, and procurement). In this scenario, trend analysis can be useful in the Close Project or
Phase process to validate if the models used in the current project can be used in future projects.

---

If a specific trend is anticipated, then necessary adjustments may need to be implemented in the
models.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Product analysis**
Incorrect. Product analysis is a tool used to define scope by describing the use,
characteristics, and other relevant aspects of what is going to be manufactured. The
product analysis is a tool that would be independently applied to other future product
development projects, not to cost forecasting models of historical projects. Besides, product
analysis is typically used in the Define Scope process, whereas the question scenario
suggests the project is in the Close Project or Phase process.
- **B Trend analysis**
Correct. Trend analysis is an analytical technique that uses mathematical models to
forecast future outcomes based on historical results. If specific trends are anticipated, then
the models that are used in the current project may be useful to future projects with some
adjustments. Trend analysis can be used in this way in the Close Project or Phase process.
- **C Schedule network analysis**
Incorrect. Schedule network analysis is a technique used to identify early and late start
dates, as well as early and late finish dates, for the uncompleted portions of project
activities. This technique does not apply to cost forecasting models. Also, it is applied in the
Develop Schedule process, not the Close Project or Phase, which is the process described
in the question.
- **D Source selection analysis**
Incorrect. Source selection analysis is a set of attributes desired by the buyer, which a seller
is required to meet or exceed to be selected for a contract. Source selection is used in the
Plan Procurement Management process, and it is not used when closing a project to
validate if models are viable for future use.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 126

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 168 of 200
Question ID: 651329
The project is wrapping up. The paperwork and files are being finalized and stored.
What is the project manager to do with the lessons learned documents?
Top of Form
- **A Compile the lessons learned documents to hand over to the customer**
- **B Transfer the lessons learned documents to a repository**
- **C Distribute the printed lessons learned documents to the project team**
- **D Publish the lessons learned documents to the end user's repository**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where should lessons learned reside after the project closes?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Lessons learned from the project are useful during the project and for future projects to learn
from. As the project is closing it is important to collect and save these lessons for others to learn
from. The most appropriate location for all across an organization to access and contribute to the
knowledge base is in a repository. A repository managed by the project management office
(PMO) is an example of a logical location.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Compile the lessons learned documents to hand over to the customer**
Incorrect. The lessons learned documentation is for the project and future projects within
the performing organization to learn from and gain knowledge. The customer does not need
these documents unless explicitly pointed out in any agreements.
- **B Transfer the lessons learned documents to a repository**
Correct. The lessons learned documentation is for the project and future projects
throughout the organization to learn from and gain knowledge. At the end of the project,
lessons learned and knowledge gained throughout the project are transferred from the
lessons learned register to the lessons learned repository.
- **C Distribute the printed lessons learned documents to the project team**
Incorrect. If the lessons learned documents are stored in a repository that project team
members can access and view, there is no need to print and distribute all the documents to
the project team members.
- **D Publish the lessons learned documents to the end user's repository**
Incorrect. The lessons learned documentation is for the project and future projects within
the organization to learn from and gain knowledge. End users typically do not need to be
provided internal project documents unless there is explicit, justified need.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 128

Question 169 of 200
Question ID: 613062
- **A project manager has just been hired to lead a project, which is already in the execution stage.**
Even though the project team members demonstrate strong social relations and collaborative
working environment, the project manager wants to improve the performance of the team and
provide the training necessary to achieve the project's objectives.
Among the following, what should the project manager do first?
Top of Form
- **A Evaluate the team members' current skills and competencies**
- **B Provide one of the courses offered by the company**
- **C Schedule a project retrospective**
- **D Conduct a team building activity**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How might enterprise environmental factors influence the Develop Team process?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question does not provide information on why the project manager wants to improve the
team performance. The question only suggests that the project manager is planning to carry out
the Develop Team process. The question also indicates that the project manager is new to the
performing organization, and, as a result, does not have a working knowledge of the project

---

team's current skills and competencies. Team member skills, competencies, and specialized
knowledge represent some of the enterprise environmental factors that may influence the
Develop Team process. All of the answer choices describe actions which may provide some
benefit; however, to identify training needs, the project manager should first seek to understand
what skills and competencies currently exist with the project team members. With this
understanding, the project manager is then equipped to look for those training and development
activities which address the specific needs of the team members. Therefore, of the available
options, before deciding on a team developmental strategy, the project manager should first
evaluate the team members' current skills and competencies.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Evaluate the team members' current skills and competencies**
Correct. Team member skills, competencies, and specialized knowledge represent some of
the enterprise environmental factors that may influence the Develop Team process. The
project manager should first seek to understand what development opportunities currently
exist with the project team before deciding on a developmental strategy.
- **B Provide one of the courses offered by the company**
Incorrect. A training course may have excellent content, but it will be of little value if it
covers existing knowledge. The project manager needs first to understand what the current
development needs of the project team members are.
- **C Schedule a project retrospective**
Incorrect. A project retrospective is a scheduled review to record lessons learned which
occurs at the end of a project. While a retrospective might be helpful in the sharing of best
practices to improve team performance on future projects, the project retrospective will not
improve the performance of the current project.
- **D Conduct a team building activity**
Incorrect. The goal of team building is to enhance the team's social relations and build a
collaborative and cooperative working environment. According to the scenario described,
the team members demonstrate that they are socially well bound and collaborate
effectively. Therefore, conducting a team building activity is not what the project manager
should do first.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 339

Question 170 of 200
Question ID: 613494
- **A project manager recently lost some key subject matter experts due to a business reorganization,**
and most of the work on the deliverable needs to be subcontracted out.
Which of the following best describes how project communications will be affected?
Top of Form
- **A The formality of the communication will increase.**
- **B The number of communication channels will increase.**
- **C The communication needs to be more frequent.**
- **D The number of communication channels will decrease.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The relationship with the vendor will require a contract.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

There are contractual agreements with subcontractors that require certain types of
communication. Hence, the project team and the subcontractor are likely to engage in more
formal communications. However, this arrangement does not necessarily result in more volume
or frequency in communications. Nor does it imply a net change in the number of
communication channels. Since the contract with the vendor will have significant legal
implications, the communications will need to be more formal.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The formality of the communication will increase.**
Correct. With internal teams, communication can be more casual, as it is easier to get
clarification and there are fewer legal implications. In a more formal contract situation
with a vendor, communications need to be more formal and conform to what is required
under the contract.
- **B The number of communication channels will increase.**
Incorrect. The number of communication channels may or may not increase in this
situation. The communication channels will increase by subcontracting with a vendor, but
communication channels are also being reduced by the loss of the subject matter experts.
Without further information, it is not possible to determine the net effect on the number of
communication channels.
- **C The communication needs to be more frequent.**
Incorrect. Communication needs to be sufficient, the changes suggested in the scenario
does not necessarily mean that communications will need to be more frequent.
- **D The number of communication channels will decrease.**
Incorrect. The number of communication channels may or may not decrease in this
scenario. The communication channels will decrease with the loss of the subject matter
experts, but communication channels are also being increased by contracting with a
supplier. Without further information, it is not possible to determine the net effect on the
number of communication channels.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 360-361, 384

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 171 of 200
Question ID: 651330
The project was a tremendous success. The project exceeded expectations by coming in under
budget and exactly on schedule. To celebrate the success, a party was announced and scheduled
for the project team. The party will be financed from cost savings that have been added to the
contingency reserves. But as the project is closing, the project manager and other stakeholders
are feeling it is better to use the funds allocated for the party to shore up future business with the
customer and appease the project sponsor.
What should be done with the funds allocated for the party?
Top of Form
- **A Applied to develop additional features**
- **B Reassigned back to the organization**
- **C Provided to the customer**
- **D Spent on the party as planned**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What has been promised?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Closing a project encompasses a lot of activities. One is to celebrate the hard work and success
of the project team. If funds are available and allocated to an event to thank the project team for

---

meeting their objective, then the project manager should honor that announced, scheduled, and
promised event. According to the scenario, the cost savings have been added to the contingency
reserves which is a common practice when opportunities are captured and resulting in cost
savings. Celebrating success is an example of a meeting that can be used among the tools and
techniques of the Close Project or Phase process described in this scenario.
We are often asked about the practice of adding cost savings to contingency reserves. According
to the reference provided, page 265, as work on the project progresses, contingency reserves may
be used as planned to cover the cost of risk responses or other contingencies. Conversely, when
opportunities are captured and resulting in cost saving, funds may be added to the contingency
amount, or taken from the project as margin/profit. The scenario describes a project in which
costs have been saved thanks to the project coming in under budget and exactly on schedule.
According to the scenario, it has been decided to add funds (that represent these cost savings) to
the contingency amount to cover the cost of the party. In other words, in this particular project,
the decision has been made to add funds to contingency reserve rather than take them from the
project as margin profit. And since these funds have been allocated for the party, spending them
on the party as planned is the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Applied to develop additional features**
Incorrect. Adding additional features or functionality beyond what has been scoped and
delivered is considered scope creep, unnecessary, and could potentially be wasteful. Project
managers are responsible for delivering per requirements and expectations, nothing more.
- **B Reassigned back to the organization**
Incorrect. In most circumstances allocating the funds back to the organization is expected,
but in this case, some of those funds were allocated to the project team to honor their
success.
- **C Provided to the customer**
Incorrect. The customer signed an agreement for the project to be completed by the project
manager's organization. There is not enough information in the question to determine if
cost savings are supposed to be given to the customer.
- **D Spent on the party as planned**
Correct. A party was promised to the project team. The project manager should honor that
promise.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 127, 265
Bottom of Form

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 172 of 200
Question ID: 613187
You are in the midst of project execution. You have identified new stakeholders and updated the
stakeholder register with the identification, assessment, and classification information.
What should you do next as part of this process?
Top of Form
- **A Ask the project sponsor to add the new stakeholders to the project charter**
- **B Submit a change request to update the project management plan**
- **C Assign the new stakeholder as a risk owner for the risks on the watch list**
- **D Perform an analysis of the stakeholders that you have identified**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which project documents or plans can be updated as part of the subsequent iterations of the
Identify Stakeholder process?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that you are performing the Identify Stakeholders process in the middle of
project execution. The stakeholder register is created as an output of the first iteration of the
Identify Stakeholders process and is updated as necessary as the project progresses. The question
indicates that the stakeholder register has already been updated. In addition to updating the
stakeholder register, the subsequent iterations of the Identify Stakeholder process may result in

---

an update to various components of the project management plan such as the requirements
management plan, communications management plan, risk management plan, and stakeholder
engagement plan. With new stakeholders being introduced into the project, it is likely that each
of these components will need to be revised. However, since the project is already in execution,
an approved change request is required to modify the project management plan. Therefore, of the
available choices, submitting a change request to update the project management plan is what
you should do next.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Ask the project sponsor to add the new stakeholders to the project charter**
Incorrect. The project charter may or may not need to be revised in this scenario. However,
the question suggests that you are performing the Identify Stakeholders process and asks
what you should do next 'as part of this process', implying as part of the Identify
Stakeholders process. The project charter is created or modified as part of the Develop
Project Charter process and not the Identify Stakeholders process. In general, the project
charter is rarely updated.
- **B Submit a change request to update the project management plan**
Correct. Components of the project management plan that may be updated as the result of
the Identify Stakeholders process described by the scenario may include the requirements
management plan, communications management plan, risk management plan, and
stakeholder engagement plan. With new stakeholders being introduced into the project, it is
likely that each of these components will need to be revised.
- **C Assign the new stakeholder as a risk owner for the risks on the watch list**
Incorrect. While there is nothing wrong with assigning the new stakeholder as a risk owner
for the risks on the watch list (assuming the roles and responsibilities of the stakeholder are
aligned with this task), this activity is typically performed as part of the processes of the
Project Risk Management Knowledge Area, while, according to the scenario, you are
performing the Identify Stakeholders process.
- **D Perform an analysis of the stakeholders that you have identified**
Incorrect. Stakeholder analysis is a technique which is performed in order to create or
update the stakeholder register as part of the Identify Stakeholders process. The question
states that the stakeholder register has already been updated with the identification,
assessment, and classification information. Therefore, a stakeholder analysis must have
already been performed.

---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 515

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 6
Top of Form
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 173 of 200
Question ID: 613726
One of your project team members indicates that she is missing some project communications
due to being left off of a group email distribution list. You document the problem and assign it to
a responsible party. The following week the team member asks you for an update.
What document should you check to find the name of the responsible party and a target date for
resolution?
Top of Form
- **A RACI chart**
- **B Responsibility assignment matrix (RAM)**
- **C Project team directory**
- **D Issue log**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What project document contains details on problems, gaps, inconsistencies, and conflicts
encountered by the project team?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The issue log is a project document that can serve as an input to the Manage Team process. This
document is used to record and monitor who is responsible for resolving specific issues and

---

includes a target date for resolution. Therefore, the issue log is the document where you should
find the name of the owner of a particular issue along with a target date for resolution.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A RACI chart**
Incorrect. A RACI chart is a type of responsibility assignment matrix which defines the
involvement of stakeholders in project activities. It does not contain information on specific
issues.
- **B Responsibility assignment matrix (RAM)**
Incorrect. A responsibility assignment matrix (RAM) is a grid that shows the project
resources assigned to each work package. It does not contain information on specific
issues.
- **C Project team directory**
Incorrect. The project team directory documents the names, project roles, and contact
information for members of the project team. It does not contain information on specific
issues.
- **D Issue log**
Correct. An issue log is used to document and monitor who is responsible for resolving
specific issues and includes a target date for resolution.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 317
Bottom of Form
